Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
The Mufti's Duty: Follow Rajih or Zahir al-Riwayah
Opening of the matn establishing the mufti's duty to follow authoritative opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufti's primary obligation in Hanafi usul al-ifta and identify the two sources of authority (rajih and Zahir al-Riwayah).

Core Idea
A mufti must follow the preferred opinion (rajih) or the manifest transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) — never his own preference.

This opening passage from Ibn Abidin's 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' establishes the foundational rule for issuing fatwa in the Hanafi school. It is not enough for a mufti to know the rulings; he must know which opinions carry authority. The poem declares it obligatory to follow what is deemed preferable or what is from the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, provided the school has not retracted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation
The passage begins 'Know that it is obligatory to follow' — the mufti has a binding duty (wajib), not a choice.
This obligation is the core of rasm al-mufti.
2
Recognize the two categories
The mufti must follow either: (a) what is 'preferred' (rajih) — the stronger opinion after weighing evidence, or (b) the manifest transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) — the rulings in the six canonical books.
Rajih takes precedence if a tarjih exists.
3
Note the condition for Zahir al-Riwayah
The text adds 'and they did not retract' — if later scholars have preferred another view, the mufti follows that new rajih.
Thus Zahir al-Riwayah is default, not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي

۳۲

اہتمام کرتا ہے لہذا راقم السطور اس کتاب کے پڑھانے والے اپنے جیسے بھائیوں سے گذارش کرتا ہے ( بڑوں کو کیسے مشورہ دے سکتا ہے ، چھوٹا منھ بڑی بات) کہ آپ بھی اس کتاب کی تدریس میں اگر اس طریقے کو اپنا ئیں ، تو ان شاء اللہ زیادہ نفع کی قوی امید ہے۔ اخیر میں اللہ پاک سے دست بہ دعا ہوں کہ اس ٹوٹی پھوٹی کوشش میں باقی رہ جانے والی ہر طرح کی خامیوں سے در گذر فرما کر اپنی بارگاہ عالی میں شرف قبولیت بخش دیں، آمین !!

متن عقود رسم المفتي

باسم الإله، شارع الأحكام * مع حمده أبدأ في نظامي
ثم الصلاة والسلام سرمدا * على نبي قد أتانا بالهدى
وآله وصحبه الكرام * على مر الدهر والأعوام
وبعد فالعبد الفقير المذنب * محمد بن عابدين يطلب
توفيق ربه الكريم الواحد * والفوز بالقبول في المقاصد
وفي نظم جوهر نضيد * وعقد در باهر فريد
وسميته عقود رسم المفتي * يحتاجه العامل أو من يفتي
وها أنا أشرع في المقصود * مستمنعا من فيض بحر الجود
اعلم بأن الواجب اتباع * ما ترجيحة عن أهله قد علما
أو كان ظاهر الرواية ولم * يرجعوا خلاف ذاك فاعلم
وكتب ظاهر الروايات أتت * ستا، وبالأصول أيضا سميت
صنفها محمد الشيباني * حرر فيها المذهب النعماني
الجامع الصغير والكبير * والسير الكبير والصغير
Aun al-Mughni fi Hall Uqud Rasm al-Mufti
32
He pays attention, therefore the writer of these lines requests from his brothers who teach this book (how can a small one advise the great? A small mouth a big matter) that you too adopt this method in teaching it, if Allah wills, there is strong hope of more benefit. Finally, I raise my hands in supplication to Allah the Pure that He overlook all kinds of deficiencies remaining in this broken effort and grant it the honor of acceptance in His exalted court, Ameen!

Text of Uqud Rasm al-Mufti

In the name of Allah, the Lawgiver of rulings * With His praise I begin my composition
Then prayer and peace eternally * Upon a prophet who brought us guidance
And his family and noble companions * Throughout the passage of time and years
And after, the needy sinful servant * Muhammad ibn Abidin seeks
The success of his generous unique Lord * And acceptance in his aims
And in an orderly jeweled composition * And a unique dazzling string of pearls
And I named it 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' * Needed by the practitioner or he who gives fatwa
And here I begin the purpose * Seeking aid from the overflowing sea of generosity
Know that it is obligatory to follow * What is deemed preferable (rajih) by its people, as is known
Or that which is from the manifest transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) and they did not * Retract, so know its contrary
And the books of the manifest transmissions came * Six, and they are also called 'al-Usul' (the fundamentals)
Authored by Muhammad al-Shaybani * In which he recorded the Nu'mani school
Al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Kabir * And al-Siyar al-Kabir and al-Saghir
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the matn 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' by Ibn Abidin. It begins with the basmala, praise of Allah, salawat upon the Prophet, and identification of the author and the book. The key ruling is stated in the lines: 'Know that it is obligatory to follow what is deemed preferable (rajih) by its people, as is known, or that which is from the manifest transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) and they did not retract, so know its contrary.' This establishes the fundamental duty of a mufti: he must not follow any opinion arbitrarily; instead, he must follow the preferred opinion (rajih) within the Hanafi school or, if no preference is determined, the opinions transmitted in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage then enumerates four of the six books: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Saghir. (The remaining two, al-Mabsut and al-Ziyadat, are mentioned in the continuation of the poem beyond this passage.) The Urdu introduction is a supplication by the commentator of this work, asking Allah's acceptance for his efforts in teaching.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted rulings in the six canonical books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered primary authoritative texts in the Hanafi school.
الراجح (ar-rajih): The preferred opinion within the madhhab, determined by weighing evidence and considering the strength of narrations.
رسم المفتي (rasm al-mufti): The rules and conditions governing the conduct of a mufti in issuing fatwas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the opening of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', what is the mufti obligated to follow?
A) Any opinion he prefers
B) The opinion of Abu Hanifa only
C) The rajih or Zahir al-Riwayah
D) The most recent fatwa

Key Takeaway
The mufti's fatwa must be based on either the preferred opinion (rajih) or the manifest transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) of the Hanafi school.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Hierarchy of Hanafi Texts and Authority of Commentaries
Explaining the relative precedence of the books and their commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the chronological order of the six core Hanafi books and explain why the Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is the most authoritative commentary for fatwa.

Core Idea
Later works and the Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi are the ultimate authority for Hanafi fatwa.

This passage from Rasm al-Mufti teaches the mufti how to prioritize sources. It explains that al-Mabsut (by Muhammad al-Shaybani) was written first, followed by al-Jami' al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir was the last of the six. Later books incorporate and supersede earlier ones. The strongest commentary on the six is the Mabsut of Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi, which is considered definitive. Knowing this hierarchy prevents errors in fatwa selection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six books and their chronological order
The six core books of Zahir al-Riwaya are: al-Mabsut (al-Asl), al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat. The passage states that al-Mabsut preceded the others, al-Jami' al-Saghir came after, and al-Siyar al-Kabir was the last.
Al-Asl is another name for al-Mabsut by Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Understand how later books relate to earlier ones
Later books are built upon earlier ones. What is in al-Jami' al-Saghir is based on al-Asl, and al-Siyar al-Kabir, being last, summarizes and refines earlier rulings. Thus, later texts take precedence in case of conflict.
3
Recognize the role of al-Kafi
Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is a compilation of all six books, making it a sufficient reference for the mufti. It incorporates the rulings from all earlier texts.
4
Identify the strongest commentary
The passage says the strongest commentary on al-Kafi is the Mabsut of Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi, comparing it to the sun. This commentary is the transmission authority; nothing in practice opposes it.
Be careful not to confuse al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi with al-Mabsut of al-Shaybani. The former is a sharh, the latter is a matn.
5
Apply the hierarchy in fatwa
When issuing a fatwa, a mufti should first consult later books (like al-Siyar al-Kabir) and then the reliable commentary (Mabsut al-Sarakhsi). Conflicting statements from earlier texts are overruled by later ones, and opposing views to al-Sarakhsi's commentary are rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واشتهر المبسوط بالأصل، وذا لسبقه الستة تصنيفا كذا الجامع الصغير بعده، فما فيه على الأصل، لذا تقدما وآخر الستة تصنيفا ورد السير الكبير، فهو المعتمد ويجمع الست كتاب الكافي للحاكم الشهيد فهو الكافي أقوى شروحه الذي كالشمس مبسوط شمس الأمة السرخسي معتمد النقول، ليس يعمل بخلفه، وليس عنه يعدل
And al-Mabsut is famous as al-Asl (the foundation), and that is because it preceded the six in authorship. Al-Jami' al-Saghir came after it, so what is in it is upon the foundation, thus it came first. And the last of the six in authorship is al-Siyar al-Kabir, so it is the relied-upon. And the book al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid gathers the six, so it is sufficient. The strongest of its commentaries, which is like the sun, is Mabsut Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi; it is the authority in transmissions, nothing is acted upon contrary to it, and nothing deviates from it.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ordering and authority of the foundational texts. Al-Mabsut by Muhammad al-Shaybani is called al-Asl because it was written before the other six books (though it itself is one of them). Al-Jami' al-Saghir came later and relies on it. Al-Siyar al-Kabir is the last of the six, hence the most relied-upon since later works incorporate earlier ones. Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is a compilation of all six and is considered sufficient. The best commentary is al-Mabsut of Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi, which is authoritative and cannot be contradicted. This helps the mufti know which sources to prioritize: later books and the Sarakhsi commentary.

Key Terms
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): A work by Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered al-Asl; also the name of the commentary by al-Sarakhsi
السير الكبير (al-Siyar al-Kabir): The last of the six core books by Muhammad al-Shaybani, covering rules of jihad and international relations
الكافي (al-Kafi): A compilation of the six books by al-Hakim al-Shahid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which commentary is described as 'like the sun' and is the authority in transmissions?
A) Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid
B) Mabsut Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi
C) Al-Jami' al-Saghir
D) Al-Ziyadat

Key Takeaway
The mufti must prioritize later books (especially al-Siyar al-Kabir) and the Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi as the ultimate authority in Hanafi fatwa.

The Six Books of Zahir al-Riwayah and Their Authority
Metred enumeration of foundational texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah in order of composition and identify each book's authority level in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy.

Core Idea
The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah form the ultimate textual authority for Hanafi fatwa; commentaries refine but never override them.

Imagine you are a mufti tasked with issuing a fatwa on a new financial transaction. Where do you begin? The Hanafi school has a clear hierarchy of textual sources. This passage from Ibn Kamal Pasha's metred work distils that hierarchy, naming the six core books by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and the most authoritative commentary. Understanding this order is essential for any student of Hanafi iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six books named in the verses
Scan the Arabic text and list each book by its common title (al-Mabsut/al-Asl, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, Masail al-Nawadir, Masail al-Nawazil). Note that Masail al-Nawadir and al-Nawazil are not part of the original six but are mentioned as related collections.
The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah are: al-Mabsut (al-Asl), al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Saghir (the latter two are implied by the collection al-Kafi).
2
Place the books in chronological order of composition
The passage states that al-Mabsut (al-Asl) was written first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, and finally al-Siyar al-Kabir. Internal evidence from the school confirms this sequence. Identify which book is earliest and which is latest.
Al-Mabsut (al-Asl) preceded all others; al-Siyar al-Kabir is the last in composition.
3
Distinguish between original compilations and later collections
The passage mentions 'Masail al-Nawadir' (rare transmissions) and 'Masail al-Nawazil' (later cases) as separate from the six. Recognise that these are not at the same level of authority as the Zahir al-Riwayah books.
Nawadir and Nawazil are considered secondary sources; a mufti should rely on Zahir al-Riwayah first.
4
Recognise the commentary hierarchy
The passage highlights al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid as a collection that gathers the six, but states that Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is the strongest commentary and the relied-upon source of transmission (mu'tamad al-nuqul).
Al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut is the supreme commentary; no fatwa can contradict it without strong evidence.
5
Apply the fatwa hierarchy principle
When issuing a fatwa, first consult al-Mabsut (al-Asl). If the ruling is clear, use it. If not, check al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Siyar al-Kabir, then refer to al-Kafi and finally al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut. Only then, if still unresolved, turn to Nawadir and Nawazil.
This principle ensures that the mufti's ruling is grounded in the most authentic transmissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الزِّيَادَاتُ مَعَ الْمُبْسُوط * تَوَاتَرَتْ بِالسَّنَدِ الْمَضْبُوط
ظاهر
كَذَا لَهُ مَسَائِلُ النَّوادِرٍ * إِسْنَادُهَا فِي الْكُتُبِ غَيْرُ وَبَعْدَهَا مَسَائِلُ النَّوَازِل خَرَّجَهَا الْأَشْيَاحُ بِالدَّلَائِل
وَاشْتَهَرَ الْمُبَسُوطُ بِالْأصْلِ، وَذَا لِسَبْقِهِ السِّتَّةَ تَصْنِيفًا كَذَا
الْجَامِعُ الصَّغِيْرُ بَعْدَهُ ، فَمَا فِيهِ عَلَى الْأَصْلِ، لِذَا تَقَدَّمَا
وَاخِرُ السِّتَّةِ تَصْنِيفًا وَرَدُ * السّيرُ الكَبِيرُ، فَهُوَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ
وَيَجْمَعُ السّتَ كِتَابُ الْكَافِي لِلْحَاكِمِ الشَّهِيدِ فَهُوَ الْكَافِي
أَقْوى شُرُوحِهِ الَّذِي كَالشَّمْسِ * مَبْسُوطُ شَمْسِ الْأُمَّةِ السَّرَخْسِي
مُعْتَمَدُ النُّقُولِ، لَيْسَ يُعْمَلْ بِخُلْفِهِ ، وَلَيْسَ عَنْهُ يُعْدَلَ
Then the Ziyadat along with the Mabsut are transmitted with sound chains. Likewise, he has Masail al-Nawadir—their chains in books are otherwise [weak]. After them are Masail al-Nawazil, which the shaykhs extracted by proofs. The Mabsut is famous as al-Asl, and this because it preceded the six in composition. The Jami' al-Saghir came after it; whatever is in it is according to al-Asl, so it takes precedence. The last of the six in composition is al-Siyar al-Kabir; it is the relied-upon. The book al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid collects the six; it is sufficient. The strongest of its commentaries, which is like the sun, is the Mabsut of Shams al-Aimma al-Sarakhsi—it is the relied-upon source of transmissions; one does not act contrary to it, nor deviate from it.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a metred enumeration of the foundational texts of the Hanafi madhhab. The author, Ibn Kamal Pasha, lists the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah as transmitted by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The first pair: al-Mabsut (also called al-Asl) and al-Ziyadat. Then Masail al-Nawadir (rare transmissions), then Masail al-Nawazil (later cases). He notes that al-Mabsut is called al-Asl because it was written before the other six. Jami' al-Saghir follows and depends on al-Asl. The last is al-Siyar al-Kabir, which is authoritative for siyar. Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid gathers all six. The best commentary is al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi, which is the final reference in transmission; no one acts against it or turns from it.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani transmitted with sound chains; they are the primary authority in the Hanafi school.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare transmissions from Imam Abu Hanifa or his students, not included in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which commentary on the six books is considered the strongest and the most relied-upon source of transmissions?
A) Al-Jami' al-Saghir
B) Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid
C) Mabsut al-Sarakhsi
D) Al-Siyar al-Kabir

Key Takeaway
The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, especially as clarified by al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut, form the bedrock of Hanafi fatwa; no ruling should contradict them.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Unbreakable Chain: Navigating the Hanafi Fatwa Hierarchy
Hierarchical principles for preferring Hanafi rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the primary sources in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy (zahir al-riwaya, mutun, shuruh, fatawa) and apply the rule that the majority of later scholars is preferred when no early transmission exists.

Core Idea
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy is a chain: zahir al-riwaya → mutun → shuruh → old fatawa, with the majority of later scholars determining the mufta bihi when early texts are silent.

Fatwa in the Hanafi school is not a free selection of any opinion. There is a strict ladder of authority. This lesson unpacks the foundational hierarchy: from the transmitted corpus of the founders down to the preferred views of the later masters. Understanding this chain ensures your fatwa is rooted in the school's most authoritative sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the highest authority
Recognize that zahir al-riwaya (the transmitted opinions from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) is the highest authority and must not be deviated from. Quote from the passage: 'وَظَاهِرُ الْمَرُوِيِّ، لَيْسَ يُعْدَلَ عَنْهُ إِلَى خِلَافِهِ'.
2
Recognize the next tier
Understand that the mutun (primary texts like al-Quduri) are preponderant over shuruh (commentaries) and old fatawa. The passage states: 'فَرَجَحَتْ عَلَى الشُّرُوحِ، وَالشُّرُوْحُ عَلَى الْفَتَاوَى الْقِدَمِ'.
This hierarchy is absolute unless a correction (taṣḥīḥ) occurs.
3
Understand the role of later scholars
When no transmission from early imams exists, the opinion of the majority of later scholars (like al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, the two Abu Ja'fars, al-Laith) is preferred. The passage explicitly lists these names.
If even these later authorities have no clear statement, the mufti must exert ijtihad with fear of Allah.
4
Apply the hierarchy
Given a hypothetical scenario, trace the correct path: check zahir al-riwaya first, then mutun, then shuruh, then old fatawa. If none provides a clear ruling, default to the majority of later scholars.
Always prioritize the highest available authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ خِلافُهُ الْمُصَحَّحَا * فَنَأْخُذُ الَّذِي لَهُمْ قَدْ وَضَحَا
فَإِنَّنَا نَرَاهُمُوْ قَدْ رَبَّحُوا مَقَالَ بَعْضٍ صَحْبِهِ ، وَصَحْحُوا
مِنْ ذَاكَ مَا قَدْ رَبَّحُوا لِزُفَرٍ مَقَالَهُ فِي سَبْعَةٍ وَّعَشَرٍ
ثُمَّ إِذَا لَمْ تُوْجَدِ الرِّوَايَهُ * عَنْ عُلَمَائِنَا ذَوِي الدِّرَايَهُ
وَاخْتَلَفَ الَّذِينَ قَدْ تَأَخَّرُوا * يُرَبَّحُ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْأَكْثَرُ
مِثْلُ الطَّحَاوِي وَأَبِي حَفْصِ الْكَبِيرُ * وَأَبَوَيْ جَعْفَرِ وَاللَّيثِ الشَّهِيرُ
وَحَيْثُ لَمْ تُوجَدُ لِهؤُلاء * مَقَالَةٌ ، وَاحْتِيجَ لِلاِفتاء
فَلْيَنْظُرِ الْمُفْتِي بِجِدٍ وَّاجْتِهَادُ * وَلْيَخْشَ بَطْشَ رَبِّهِ يَوْمَ الْمَعَادُ
فَلَيْسَ يَجْسُرُ عَلَى الْأَحْكَام * سِوَى شَقِي خَاسِرِ الْمَرَام
وَههُنَا ضَوَابِطُ مُحَرَّرَهُ * غَدَتْ لَدَى أَهْلِ النُّهَى مُقَرَّرَهُ
فِي كُلِّ أَبْوَابِ الْعِبَادَاتِ رُجّحُ قَوْلُ الْإِمَامِ مُطْلَقًا ، مَا لَمْ تَصِحُ عَنْهُ رِوَايَةٌ بِهَا الْغَيْرُ أَخَذُ مِثْلُ تَيَمُّمٍ لِمَنْ تَمُرًا نَّبَذ
وَكُلُّ فَرُعِ بِالْقَضَا تَعَلَّقَا * قَوْلُ أَبِي يُوسُفَ فِيهِ يُنتَقَى
وَفِي مَسَائِلِ ذَوِي الْأَرْحَامِ قَدْ أَفْتَوُا بِمَا يَقُولُهُ مُحَمَّدُ
وَرَبَّحُوا اسْتِحْسَانَهُمْ عَلَى الْقِياسُ إِلَّا مَسَائِلَ، وَمَا فِيهَا الْتِبَاسُ
وَظَاهِرُ الْمَرُوِيِّ، لَيْسَ يُعْدَلَ عَنْهُ إِلَى خِلَافِهِ ، إِذْ يُنْقَلْ لَا يَنْبَغِيُّ الْعُدُولُ عَنْ دِرَايَهُ إِذَا أَتَى بِوَفُقِهَا رِوَايَهُ
وَكُلُّ قَوْلٍ جَاءَ يَنْفِي الْكُفْرَا هِ عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ ، وَلَوْ ضَعِيفًا أَحْرَى
وَكُلُّ مَا رَجَعَ عَنْهُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ * صَارَ كَمَنْسُوحٍ ، فَغَيْرَهُ اعْتَمِدُ
وَكُلٌّ قَوْلٍ فِي الْمُتُونِ أَثْبِتَا فَذَاكَ تَرْجِيحٌ لَهُ ضِمُنَّا أَتَى
فَرَجَحَتْ عَلَى الشُّرُوحِ ، وَالشُّرُوْحُ عَلَى الْفَتَاوَى الْقِدَمِ مِنْ ذَاتِ رُجُوحُ
مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ سِوَاهُ لَفُظًا صُحِحَا فَالْأَرْجَحُ الَّذِي بِهِ قَدْ [؟]
وَسَابِقُ الْأَقْوَالِ فِي الْخَانِيَّهُ * وَمُلْتَقَى الْأَبْحُرِ ذُو مَزِيَّهُ
وَفِي سِوَاهُمَا اعْتُمِدَ مَا أَخَرُوا * دَليْلَهُ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُحَرَّرُ
كَمَا هُوَ الْعَادَةُ فِي الْهِدَايَهُ * وَنَحْوِهَا لِرَاجِحِ الدِّرَايَهُ
وَكَذَا إِذَا مَا وَاحِدًا قَدْ عَلَّلُوا * لَهُ ، وَتَعْلِيْلَ سِوَاهُ أَهْمَلُوا
وَحَيْثُمَا وَجَدْتَ قَوْلَيْنِ ، وَقَدْ صُحِحَ وَاحِدٌ، فَذَاكَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ
بِنَحْو : ذَا الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ الْأَشْبَهُ وَالأَظْهَرُ الْمُخْتَارُ ذَا وَالْأَوْجَهُ
أَوِ الصَّحِيحُ وَالأَصَحُ اكَدَ مِنْهُ ، وَقِيلَ : عَكْسُهُ الْمُؤكَّد ، كَذَا بِهِ يُفْتَى عَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى * وَذَانِ مِنْ جَمِيعِ تِلْكَ أَقْوى
وَإِن تَجِدُ تَصْحِيْحَ قَوْلَيْنِ وَرَدْ * فَاخْتَرُ لِمَا شِئْتَ ، فَكُلِّ مُعْتَمَدُ
إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَا صَحِيحًا وَأَصَحُ * أَوْقِيلَ: ذَا يُفْتَى بِهِ فَقَدْ رَجَحُ
أَوْ كَانَ فِي الْمُتُؤنِ أَوْ قَوْلَ الْإِمَامُ * أَوْظَاهِرَ الْمَرْوِيَ أَرْجُلُ الْعِظَامُ [؟]
قَالَ بِهِ ، أَو كَانَ الْإِسْتِحْسَانَا اَوْ زَادِ لِلَّاوُقَافِ نَفْعًا بَانَـا
Unless his disagreement is corrected, we take what is clear to them. Indeed we see that they have preferred the statement of some of his companions and corrected. From that they preferred Zufar's statement in seventeen issues. Then when no transmission is found from our scholars of knowledge, and the later ones differ, the one followed by the majority is preferred, like al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, and the two Abu Ja'fars and al-Laith the famous. And when no statement is found for these, and a fatwa is needed, let the mufti look with seriousness and ijtihad, and fear the grasp of his Lord on the Day of Return. None dares to issue legal rulings except a wretched loser. And here are established principles, settled by people of intellect: In all chapters of worship, the statement of the Imam is preferred absolutely, unless a transmission from him is authenticated by which the other took, like tayammum for one who discarded dates? And every branch related to qada, the statement of Abu Yusuf is chosen therein. And in issues of dhawil-arham, they gave fatwa with what Muhammad says. And they preferred their istihsan over qiyas except for some issues and what is ambiguous in them. And the apparent transmitted (zahir al-riwaya) is not deviated from to its opposite, for when a tradition is transmitted, one should not deviate from knowledge when a transmission agrees with it. And every statement that negates disbelief from a Muslim, even if weak, is more appropriate. And every ruling from which a mujtahid retracted becomes like abrogated, so rely on other than it. And every statement established in the texts (mutun) is a tarjih for it implicitly. So they (the mutun) are preponderant over commentaries, and commentaries over old fatwas that have preponderance. Unless another wording is corrected, so the most preponderant is the one with which... And the earlier statements in al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhar have superiority. And in other than them, rely on what the later ones have, for its proof because it is the corrected (al-muharrar). As is the custom in al-Hidayah and similar works for the preponderant of knowledge. And similarly when they give an illa (rationale) for one and neglect the illa of the other. And wherever you find two statements and one is corrected, that is the relied-upon. By expressions like: 'the fatwa is on this', 'the most similar', 'the most apparent', 'the chosen', 'this and the most appropriate'. Or 'the sahih and asahh' is stronger than it, and it is said its opposite is emphasized. Thus the fatwa is given on it, and these two are strongest of all. And if you find the correction of two statements that have been reported, then choose whichever you wish, for each is relied-upon. Except when they are sahih and asahh, or it is said 'this is the fatwa', then it has preponderance. Or it is in the texts, or the statement of the Imam, or the apparent transmitted, the strongest of all? He said by it, or it is istihsan, or it gives clear benefit for the endowments.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a methodological exposition of the hierarchy of authority within the Hanafi madhhab for issuing fatwas. The text is a poetic summary (nazm) of the principles of tarjih (preference) when multiple opinions exist. It begins by establishing that when there is a preferred (musahhah) opinion from the founding imams, we take what is clear from them. The author notes instances where the school preferred Zufar's opinion in seventeen specific issues. When no direct transmission (riwaya) from the early imams exists, and later scholars differ, the opinion of the majority among them is preferred, such as al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, the two Abu Ja'fars, and al-Laith. If even these later authorities have no clear statement, the mufti must exert ijtihad with fear of Allah. Then the text lays down several specific rules: (1) In all chapters of 'ibadat (worship), the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa is absolutely preponderant, unless a transmission from him is corrected that the other (Abu Yusuf or Muhammad) acted upon, with the example of tayammum. (2) In all branches related to judicial matters (qada), the statement of Abu Yusuf is chosen. (3) In issues of dhawil-arham (inheritance of distant kindred), the fatwa is according to Muhammad al-Shaybani. (4) Their istihsan is preponderant over qiyas except for certain ambiguous issues. (5) The apparent transmitted (zahir al-riwaya) from the madhhab founders is not to be deviated from, as knowledge (diraya) should not contradict transmission. (6) Any statement that negates disbelief from a Muslim, even if weak, is given precedence (this is the well-known rule 'al-khuruj min al-khilaf mustahabb'). (7) A ruling from which a mujtahid retracted is like abrogated. (8) A statement recorded in the primary texts (mutun, like al-Quduri) is inherently preponderant. The hierarchy of sources is: mutun > shuruh (commentaries) > old fatawa. (9) Exceptions: if another wording is corrected, the most preponderant is considered. (10) The early compilations like al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhar have superiority; after them, later works (like al-Hidayah) are relied upon. (11) When scholars give an illa (rationale) for one opinion and neglect another, that opinion is preferred. (12) If two statements exist and one is explicitly 'corrected' (sahhaha), that is the relied-upon. Expressions like 'asbah' (most similar), 'azhar' (most apparent), 'al-mukhtar' (chosen), 'awjah' (most appropriate), 'sahih' (correct), and 'asahh' (most correct) indicate preference. (13) If both statements are corrected, the mufti may choose any. (14) Exceptions: if one is 'sahih' and the other 'asahh', or if it is explicitly said 'this is the fatwa', or if the opinion is in the mutun, or is the statement of the Imam, or is the apparent transmitted, then it is the strongest. Also if it is istihsan or clearly beneficial for awqaf (endowments), it is preferred.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjih): Preferring one legal opinion over another based on established criteria.
قول الإمام (qawl al-imam): The statement of Imam Abu Hanifa.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The transmitted opinions from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the highest authority in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy when it is available?
A) Old fatawa
B) Commentaries (shuruh)
C) Zahir al-riwaya
D) The majority of later scholars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy is a fixed chain: zahir al-riwaya → mutun → shuruh → old fatawa, with the majority of later scholars resolving gaps.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Domain-Specific Tarjih: Each Imam Has His Arena
Subject-specific tarjih rules for Hanafi fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the specific tarjih rules for ibadat, qada, and inheritance of dhawil-arham, and explain why istihsan is preferred over qiyas in Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
In ibadat, Abu Hanifa's word is absolute; in qada, Abu Yusuf leads; for distant kindred, Muhammad rules; and istihsan overrides qiyas—each domain has its own imam.

The Hanafi school is not monochrome. Each of the three major imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad—has a primary domain where his opinion is given precedence. This lesson clarifies those domains and the special status of istihsan over qiyas. Knowing these rules prevents misapplication of tarjih across different fiqh chapters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the domain of ibadat
The passage states: 'فِي كُلِّ أَبْوَابِ الْعِبَادَاتِ رُجّحُ قَوْلُ الْإِمَامِ مُطْلَقًا' meaning in all chapters of worship, the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is absolutely preponderant.
2
Understand the exception
The exception is: 'مَا لَمْ تَصِحُ عَنْهُ رِوَايَةٌ بِهَا الْغَيْرُ أَخَذُ' i.e., unless a transmission from Abu Hanifa is authenticated where the other (Abu Yusuf or Muhammad) acted upon it. The example of tayammum is given.
3
Distinguish qada and dhawil-arham
For judicial matters (qada), the statement of Abu Yusuf is chosen: 'وَكُلُّ فَرُعِ بِالْقَضَا تَعَلَّقَا قَوْلُ أَبِي يُوسُفَ فِيهِ يُنتَقَى'. For inheritance of distant kindred (dhawil-arham), fatwa is given according to Muhammad: 'وَفِي مَسَائِلِ ذَوِي الْأَرْحَامِ قَدْ أَفْتَوُا بِمَا يَقُولُهُ مُحَمَّدُ'.
4
Analyze istihsan's position
The passage says: 'وَرَبَّحُوا اسْتِحْسَانَهُمْ عَلَى الْقِياسُ إِلَّا مَسَائِلَ' meaning they (the earlier scholars) preferred istihsan over qiyas except for certain issues.
5
Apply to a mixed case
If a case involves both ibadat and qada, one must apply the rule corresponding to the primary subject. For example, if a judicial matter touches on worship (e.g., qada of missed prayers), the rule for qada (Abu Yusuf) applies, not the ibadat rule.
The passage separates the categories; the mufti must classify the case correctly.

Source Text

مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ خِلافُهُ الْمُصَحَّحَا * فَنَأْخُذُ الَّذِي لَهُمْ قَدْ وَضَحَا
فَإِنَّنَا نَرَاهُمُوْ قَدْ رَبَّحُوا مَقَالَ بَعْضٍ صَحْبِهِ ، وَصَحْحُوا
مِنْ ذَاكَ مَا قَدْ رَبَّحُوا لِزُفَرٍ مَقَالَهُ فِي سَبْعَةٍ وَّعَشَرٍ
ثُمَّ إِذَا لَمْ تُوْجَدِ الرِّوَايَهُ * عَنْ عُلَمَائِنَا ذَوِي الدِّرَايَهُ
وَاخْتَلَفَ الَّذِينَ قَدْ تَأَخَّرُوا * يُرَبَّحُ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْأَكْثَرُ
مِثْلُ الطَّحَاوِي وَأَبِي حَفْصِ الْكَبِيرُ * وَأَبَوَيْ جَعْفَرِ وَاللَّيثِ الشَّهِيرُ
وَحَيْثُ لَمْ تُوجَدُ لِهؤُلاء * مَقَالَةٌ ، وَاحْتِيجَ لِلاِفتاء
فَلْيَنْظُرِ الْمُفْتِي بِجِدٍ وَّاجْتِهَادُ * وَلْيَخْشَ بَطْشَ رَبِّهِ يَوْمَ الْمَعَادُ
فَلَيْسَ يَجْسُرُ عَلَى الْأَحْكَام * سِوَى شَقِي خَاسِرِ الْمَرَام
وَههُنَا ضَوَابِطُ مُحَرَّرَهُ * غَدَتْ لَدَى أَهْلِ النُّهَى مُقَرَّرَهُ
فِي كُلِّ أَبْوَابِ الْعِبَادَاتِ رُجّحُ قَوْلُ الْإِمَامِ مُطْلَقًا ، مَا لَمْ تَصِحُ عَنْهُ رِوَايَةٌ بِهَا الْغَيْرُ أَخَذُ مِثْلُ تَيَمُّمٍ لِمَنْ تَمُرًا نَّبَذ

وَظَاهِرُ الْمَرُوِيِّ، لَيْسَ يُعْدَلَ عَنْهُ إِلَى خِلَافِهِ ، إِذْ يُنْقَلْ لَا يَنْبَغِيُّ الْعُدُولُ عَنْ دِرَايَهُ إِذَا أَتَى بِوَفُقِهَا رِوَايَهُ
وَكُلُّ قَوْلٍ جَاءَ يَنْفِي الْكُفْرَا هِ عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ ، وَلَوْ ضَعِيفًا أَحْرَى
وَكُلُّ مَا رَجَعَ عَنْهُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ * صَارَ كَمَنْسُوحٍ ، فَغَيْرَهُ اعْتَمِدُ
وَكُلٌّ قَوْلٍ فِي الْمُتُونِ أَثْبِتَا فَذَاكَ تَرْجِيحٌ لَهُ ضِمُنَّا أَتَى
فَرَجَحَتْ عَلَى الشُّرُوحِ ، وَالشُّرُوْحُ عَلَى الْفَتَاوَى الْقِدَمِ مِنْ ذَاتِ رُجُوحُ
مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ سِوَاهُ لَفُظًا صُحِحَا فَالْأَرْجَحُ الَّذِي بِهِ قَدْ [؟]

كَمَا هُوَ الْعَادَةُ فِي الْهِدَايَهُ * وَنَحْوِهَا لِرَاجِحِ الدِّرَايَهُ
وَكَذَا إِذَا مَا وَاحِدًا قَدْ عَلَّلُوا * لَهُ ، وَتَعْلِيْلَ سِوَاهُ أَهْمَلُوا
وَحَيْثُمَا وَجَدْتَ قَوْلَيْنِ ، وَقَدْ صُحِحَ وَاحِدٌ، فَذَاكَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ
بِنَحْو : ذَا الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ الْأَشْبَهُ وَالأَظْهَرُ الْمُخْتَارُ ذَا وَالْأَوْجَهُ
أَوِ الصَّحِيحُ وَالأَصَحُ اكَدَ مِنْهُ ، وَقِيلَ : عَكْسُهُ الْمُؤكَّد ، كَذَا بِهِ يُفْتَى عَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى * وَذَانِ مِنْ جَمِيعِ تِلْكَ أَقْوى
وَإِن تَجِدُ تَصْحِيْحَ قَوْلَيْنِ وَرَدْ * فَاخْتَرُ لِمَا شِئْتَ ، فَكُلِّ مُعْتَمَدُ
إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَا صَحِيحًا وَأَصَحُ * أَوْقِيلَ: ذَا يُفْتَى بِهِ فَقَدْ رَجَحُ
أَوْ كَانَ فِي الْمُتُؤنِ أَوْ قَوْلَ الْإِمَامُ * أَوْظَاهِرَ الْمَرْوِيَ أَرْجُلُ الْعِظَامُ [؟]
قَالَ بِهِ ، أَو كَانَ الْإِسْتِحْسَانَا اَوْ زَادِ لِلَّاوُقَافِ نَفْعًا بَانَـا
Unless his disagreement is corrected, we take what is clear to them. Indeed we see that they have preferred the statement of some of his companions and corrected. From that they preferred Zufar's statement in seventeen issues. Then when no transmission is found from our scholars of knowledge, and the later ones differ, the one followed by the majority is preferred, like al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, and the two Abu Ja'fars and al-Laith the famous. And when no statement is found for these, and a fatwa is needed, let the mufti look with seriousness and ijtihad, and fear the grasp of his Lord on the Day of Return. None dares to issue legal rulings except a wretched loser. And here are established principles, settled by people of intellect: In all chapters of worship, the statement of the Imam is preferred absolutely, unless a transmission from him is authenticated by which the other took, like tayammum for one who discarded dates? And every branch related to qada, the statement of Abu Yusuf is chosen therein. And in issues of dhawil-arham, they gave fatwa with what Muhammad says. And they preferred their istihsan over qiyas except for some issues and what is ambiguous in them. And the apparent transmitted (zahir al-riwaya) is not deviated from to its opposite, for when a tradition is transmitted, one should not deviate from knowledge when a transmission agrees with it. And every statement that negates disbelief from a Muslim, even if weak, is more appropriate. And every ruling from which a mujtahid retracted becomes like abrogated, so rely on other than it. And every statement established in the texts (mutun) is a tarjih for it implicitly. So they (the mutun) are preponderant over commentaries, and commentaries over old fatwas that have preponderance. Unless another wording is corrected, so the most preponderant is the one with which... And the earlier statements in al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhar have superiority. And in other than them, rely on what the later ones have, for its proof because it is the corrected (al-muharrar). As is the custom in al-Hidayah and similar works for the preponderant of knowledge. And similarly when they give an illa (rationale) for one and neglect the illa of the other. And wherever you find two statements and one is corrected, that is the relied-upon. By expressions like: 'the fatwa is on this', 'the most similar', 'the most apparent', 'the chosen', 'this and the most appropriate'. Or 'the sahih and asahh' is stronger than it, and it is said its opposite is emphasized. Thus the fatwa is given on it, and these two are strongest of all. And if you find the correction of two statements that have been reported, then choose whichever you wish, for each is relied-upon. Except when they are sahih and asahh, or it is said 'this is the fatwa', then it has preponderance. Or it is in the texts, or the statement of the Imam, or the apparent transmitted, the strongest of all? He said by it, or it is istihsan, or it gives clear benefit for the endowments.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a methodological exposition of the hierarchy of authority within the Hanafi madhhab for issuing fatwas. The text is a poetic summary (nazm) of the principles of tarjih (preference) when multiple opinions exist. It begins by establishing that when there is a preferred (musahhah) opinion from the founding imams, we take what is clear from them. The author notes instances where the school preferred Zufar's opinion in seventeen specific issues. When no direct transmission (riwaya) from the early imams exists, and later scholars differ, the opinion of the majority among them is preferred, such as al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, the two Abu Ja'fars, and al-Laith. If even these later authorities have no clear statement, the mufti must exert ijtihad with fear of Allah. Then the text lays down several specific rules: (1) In all chapters of 'ibadat (worship), the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa is absolutely preponderant, unless a transmission from him is corrected that the other (Abu Yusuf or Muhammad) acted upon, with the example of tayammum. (2) In all branches related to judicial matters (qada), the statement of Abu Yusuf is chosen. (3) In issues of dhawil-arham (inheritance of distant kindred), the fatwa is according to Muhammad al-Shaybani. (4) Their istihsan is preponderant over qiyas except for certain ambiguous issues. (5) The apparent transmitted (zahir al-riwaya) from the madhhab founders is not to be deviated from, as knowledge (diraya) should not contradict transmission. (6) Any statement that negates disbelief from a Muslim, even if weak, is given precedence (this is the well-known rule 'al-khuruj min al-khilaf mustahabb'). (7) A ruling from which a mujtahid retracted is like abrogated. (8) A statement recorded in the primary texts (mutun, like al-Quduri) is inherently preponderant. The hierarchy of sources is: mutun > shuruh (commentaries) > old fatawa. (9) Exceptions: if another wording is corrected, the most preponderant is considered. (10) The early compilations like al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhar have superiority; after them, later works (like al-Hidayah) are relied upon. (11) When scholars give an illa (rationale) for one opinion and neglect another, that opinion is preferred. (12) If two statements exist and one is explicitly 'corrected' (sahhaha), that is the relied-upon. Expressions like 'asbah' (most similar), 'azhar' (most apparent), 'al-mukhtar' (chosen), 'awjah' (most appropriate), 'sahih' (correct), and 'asahh' (most correct) indicate preference. (13) If both statements are corrected, the mufti may choose any. (14) Exceptions: if one is 'sahih' and the other 'asahh', or if it is explicitly said 'this is the fatwa', or if the opinion is in the mutun, or is the statement of the Imam, or is the apparent transmitted, then it is the strongest. Also if it is istihsan or clearly beneficial for awqaf (endowments), it is preferred.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjih): Preferring one legal opinion over another based on established criteria.
قول الإمام (qawl al-imam): The statement of Imam Abu Hanifa.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The transmitted opinions from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, whose statement is chosen for every branch related to qada (judicial matters)?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad
D) Al-Tahawi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has domain-specific tarjih rules: Abu Hanifa in ibadat, Abu Yusuf in qada, Muhammad in dhawil-arham, and istihsan generally over qiyas.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Decoding the Vocabulary of Tarjih: Sahih, Asahh, and Beyond
Expressions and rules for preferring Hanafi statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key expressions of tarjih (sahih, asahh, asbah, etc.) and apply the rules for when a statement is explicitly corrected or when both are corrected.

Core Idea
The words 'sahih', 'asahh', 'asbah', 'azhar', and 'al-fatwa alayhi' each carry specific weight in the tarjih hierarchy—and if an opinion is explicitly corrected, it becomes the mufta bihi.

Not all statements in Hanafi texts are equal. The later scholars have developed a precise vocabulary to indicate which opinion is preferred. Expressions like 'sahih', 'asahh', 'asbah', and 'al-fatwa alayhi' are not just stylistic; they determine the operative ruling. This lesson decodes that vocabulary and teaches the rules when two statements are both corrected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the correction expressions
The passage lists: 'ذَا الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ', 'الْأَشْبَهُ', 'الْأَظْهَرُ', 'الْمُخْتَارُ', 'الْأَوْجَهُ', 'الصَّحِيحُ', 'الْأَصَحُ'. Recognize that these are technical terms used by later Hanafi scholars to indicate preference.
2
Understand their relative strength
The passage clarifies that 'asahh' (أَصَح) is stronger than 'sahih' (صَحِيح): 'أَوِ الصَّحِيحُ وَالأَصَحُ اكَدَ مِنْهُ'. However, it also notes that some say the opposite. The author states that both 'asbah' and 'azhar' are among the strongest.
3
Apply the rule for a single corrected opinion
If one of two statements is explicitly corrected (musahhah), that is the relied-upon (mu'tamad). The passage says: 'وَحَيْثُمَا وَجَدْتَ قَوْلَيْنِ، وَقَدْ صُحِحَ وَاحِدٌ، فَذَاكَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ'.
4
Apply the rule for two corrected opinions
If both are corrected, the mufti may choose any: 'فَاخْتَرُ لِمَا شِئْتَ، فَكُلِّ مُعْتَمَدُ'. But there are exceptions: if one is 'sahih' and the other 'asahh', or if it is explicitly said 'this is the fatwa', then the stronger prevails.
5
Recognize other indicators
Other indicators of preference include: when an illa (rationale) is given for one opinion and neglected for another; when the opinion is in the mutun or is the qawl al-imam; when it is the zahir al-riwaya; when it is based on istihsan; or when it is clearly beneficial for awqaf (endowments).

Source Text

فَلْيَنْظُرِ الْمُفْتِي بِجِدٍ وَّاجْتِهَادُ * وَلْيَخْشَ بَطْشَ رَبِّهِ يَوْمَ الْمَعَادُ
فَلَيْسَ يَجْسُرُ عَلَى الْأَحْكَام * سِوَى شَقِي خَاسِرِ الْمَرَام
وَههُنَا ضَوَابِطُ مُحَرَّرَهُ * غَدَتْ لَدَى أَهْلِ النُّهَى مُقَرَّرَهُ
فِي كُلِّ أَبْوَابِ الْعِبَادَاتِ رُجّحُ قَوْلُ الْإِمَامِ مُطْلَقًا ، مَا لَمْ تَصِحُ عَنْهُ رِوَايَةٌ بِهَا الْغَيْرُ أَخَذُ مِثْلُ تَيَمُّمٍ لِمَنْ تَمُرًا نَّبَذ
وَكُلُّ فَرُعِ بِالْقَضَا تَعَلَّقَا * قَوْلُ أَبِي يُوسُفَ فِيهِ يُنتَقَى
وَفِي مَسَائِلِ ذَوِي الْأَرْحَامِ قَدْ أَفْتَوُا بِمَا يَقُولُهُ مُحَمَّدُ

وَظَاهِرُ الْمَرُوِيِّ، لَيْسَ يُعْدَلَ عَنْهُ إِلَى خِلَافِهِ ، إِذْ يُنْقَلْ لَا يَنْبَغِيُّ الْعُدُولُ عَنْ دِرَايَهُ إِذَا أَتَى بِوَفُقِهَا رِوَايَهُ

وَكُلُّ مَا رَجَعَ عَنْهُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ * صَارَ كَمَنْسُوحٍ ، فَغَيْرَهُ اعْتَمِدُ
وَكُلٌّ قَوْلٍ فِي الْمُتُونِ أَثْبِتَا فَذَاكَ تَرْجِيحٌ لَهُ ضِمُنَّا أَتَى
فَرَجَحَتْ عَلَى الشُّرُوحِ ، وَالشُّرُوْحُ عَلَى الْفَتَاوَى الْقِدَمِ مِنْ ذَاتِ رُجُوحُ
مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ سِوَاهُ لَفُظًا صُحِحَا فَالْأَرْجَحُ الَّذِي بِهِ قَدْ [؟]
وَسَابِقُ الْأَقْوَالِ فِي الْخَانِيَّهُ * وَمُلْتَقَى الْأَبْحُرِ ذُو مَزِيَّهُ
وَفِي سِوَاهُمَا اعْتُمِدَ مَا أَخَرُوا * دَليْلَهُ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُحَرَّرُ
كَمَا هُوَ الْعَادَةُ فِي الْهِدَايَهُ * وَنَحْوِهَا لِرَاجِحِ الدِّرَايَهُ

(12) If two statements exist and one is explicitly 'corrected' (sahhaha), that is the relied-upon. (13) If both statements are corrected, the mufti may choose any. قول الإمام (qawl al-imam): The statement of Imam Abu Hanifa.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The transmitted opinions from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

A) The 'sahih'

D) Neither, need further ijtihad

Key Takeaway
Technical expressions like 'asahh', 'asbah', and 'al-fatwa alayhi' are keys to determining the mufta bihi, and when both opinions are corrected, the mufti has choice unless an exception applies.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
Two Core Principles for Muftis: Avoiding Takfir and Following Retractions
First two verses of the poem: rules for favoring lenient sayings and retracted rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply two key principles from Rasm al-Mufti: preferring the opinion that avoids takfir over stronger opposing evidence, and discarding a mujtahid's retracted ruling in favor of his later view.

Core Idea
Always favor a ruling that avoids calling a Muslim a kafir, even if weak; a mujtahid's retraction abrogates his old view.

Muftis often face conflicting reports and must decide which opinion to rely on. These two verses from the poem provide decisive hierarchical rules: first, protect the faith of a Muslim by avoiding takfir whenever possible; second, track the development of the madhhab by discarding any ruling the mujtahid himself later retracted. These principles ensure fatwas are both merciful and up-to-date.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict
When two opinions conflict on an issue that could involve kufr, note that one leads to takfir and the other does not.
The principle applies even if the conflicting opinion is about a non-kufr matter? Only applies when kufr is a possible outcome.
2
Apply the first rule
Choose the opinion that avoids declaring a Muslim a kafir, even if its evidence is weaker than the opposing view.
The poet emphasizes 'even if weak' (wa law da'ifan) to show that protecting a Muslim's faith outweighs evidentiary strength.
3
Recognize a retraction
If you learn that the mujtahid (e.g., Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) later retracted a specific ruling, treat that earlier ruling as invalid.
The poem compares it to abrogation (mansukh) in the Quran, meaning it has no legal effect.
4
Determine the operative ruling
Rely on the mujtahid's later position (the non-retracted view) for fatwa. If multiple retractions occur, the most recent one prevails.
This requires knowing the chronological order of the mujtahid's works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ قَوْلٍ جَاءَ يَنْفِي الْكُفْرَ عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ، وَلَوْ ضَعِيفًا أَحْرَى. وَكُلُّ مَا رَجَعَ عَنْهُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ صَارَ كَمَنْسُوحٍ، فَغَيْرَهُ اعْتَمِدُ.
Every statement that comes negating disbelief from a Muslim, even if weak, is more worthy. And everything a mujtahid retracts from becomes like abrogated, so rely on other than it.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage from the poem Rawd al-Mufti gives two fundamental guidelines for a mufti. First, when faced with conflicting narrations or rulings, prefer any statement that avoids declaring a Muslim an unbeliever (takfir), even if that statement is weak in terms of proof. Second, if a mujtahid (like Abu Hanifa or his students) retracts a previous ruling, that earlier ruling becomes like a mansukh (abrogated) and is no longer acted upon; the later position is the relied-up one. These principles prioritize leniency and follow the development of the madhhab.

Key Terms
كفر (kufr): Unbelief; the quality that takes a person out of Islam. The poem instructs to favor any interpretation that avoids such a charge.
رجوع المجتهد (ruju' al-mujtahid): The mujtahid's retraction of a former opinion. Such a retraction renders the old opinion invalid, like an abrogated verse.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling that has been replaced by a later ruling. Here it is used analogously for a retracted fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two narrations conflict, one declares a Muslim a kafir and the other avoids that, which should a mufti prefer?
A) The one that declares kufr because it may be stronger.
B) The one that negates kufr, even if weaker.
C) The one with the strongest chain.
D) The one that agrees with the majority.

Key Takeaway
When issuing fatwa, always prioritize a ruling that avoids takfir, and always follow the mujtahid's latest position.

Custom and Weak Hadith in Fatwa and Judgment
Three fatwa rules in verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the three fatwa rules: using mafhum without contradicting explicit text, relying on custom, and restricting weak hadith to necessity or knowledgeable questioners, while judges are prohibited from using weak hadith.

Core Idea
A mufti may use mafhum and custom, but weak hadith are not for fatwa except necessity, and never for a judge.

The poem summarizes key principles of the mufti's methodology (rasm al-mufti). It clarifies that implied meanings from narrations and customary practices are valid sources, provided they do not conflict with explicit texts. Weak hadith, however, are severely restricted: they cannot be used for fatwa generally, and judges cannot base verdicts on them at all. Understanding these distinctions is essential for issuing sound legal opinions and judgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Rules
Read the poem and locate the three distinct rules: (1) acting on mafhum, (2) consideration of custom, (3) restrictions on weak hadith.
Each rule is signaled by a clear imperative or prohibition.
2
Analyze the Rule on Mafhum
The poem says: 'اعْمَلْ بِمَفْهُومِ رِوَايَاتٍ أَتَى مَا لَمْ يُخَالِفْ لِصَرِيحٍ ثَبَنَا.' This means you may act on the implied meaning (mafhum) of narrations as long as it does not contradict an explicit established text.
Mafhum refers to the understood meaning derived from the text's context or implication.
3
Analyze the Rule on Custom (Urf)
The poem states: 'وَالْعُرْفُ فِي الشَّرْعِ لَهُ اعْتِبَارُ لِذَا عَلَيْهِ الْحُكْمُ قَدْ يُدَارُ.' Custom has legal weight in Sharia, and many rulings are based on it.
Hanafis consider urf a valid source, especially in mu'amalat, as long as it doesn't contradict a clear text.
4
Analyze the Rule on Weak Hadith
The poem prohibits using a weak hadith for fatwa generally ('وَلَا يَجُوزُ بِالضَّعِيفِ الْعَمَلُ * وَلَا بِهِ يُجَابُ مَنْ جَاءَ يَسْأَلُ') but allows two exceptions: necessity or a questioner with famous knowledge. However, a judge ('الْقَاضِي') cannot use it, and if he does, his judgment is void.
The restriction is tighter for judges because their rulings are binding; they must rely on strong evidence from the preponderant views of the madhhab.
5
Understand the Hanafi Judge's Constraint
The poem ends with 'لَاسِيَّمَا قُضَاتُنَا إِذْ قَيَّدُوا * بِرَاجِحِ الْمَذْهَبِ حِينَ قَلَّدُوا.' Hanafi judges are bound by the preponderant (rajih) views of the madhhab, so they cannot use weak hadith regardless.
This reflects the later Hanafi practice of taqlid of the school's authoritative positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْمَلْ بِمَفْهُومِ رِوَايَاتٍ أَتَى مَا لَمْ يُخَالِفْ لِصَرِيحٍ ثَبَنَا. وَالْعُرْفُ فِي الشَّرْعِ لَهُ اعْتِبَارُ لِذَا عَلَيْهِ الْحُكْمُ قَدْ يُدَارُ. وَلَا يَجُوزُ بِالضَّعِيفِ الْعَمَلُ * وَلَا بِهِ يُجَابُ مَنْ جَاءَ يَسْأَلُ. إِلَّا لِعَامِلٍ لَهُ ضَرُورَةٌ * أَوْ مَنْ لَهُ مَعْرِفَةٌ مَشْهُورَةٌ. لَكِنَّمَا الْقَاضِي بِهِ لَا يَقْضِي وَإِنْ قَضَى فَحُكْمُهُ لَا يَمْضِي. لَاسِيَّمَا قُضَاتُنَا إِذْ قَيَّدُوا * بِرَاجِحِ الْمَذْهَبِ حِينَ قَلَّدُوا.
And act upon the implied meaning (mafhum) of narrations as long as it does not contradict an explicit established text. And custom (urf) in Sharia has consideration; therefore rulings are often based on it. And it is not permissible to act upon a weak (hadith), nor to answer a questioner with it, except for an act of necessity or one who has famous knowledge. But the judge does not judge by it; if he judges, his judgment does not pass. Especially our judges, for they are bound by the preponderant of the madhhab when they follow.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This final section covers three important points. First, the mufti may rely on the mafhum (implied meaning) of narrations (such as a faqih's understanding of a hadith) as long as it does not contradict a clear, established text (nas sarih). Second, custom (urf) is a recognized source in Islamic law, and many rulings are based upon it. Third, weak hadith have limited use: they cannot be acted upon in general, nor can a mufti give a fatwa based solely on a weak hadith, except in cases of necessity (e.g., if no other evidence exists) or if the questioner is a person of well-known religious knowledge and can appreciate the weakness. However, a qadi (judge) cannot base his verdict on a weak hadith; if he does, the judgment is ineffective and does not take effect. This is especially true for Hanafi judges, who are bound to follow the preponderant views of the Hanafi madhhab. The poem ends with praise to Allah.

Key Terms
مفهوم الروايات (mafhum al-riwayat): The implied meaning derived from transmitted narrations (hadith or athar), as opposed to the explicit wording.
العرف (al-urf): Customary practice among people that is not contradicted by Sharia.
الحديث الضعيف (al-hadith al-da'if): A hadith that does not meet the conditions of authenticity. It cannot be used for fatwa or judgment generally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The verdict is valid if the judge deems the hadith reliable.
B) The verdict is void and does not take effect.
C) The verdict can be appealed but stands otherwise.
D) The judge is required to refer to a mufti for confirmation.

Key Takeaway
A mufti may use mafhum and custom, but weak hadith are almost never permissible for fatwa, and never for a judge.

Rules for Mufti's Preference, Custom, and Weak Hadith
Concluding rules from the poem on mufti's methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for preferring rulings, acting on custom, and restricting the use of weak hadith in fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must prefer the preponderant opinion, may consider custom, and cannot issue fatwa based on weak hadith except for personal necessity.

This passage from the poem on mufti methodology lays down critical principles that govern the mufti's practice. It addresses how to choose between conflicting opinions, the role of custom in Shari'ah, and the strict limitation on using weak hadith. Understanding these rules ensures that the mufti operates within the established hierarchy of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios for tarjih
The mufti chooses the more suitable (for the time) or clearer proof when authentications conflict or no explicit text exists.
Tarjih is based on strength of evidence and contextual appropriateness.
2
Understand the rule on mafhum riwāyāt
Act on the implied meaning of narrations only if it does not contradict an explicit established text (ṣarīḥ thabana).
Mafhum (implied meaning) is subordinate to explicit texts.
3
Recognize the authority of ‘urf
Custom has legal consideration in Shari'ah, and rulings may be based on it.
‘Urf is especially weighty in mu‘amalat (transactions).
4
Delineate the prohibition of weak hadith
Acting on weak hadith is not permissible for fatwa, except for a person with necessity or a well-known scholar (for personal practice).
Judges cannot use weak hadith; if they do, the judgment is void.
5
Apply the restriction on judges
Hanafi judges are bound to the preponderant view of the madhhab and cannot use weak hadith.
This reflects the taqlīd obligation for judges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَوْ كَانَ ذَا أَوْفَقَ لِلزَّمَانِ أَوْ كَانَ ذَا أَوضَحَ فِي الْبُرْهَانِ هَذَا إِذَا تَعَارَضَ التَّصْحِيحُ أَوَلَمْ يَكُنْ أَصْلًا بِهِ تَصْرِيحُ فَتَأْخُذُ الَّذِي لَهُ مُرَجّح * مِمَّا عَلِمْتَهُ ، فَهَذَا الْأَوْضَحْ وَاعْمَلُ بِمَفْهُومِ رِوَايَاتٍ أَتَى مَا لَمْ يُخَالِفُ لِصَرِيحٍ ثَبَنَا وَالْعُرُقُ فِي الشَّرُعَ لَهُ اعْتِبَارُ لِذَا عَلَيْهِ الْحُكْمُ قَدْ يُدَارُ وَلاَ يَجُوزُ بِالصَّعِيفِ الْعَمَلَ * وَلا بِهِ يُجَابُ مَنْ جَاءَ يَسْأَلُ إِلَّا لِعَامِل لَهُ ضَرُورَهُ * أَوْمَنْ لَهُ مَعْرِفَةٌ مُشْهُورَهُ لَكِنَّمَا الْقَاضِي بِهِ لَا يَقْضِي وَإِنْ قَضَا فَحُكْمُهُ لَا يَمْضِي لاسِيَّمَا قُضَاتُنَا إِذْ قَيدُوا * بِرَاجِحِ الْمَذْهَبِ حِينَ قَلِدُوا وَتَمَّ مَا نَظَمُتُهُ فِي سِلْك * وَالحَمدُ لِلَّهِ خِتَامُ مِسْك
Or if it is more suitable for the time, or if it is clearer in proof. This is when the authentication conflicts, or if there is no explicit text on it originally. So take that which has a preponderance from what you have learned; that is the clearer. And act upon the meaning of narrations that come, as long as it does not contradict a clear established text. And custom in the Shari'ah has consideration; therefore the ruling may be based upon it. And it is not permissible to act upon the weak (hadith), nor to answer with it one who comes asking, except for a person who has a necessity for it, or one who has well-known knowledge. Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a set of concluding rules from the poem on the methodology of mufti. It begins with the rule of preferring a ruling that is more suitable for the time or clearer in proof when authentications conflict or there is no explicit text. The mufti must choose the one with preponderance. Next, he should act upon the implications of narrations as long as they do not contradict an explicit established text. Custom ('urf) is given weight in Shari'ah and rulings may be based on it. Acting on weak hadith is prohibited except for a person with personal necessity or for a well-known scholar (for their own practice), but a judge may not base his judgment on weak hadith; if he does, it is void. This is especially for Hanafi judges who are restricted to the preponderant view of the madhhab. The poem ends with praise to Allah.

Key Terms
مَفْهُومِ رِوَايَاتٍ (mafhūm riwāyāt): The understood meaning derived from transmitted narrations (hadith or reports)
صَرِيحٍ ثَبَنَا (ṣarīḥ thabana): An explicit established text (Quran or mutawatir hadith)
عُرُق (‘urf): Customary practice that has legal consideration in the Shari'ah
صَعِيف (ḍa‘īf): A hadith that does not meet the criteria for authenticity (weak)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mufti must prefer the preponderant opinion, may consider custom, and cannot use weak hadith in fatwa except for personal necessity or a scholar's private practice.

Obligation to Follow the Rajih or Zahir al-Riwayah
Rasm al-mufti rule stating the mufti's obligation to follow the rajih or Zahir al-Riwayah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for a mufti's obligation regarding which opinion to follow in fatwa, and correctly apply the hierarchy: first seek tarjih, then Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
The mufti must follow the preponderant view or, absent tarjih, the Zahir al-Riwayah.

A mufti cannot simply choose any opinion from the madhhab. This rule from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti establishes a clear hierarchy: first, follow the opinion that the scholars of tarjih have weighed as stronger. If no such tarjih exists, the mufti must adhere to the well-known transmissions of Zahir al-Riwayah. This preserves consistency and authority in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sources of authority
Recognize that the rule presents two sources: (1) the rajih (preponderant) opinion determined by scholars of tarjih, and (2) Zahir al-Riwayah (the authoritative transmissions) when tarjih is absent.
Tarjih is done by qualified mujtahids, not by the mufti himself.
2
Apply the hierarchy in a scenario
Given a case with multiple narrations, first check if the scholars of tarjih have declared one as rajih. If yes, that is the view. If not, resort to Zahir al-Riwayah.
The rule creates a default: Zahir al-Riwayah is the fallback unless a stronger view is established.
3
Understand the restriction on the mufti
The mufti is bound to these sources. He cannot issue fatwa based on his own preference or weaker narrations without justification (darura or ihtiyat).
This ensures fatwa consistency within the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعْلَمُ بِأَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ الْاِكْتِفَاءُ بِمَا وَ تَرْجِيْحُهُ عَنْ أَهْلِهِ قَدْ عُلِمَا أَوْ كَانَ ظَاهِرَ الرّوَايَةِ وَلَمْ يُرَجَّحُوا خِلَافَ ذَاكَ فَاعْلَمُ
Know that it is obligatory to suffice with that which its preponderance (tarjih) from its people is known, or (if) it is from Zahir al-Riwayah and they did not preponderate contrary to that, then know.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule from the poetic text 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' by Muhammad Amin ibn 'Abidin. The poet states two scenarios where the mufti must issue fatwa based on a particular view. First, if the scholars of tarjih (those qualified to weigh evidences) have given preponderance to one opinion over others, then it is obligatory (wajib) for the mufti to follow that rajih (preponderant) opinion. Second, if there is no such tarjih from capable scholars, then the mufti must follow the Zahir al-Riwayah—that is, the well-known and authoritative narrations from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The phrase 'they did not preponderate contrary to that' means that if the scholars of tarjih have not declared a different view as stronger, then the Zahir al-Riwayah is the default reference. This rule is foundational for muftis to avoid arbitrariness and to preserve the integrity of the madhhab. The commentary in the text clarifies that 'al-wajib al-iktifa' bima tarjihuhu 'an ahlihi qad 'ulima' means the mufti must act upon what has been made evidently preponderant by the people of tarjih. The term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' refers to the six major works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which constitute the primary source of Hanafi fatwa.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and authoritative narrations from the Hanafi founding imams, primarily the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of weighing evidences to determine which opinion is stronger (rajih) within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mufti finds that the scholars of tarjih have not declared any specific view as preponderant, which source must he follow?
A) His own personal ijtihad
B) The Zahir al-Riwayah
C) The weakest opinion reported in the madhhab
D) The opinion of the later scholars (mutakhkhirin)

Key Takeaway
The mufti is obligated to follow the preponderant opinion (rajih) when known, otherwise the authoritative narrations of Zahir al-Riwayah, preserving madhhab consistency.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
The First Principle: Following the Preponderant Opinion
Explanation of the first principle: obligation to follow the preponderant opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the first principle of fatwa by identifying when an opinion is rajih and stating the obligation to verify it through multiple sources.

Core Idea
The mufti must adopt the preponderant opinion verified by multiple sources, not any single claim.

This lesson introduces the foundational rule for issuing fatwas in the Hanafi school: the mufti must follow the opinion that has been declared preponderant (rajih) by qualified scholars of tarjih. The source text, from the commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', emphasizes that the mufti cannot rely on a single book but must verify through multiple references. Let's work through the reasoning and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Source
First, locate the two verses (9-10) in the Arabic text. Note that the first verse states it is obligatory (wajib) to follow the opinion whose preponderance has been established. The second verse adds an alternative: if the opinion is from Zahir al-Riwayah and no tarjih has favored another, it must also be followed.
The Arabic verb 'عْلَمُ' (i'lam) is an imperative, indicating the ruling is binding.
2
Define Key Terms: Rajih and Tarjih
Understand that 'rajih' means preponderant, and 'tarjih' is the process of weighing opinions. The text specifies that tarjih is performed by 'its people' – the scholars of tarjih, who are qualified mujtahids.
Tarjih criteria include strength of evidence, number of transmitters, and conformity with usul.
3
Analyze the Exception: Zahir al-Riwayah
The second verse introduces an alternative: if an opinion is from Zahir al-Riwayah (the core transmitted texts) and no scholar has preponderated a different view, then that opinion itself is binding, regardless of explicit tarjih.
Zahir al-Riwayah has higher authority; later tarjih can override it only if properly established.
4
Apply the Verification Requirement
The commentary stresses that the mufti must not accept a claim of preponderance from a single book. He must consult multiple reliable sources and confirm the tarjih, because sometimes a marjuh (weaker) opinion is mistakenly labeled rajih.
This ensures the fatwa aligns with the soundest view in the madhhab.
5
Extract the Practical Consequence
The ruling directly impacts the mufti's process: before issuing a fatwa, he must research widely, compare authorities, and settle on the mufta bihi (operative opinion). Failure to do so may lead to issuing a fatwa on a weak or incorrect view.
This principle safeguards the integrity of fatwa in the Hanafi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي
ام
شرح : پہلے مصرع میں علامہ نے اپنے منظو مے کا نام بیان فرمایا ہے کہ
میں نے اس کا نام عقود رسم المفتي “ رکھا ہے ، عقود : جمع ہے "عقد" کی ، ہار۔ مراد منظوم کلام - رسم“ : علامت جس کے ذریعے مسافر راستے کی راہ نمائی پاتا ہے؛ لہذا عقود رسم المفتي “ کا معنی ہوا: فتوی دینے کے سلسلے میں مفتی کی راہ نمائی کرنے والا منظوم کلام ۔ دوسرے مصرع میں اس کی اہمیت وضرورت کو واضح کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ اس منظومے کی ضرورت خود عمل کرنے والے اور دوسروں کو مسئلہ بتانے والے( مفتی) کو یکساں ہے یعنی یہ منظومہ بہت ہی اہم ہے؛ اس لیے کہ یہ ہر ایک کی ضرورت ہے۔
دوسرے شعر میں علامہ نے یہ فرمایا کہ اب تمہیدی گفتگو سے فارغ ہوکر، اللہ پاک کی مدد سے مقصد کو بیان کرنے کے سلسلے کا آغاز کر رہا ہوں۔ راجح قول پر فتوی دینا ضروری ہے
۹
عْلَمُ بِأَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ الْبَاعُ مَا وَ تَرْجِيْحُهُ عَنْ أَهْلِهِ قَدْ عُلِمَا ١٠ أو كَانَ ظَاهِرَ الرّوَايَةِ وَلَمْ يُرَجَحُوا خِلافَ ذَاكَ فَاعْلَمُ أَوْ ترجمه : [9] (فتوی دینے کے سلسلے میں ) یہ بات اچھی طرح سمجھ لیجیے کہ ترجیح دینے کی صلاحیت رکھنے والے ائمہ کی جانب سے جس قول کی ترجیح ہوگئی ہو، اُسی قول کے مطابق فتویٰ دینا ضروری ہے۔ [۱۰] (یا پھر یہ کہ ) وہ قول (جس کے مطابق فتوی دیا جارہا ہو ) ظاہر الروایۃ ہو، نیز علمائے ترجیح نے اُس ظاہر روایہ کے علاوہ قول کو راجح قرار نہ دیا ہو، اسے اچھی طرح سمجھ لیجیے۔
مُلاحظة :” عُلِمَا “ میں الف اشباع کا ہے، اصل ”علم“ ہے، ضرورت شعری کی بنا پر ایسا کیا گیا ہے۔
۴۲
اشباع کہتے ہیں ضمے کو داو، فتے کو الف اور کسرے کو یاء بنادینے کو ۔ شعر کے وزن کی درستگی کے لیے ضرورت پر ایسا کیا جاتا ہے؛ یہ الف اس منظومے میں مجموعی طور پر بارہ مقامات پر آیا ہے۔
تفصیل یہ ہے : شعر/ ۹: (علما ) میں ۔ شعر/ ۱۸: (تقدما ) میں ۔ شعر/ ۳۱: المصححا) اور (وضحا) میں ۔ شعر / ۴۳: ( تعلقا ) میں ۔ شعر/ ۴۸: (الكفرا) میں۔ شعر / ۵۰: (اثبتا) میں شعر ۵۲: ( صححا ) اور ( صرحا ) میں ۔ شعر / ۶۴ : ( الاستحسانا ) اور (بانا ) میں شعر / ۶۸: (ثبتا ) میں۔ اور ایک جگہ شعر / ۳۲: (نراھموا) میں واو استعمال ہوا ہے۔ شرح : علامہ شامی نے ان دو شعر میں فتویٰ نویسی کے تین ضابطے بیان فرمائے ہیں:
پہلا ضابطہ یہ بیان فرمایا کہ فتویٰ دینے ، اسی طرح خود عمل کرنے کے وقت مفتی کے لیے لازم ہے کہ وہ اس قول کو اختیار کرے، جسے علمائے اہل ترجیح نے راجح قرار دیا ہو، غور و فکر اور تحقیق کے بغیر متعد دو مختلف منقول اقوال میں سے کسی پر بھی فتوی دے دینا درست نہیں ؛ بل کہ کسی ایک آدھ کتاب میں، اگر کسی قول کو راجح قرار دیا گیا ہو، تو اُس پر بھی فورا اطمینان کر کے فتویٰ دینا درست نہیں؛ جب تک کہ مفتی متعدد کتابوں کی مراجعت اور تحقیق کے بعد اُس قول کی تصحیح کو یقینی نہ بنالے؛ کیوں کہ بعض مرتبہ ایسا ہوتا ہے کہ کسی کتاب میں کسی مرجوح قول کی تصحیح
Aun al-Mughni fi Hill 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. Commentary: In the first couplet, the author (Allamah) stated the name of his poem: 'I have named it 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti'. 'Uqud is the plural of 'aqd, meaning necklace; intended is the poetic composition. 'Rasm' is a sign by which a traveler finds guidance on the path; so 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' means: a poetic composition that guides the mufti in the matter of giving fatwa. In the second couplet, clarifying its importance and necessity, he said that the need for this poem is equal for the one who acts and the one who tells others (the mufti), meaning this poem is very important; because it is needed by everyone. In the second verse, Allamah said: Now, having finished the introductory speech, with the help of Allah Almighty, I am beginning the series of stating the purpose. It is necessary to give fatwa according to the preponderant (rajih) opinion. Verse 9: 'Know that it is obligatory to follow that which its preponderance from its people has been known.' Verse 10: 'Or it was Zahir al-Riwayah and they (the scholars of tarjih) did not preponderate other than that, so know [that].' Translation: [9] Understand well that it is necessary to give fatwa according to the opinion that has been preponderated by the Imams who are capable of tarjih. [10] Or that the opinion is Zahir al-Riwayah, and the scholars of tarjih have not preponderated an opinion other than that Zahir al-Riwayah, understand this well. Observation: The alif in 'عُلِمَا' is an alif ishba' (prolongation); the original is 'علم', and this is done due to poetic necessity. Ishba' is called making a dammah into a waw, a fatha into an alif, and a kasrah into a ya. This is done for poetic meter. This alif occurs in twelve places in this poem. Details: Verse 9: (علما); Verse 18: (تقدما); Verse 31: (المصححا) and (وضحا); Verse 43: (تعلقا); Verse 48: (الكفرا); Verse 50: (اثبتا); Verse 52: (صححا) and (صرحا); Verse 64: (الاستحسانا) and (بانا); Verse 68: (ثبتا); and one place Verse 32: (نراھموا) where waw is used. Commentary: Allamah Shami stated three principles of fatwa-writing in these two verses: The first principle: It is obligatory for the mufti, when giving fatwa and also when acting himself, to adopt the opinion that has been declared preponderant by the scholars of tarjih. It is not correct to give fatwa on any of the two different transmitted opinions without reflection and research; rather, it is also not correct to immediately give fatwa based on an opinion that has been declared preponderant in one or two books, until the mufti confirms its correctness after consulting and researching multiple books; because sometimes it happens that a weak (marjuh) opinion is given preponderance in some books.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening verses of the poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', explaining the first principle of fatwa. The author first explains the title: 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' is a poetic guide for the mufti in issuing fatwas. The poem is essential for both the mufti and the layperson. Then the two verses (9-10) are presented. Verse 9 states that it is obligatory to follow the opinion whose preponderance has been established by the 'people of tarjih' (scholars of weighting). Verse 10 adds that if the opinion is Zahir al-Riwaya (the well-known transmitted opinion) and no scholar of tarjih has preponderated another opinion, then that too must be followed. The commentator then discusses the technical term 'alif ishba' used for poetic meter, listing its occurrences in the poem. Finally, the commentary explains that Imam Shami (the commentator of the poem) derived three principles from these verses. The first principle, detailed here, requires the mufti to adopt the opinion that has been declared rajih by the scholars of tarjih. The mufti must not rely on a single book; he must verify the correctness of a preponderant opinion by consulting multiple sources, because sometimes a marjuh (weaker) opinion is mistakenly presented as rajih in some books.

Key Terms
راجح (raajih): The preponderant opinion among the existing transmitted opinions; the one given preference by scholars of tarjih.
ظاهر الرواية (zaahir al-riwaayah): The well-known and established transmitted opinions from the six major books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah).
ترجیح (tarjeeh): The process of weighing different legal opinions to determine which is preponderant (rajih), based on evidence and criteria.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first principle explained in the passage, what must a mufti do before giving a fatwa based on an opinion that is claimed to be rajih in a single book?
A) He can give fatwa immediately if the book is famous.
B) He must verify the correctness of that opinion by consulting multiple books and researching.
C) He must follow the opinion of his teacher regardless of books.
D) He should only rely on the opinion of the first scholar he finds.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must follow the preponderant (rajih) opinion after verifying it through multiple authoritative sources.
