Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Default Preference of Zahir al-Riwayah and Its Exception
Rules of fatwa selection between Zahir and non-Zahir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a mufti must apply Zahir al-Riwayah and when he must adopt a non-Zahir al-Riwayah position based on explicit direction from madhhab scholars.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the default for fatwa, except when scholars explicitly adopt a non-Zahir ruling due to an illah.

In the Hanafi madhhab, fatwa selection follows a structured hierarchy. The primary default is Zahir al-Riwayah—the established transmission from Imam Muhammad's six books. However, this default can be overridden when later scholars explicitly direct the mufti to adopt a non-Zahir position based on a valid cause. This lesson will walk through the two key rules from this passage, enabling you to apply them in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
Recognize that Zahir al-Riwayah itself necessitates preference (ظاہر الروایہ خود بہ خود ترجیح کی مقتضی ہوتی ہے). This means in the absence of an explicit override, the mufti must give fatwa on the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
The default applies to all chapters of fiqh.
2
Apply the default to a concrete case
Consider the talaq example: husband says 'طلقِي نَفْسَكِ', wife responds 'أَبَنْتُ نَفْسِي'. On Zahir al-Riwayah, one revocable divorce occurs. The mufti must give this ruling unless an explicit override exists.
3
Recognize the exception (third rule)
When scholars of the madhhab explicitly state to leave Zahir al-Riwayah and adopt a non-Zahir ruling due to an illah, the mufti is obligated to follow that direction. This is not optional.
The 'illah must be valid; the scholars' consensus (or established practice) is sufficient.
4
Apply the exception to a case
Examine the janaza example: a child born with incomplete creation. Zahir al-Riwayah says no ghusl, but later scholars adopted non-Zahir that ghusl is required. Since they explicitly directed this, the mufti must give fatwa on the non-Zahir position.
The mufti cannot revert to Zahir al-Riwayah once the override is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظاہر الروایہ خود بہ خود ترجیح کی مقتضی ہوتی ہے۔

ظاہر الروایۃ پر فتوے کی مثال
اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا: "طلقِي نَفْسَكِ " ( تو اپنے آپ کو طلاق دے لے ) بیوی نے جواب میں کہا: ” أَبَنْتُ نَفْسِي “ ( میں نے اپنے آپ کو طلاق بائن دے لی) تو ظاہر الروایہ یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں اُس خاتون پر ایک طلاق رجعی واقع ہو جائے گی ، جب کہ امام صاحب کا ایک قول غیر ظاہر الروایۃ میں یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی، یہاں فتویٰ
ظاہر الروایہ پر ہے کہ اس صورت میں طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔
مسئلے کی مکمل تفصیلات اور دلائل کے لیے دیکھئے: (هدایة، الطلاق، تفویض الطلاق، فصل في المشية : ٣٦٠/٢-٣٦١)

غیر ظاہر الروایۃ پر فتوی
تیسر ا ضابطہ علامہ نے یہ بیان فرمایا کہ اگر علمائے مذہب نے کسی علت کی بنیاد پر ظاہر الروایہ کو چھوڑ کر، غیر ظاہر الروایہ پر فتویٰ دینے کی صراحت کی ہو، تو ایسی صورت میں مفتی مقلد پر لازم ہے کہ وہ علمائے مذہب کی پیروی کرتے ہوئے غیر ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق فتوی دے۔

غیر ظاہر الروایۃ پر فتوے کی مثال
غیر مستین الخلقت بچے کے متعلق ظاہر الروایۃ یہ ہے کہ جو بچہ غیر تام الخلقت ایسا بچہ کہ پیدائش کے وقت، جس کے بعض اعضاء بنے ہوئے ہوں اور بعض بنے ہوئے نہ ہوں ) پیدا ہو، تو اُسے غسل کے بغیر ہی کسی کپڑے میں لپیٹ کر دفن کر دیا جائے گا مگر غیر ظاہر الروایۃ میں ہے کہ اُسے غسل دیا جائے گا اور اُسے ہی مفتی بہ قرا ردیا گیا ہے لہذا جب غیر ظاہر الروایۃ پر فتوے کی صراحت آگئی ، تو اب مفتی اسی کے مطابق فتوی دے گا؛ اس کے لیے جائز نہیں کہ اس صراحت کے باوجود بھی ، وہ ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق ہی فتوی دے۔
Zahir al-Riwayah itself necessitates preference by itself.

Example of fatwa on Zahir al-Riwayah:
If a man said to his wife: 'Divorce yourself (طلقِي نَفْسَكِ)', and the wife responded: 'I have given myself a irrevocable divorce (أَبَنْتُ نَفْسِي)', then in Zahir al-Riwayah, in this case one revocable divorce will occur, while Imam (Abu Hanifa) has a non-Zahir al-Riwayah saying that no divorce occurs. Here the fatwa is on Zahir al-Riwayah that divorce occurs.
For full details and proofs see: (Hidayah, Talaq, Tafwid al-Talaq, Fasl fi al-Mashiyyah: 2/360-361)

Fatwa on non-Zahir al-Riwayah:
The third rule: the 'Allamah stated that if the scholars of the madhhab have explicitly stated to leave Zahir al-Riwayah and give fatwa on non-Zahir al-Riwayah due to some cause ('illah), then in such a case the muqallid mufti is obligated to follow the scholars of the madhhab and give fatwa according to non-Zahir al-Riwayah.

Example of fatwa on non-Zahir al-Riwayah:
Regarding a child that is not fully formed (ghayr tamm al-khilqah): in Zahir al-Riwayah, such a child is wrapped in cloth and buried without washing, but in non-Zahir al-Riwayah, he is given a bath (ghusl), and that is adopted as mufta bih. Therefore, when the explicit instruction to give fatwa on non-Zahir al-Riwayah has come, the mufti will give fatwa accordingly; it is not permissible for him to give fatwa according to Zahir al-Riwayah despite this explicitness.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage from Aun Ul Mughni presents two interrelated rules from the methodology of ifta in the Hanafi madhhab. The first rule establishes that Zahir al-Riwayah (the well-known transmission from Imam Muhammad's six books) automatically has preference when there is no explicit tarjih by later scholars. The example given is a talaq case: when a husband delegates divorce and the wife responds with an expression of irrevocability, Zahir al-Riwayah rules that one revocable divorce occurs, and this is the fatwa despite an alternative transmission. The second rule (the third dabit) states that if the scholars of the madhhab have explicitly directed to leave Zahir al-Riwayah for a non-Zahir al-Riwayah position on the basis of a valid cause (illah), then the mufti must follow that direction. The example is a newborn with incomplete creation: Zahir al-Riwayah says no washing, but non-Zahir al-Riwayah requires washing, and the later scholars have adopted that, so the mufti must give fatwa accordingly. The passage emphasizes that the mufti is bound by the explicit guidance of the madhhab's authorities, not his own preference.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایۃ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known, established transmission from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Mabsut, Jami' Saghir, Jami' Kabir, Ziyadat, Siyar Saghir, Siyar Kabir).
غیر ظاہر الروایۃ (Ghayr Zahir al-Riwayah): Transmissions that are not from the six core books, including opinions from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, or Muhammad al-Shaybani recorded in other works (Nawadir, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a mufti have to give fatwa according to non-Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) Whenever he personally finds it stronger
B) Only when later scholars explicitly direct to do so due to an illah
C) Never; Zahir al-Riwayah is always binding
D) Only in cases of talaq and janaza

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul al-ifta, Zahir al-Riwayah is the default, but explicit direction by later scholars to adopt a non-Zahir position due to a valid cause is binding on the mufti.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Zahir al-Riwayah: The Foundation of Hanafi Fatwa
Defines Zahir al-Riwayah and lists the six foundational Hanafi books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Zahir al-Riwayah, identify its six books, and explain their authority in Hanafi ifta.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the backbone of Hanafi fatwa: six tawatur-transmitted books by Imam Muhammad.

This lesson defines the term Zahir al-Riwayah and lists its six foundational books. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for any mufti to know which narrations are most authoritative and how to navigate between different layers of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept
Zahir al-Riwayah refers to narrations transmitted by tawatur (massively widespread chains) in Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books. These are the most authoritative sources in the Hanafi school.
These are distinct from later or unilateral narrations (ghayr al-riwayah).
2
Identify the six books
Memorize the six works: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut.
They are also called 'al-usul' (the principles) because they form the foundation of the madhhab.
3
Recognize the transmission strength
These books are transmitted with strong chains via tawatur, giving them supreme authority. This is why they are given preference in fatwa.
Other narrations (nawadir) are not transmitted with this level of certainty.
4
Distinguish from ghayr al-riwayah
If a ruling from ghayr al-riwayah is explicitly adopted for fatwa by later authorities, it can override the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
This exception is only valid when clearly indicated by ahl al-tarjih.
5
Understand the role of tarjih
Only qualified scholars (ahl al-tarjih, fifth class of Hanafi jurists) can prefer one narration over another. Their tarjih is authoritative.
Examples: Imam al-Quduri, Sahib al-Hidayah, Ibn al-Humam, etc.

Source Text

ہوئے نہ ہوں ) پیدا ہو، تو اُسے غسل کے بغیر ہی کسی کپڑے میں لپیٹ کر دفن کر دیا جائے گا مگر غیر ظاہر الروایۃ میں ہے کہ اُسے غسل دیا جائے گا اور اُسے ہی مفتی بہ قرا ردیا گیا ہے لہذا جب غیر ظاہر الروایۃ پر فتوے کی صراحت آگئی ، تو اب مفتی اسی کے مطابق فتوی دے گا؛ اس کے لیے جائز نہیں کہ اس صراحت کے باوجود بھی ، وہ ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق ہی فتوی دے۔
ہر کسی کی ترجیح کا اعتبار نہیں
یہاں پہلے شعر کے دوسرے مصرعے میں علمائے اہل ترجیح کا تذکرہ آیا ہے، جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کسی بھی قول کا رائج ہونا، اُس وقت تسلیم کیا جائے گا، جب اُسے ایسے علماء نے راجح قرار دیا ہو ، جن کے اندر مختلف اقوال میں ترجیح قائم کرنے کی ، کی صلاحیت ہو، جیسے: امام قدوری ، صاحب ہدایہ، علامہ ابن ہمام ، امام علی الرازی وغیرہ لہذا علی الاطلاق کسی کی بھی ترجیح کا اعتبار نہیں ہو گا۔
شرح میں اِس مناسبت سے علامہ ابن کمال پاشا کے حوالے سے حضرات فقہاء کے سات طبقات بیان کیے گئے ہیں، ان میں اہل ترجیح کا پانچواں طبقہ ہے۔ حضرات فقہاء کے طبقات کی اس تقسیم کو بہت پسند کیا گیا ہے؛ البتہ ان کی جو مثالیں بیان کی گئی ہیں، ان سے اختلاف کیا گیا ہے، شرح میں وضاحت موجود ہے۔
مُلاحظة : ”ظاہر الروایة " ان مسائل کو کہا جاتا ہے، جو امام محمد اے کی کتب سته مبسوط، زیادات، جامع صغیر، جامع کبیر، سیر صغیر سیر کبیر میں مذکور ہیں، ان کتابوں کا تذکرہ آگے شعر : ۱۱ تا ۱۴ میں آرہا ہے۔
وَكُتُبُ ظَاهِرِ الرِّوَايَاتِ أَتَتْ * سِتّا، وَبِالْأُصُولِ أَيضاً سُمِّيَتْ ۱۲ صَنَّفَهَا مُحَمَّدُنِ الشَّيْبَانِيِّ * حَرَّرَ فِيهَا الْمَذْهَبَ النُّعْمَانِي ۱۳ الْجَامِعُ الصَّغِيرُ وَالْكَبِيرُ * وَالسّيرُ الكَبِيرُ وَالصَّغِير ثُمَّ الزِّيَادَاتُ مَعَ الْمُبْسُوط * تَوَاتَرَتْ بِالسَّنَدِ الْمَضْبُوط ترجمة [11] اور ظاہر الروایات کتابیں ( تصنیف ہو کر ) چھ آئی ہیں، ان کا دوسرا نام اصول بھی ہے۔
[۱۲] ( یہ سب امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کی تصنیف کردہ ہیں، جن میں اُنھوں نے امام صاحب کے مذہب کو شان دار طریقے سے بیان کیا ہے۔ (۱۳) ( وہ چھ کتابیں یہ ہیں: ) جامع صغیر، جامع کبیر، مسیر کبیر، سیر صغیر [۱۴] پھر زیادات اور مبسوط؛ ( یہ سب) مضبوط سند کے ساتھ بہ طریق تواتر مروی ہیں۔
وضاحت : ظاهر الرواية، مرکب اضافی ہے، مگر در حقیقت یہ مرکب توصیفی ہے، "أي رواية ظاهرة "کلام میں روانی اور آسانی کے پیش نظر ترتیب بدل دی گئی ہے۔ شرح : امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کی یہ وہ چھ کتابیں ہیں، جن کی روایت کو تو اتر یا شہرت کے ساتھ منقول ہونے کی وجہ سے ” ظاہر الروایہ کہا جاتا ہے، اور چوں کہ امام محمد کی یہ چھ کتابیں فقہ حنفی کی اساس و بنیاد ہیں ؛ اس لیے انھیں ” اصول بھی
(If a child is born dead) he will be wrapped in cloth and buried without bath, but in ghayr zahir al-riwayah it is said that he should be given a bath and that is the relied-upon fatwa. Therefore, when the fatwa explicitly states ghayr zahir al-riwayah, the mufti will give fatwa accordingly; it is not permissible for him to give fatwa according to zahir al-riwayah despite this explicit statement. Not everyone's tarjih is accepted. Here, in the second hemistich of the first verse, mention is made of the scholars of tarjih. This means that any saying will be considered current only when it has been deemed rajih by scholars who have the capability to establish preference among different sayings, such as Imam Quduri, Sahib al-Hidayah, Allamah Ibn Humam, Imam Ali al-Razi, etc. Therefore, absolutely no one's tarjih will be accepted. In the commentary, on this occasion, seven classes of jurists are mentioned from Allamah Ibn Kamal Pasha; among them the fifth class is the people of tarjih. This division of the classes of jurists is much appreciated; however, there is disagreement with the examples given, as clarified in the commentary. Note: "Zahir al-Riwayah" refers to those issues that are mentioned in Imam Muhammad's six books: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir. Their mention comes ahead in verses 11-14. And the books of the zahir al-riwayat came as six, and they are also called usul. [12] They are all authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; in them he refined the Nu'mani madhhab. [13] They are: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, then al-Ziyadat and al-Mabsut; they have been transmitted with a strong chain by tawatur. Translation [11]: And the books of the zahir al-riwayat came as six, and they are also called usul. [12] These are all authored by Imam Muhammad, in which he explained the Imam's madhhab in a brilliant manner. [13] The six books are: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, then al-Ziyadat and al-Mabsut; all transmitted with strong chain by tawatur. Explanation: Zahir al-Riwayah is an idaafi compound, but actually it is a descriptive compound, meaning "apparent narration"; the order was changed for fluency. Commentary: These six books of Imam Muhammad are called Zahir al-Riwayah because their narration is transmitted by tawatur and fame, and because these six books are the foundation of Hanafi fiqh, they are also called usul.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion on the concept of Zahir al-Riwayah and the authority of different narrations in the Hanafi madhhab. It begins by presenting a ruling from ghayr zahir al-riwayah (unilateral narration) that a stillborn child should be washed, and then states that when such a ruling is explicitly adopted for fatwa, the mufti must give fatwa according to it, even if it contradicts zahir al-riwayah. This illustrates that later authorities can override earlier widespread narrations under certain conditions. Next, the text addresses whose tarjih (preference) is accepted: only qualified scholars like Imam Quduri, Sahib al-Hidayah, Ibn al-Humam, and Ali al-Razi. Their preferences are weighty, but not everyone's. Then the seven classes (tabaqat) of Hanafi jurists are mentioned, with the fifth class being the ahl al-tarjih. Finally, the passage defines Zahir al-Riwayah: it is the body of rulings found in Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books, which are al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. These are called 'usul' (principles) because they form the foundation of the madhhab. They are transmitted by tawatur (massively widespread chains), giving them the highest authority. This lesson is essential for a mufti to understand the hierarchy of sources and which narrations take precedence.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and widely transmitted narrations found in Imam Muhammad's six books, considered the foundational sources of the Hanafi school.
كتب ستة (Kutub Sittah): The six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut.
أصول (Usul): Another name for the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, meaning they are the principles and foundations of the Hanafi madhhab.
ترجیح (Tarjih): The process of preferring one narration or opinion over another by qualified scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Al-Sharh al-Kabir
D) Al-Siyar al-Kabir

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-Riwayah is the authoritative foundation of Hanafi fiqh, transmitted by tawatur in Imam Muhammad's six books.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
The Six Books of Zahir al-Riwayah and Their Hierarchy
Poetic matn and commentary defining the six books and the fatwa hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah and apply the hierarchy of sources in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the primary source for Hanafi fatwa; only when later scholars explicitly adopt another does it take precedence.

This lesson introduces the six foundational books of the Hanafi school, known as Zahir al-Riwayah. You will learn their names, their authoritative status, and the strict order a mufti must follow when issuing fatwas. Understanding this hierarchy is essential to correctly navigating the Hanafi legal tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Six Books
From the poetic matn, list the six books authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut.
These are called the books of Zahir al-Riwayah and also Usul.
2
Understand the Meaning of 'Zahir al-Riwayah'
Recognize that 'Zahir al-Riwayah' means 'clear/well-known transmission' – these books are transmitted with tawatur (conclusive) or widespread acceptance, making them the most authentic source.
This is why they are given priority.
3
Recognize the Three-Tier Hierarchy
The text establishes a strict order: (1) Zahir al-Riwayah, (2) Nawadir al-Riwayah (rare transmissions), and (3) later Fatawa and Waqi'at (contemporary rulings).
This order must be followed in issuing fatwas.
4
Apply the Hierarchy to a Scenario
Given a conflict between Zahir and Nawadir, state that Zahir prevails unless later mashayikh have explicitly adopted the Nawadir ruling as mufta bihi.
The exception is crucial: the hierarchy is strict but can be overridden by scholarly consensus (ijma' of later jurists).
5
Identify the Exception
If later mashayikh have explicitly given fatwa contrary to Zahir based on Nawadir or Fatawa, then that becomes the operative ruling (mufta bihi).
This exception preserves flexibility while maintaining overall consistency.

And the books of Zahir al-Riwayah came as six, and they are also called the principles. 12 They were authored by Muhammad al-Shaybani; he refined in them the Nu'mani school. 13 Al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir and al-Saghir, then al-Ziyadat with al-Mabsut, they were transmitted with tawatur and reliable chain. Translation [11] And the books of Zahir al-Riwayah came as six, and they are also called Usul. [12] (All these are authored by Imam Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in which he expounded the school of Imam Abu Hanifa in a splendid manner.) [13] (Those six books are:) Al-Jami' al-Saghir, Al-Jami' al-Kabir, Al-Siyar al-Kabir, Al-Siyar al-Saghir, [14] then al-Ziyadat and al-Mabsut; (all these) are transmitted with a strong chain by way of tawatur. Explanation: 'Zahir al-Riwayah' is a possessive construction, but in reality it is a descriptive construction: 'i.e., a clear narration'. The order was changed for fluency and ease in speech. Commentary: These are the six books of Imam Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, whose transmission is called 'Zahir al-Riwayah' due to its being transmitted with tawatur or widespread acceptance, and because these six books of Imam Muhammad are the foundation and basis of Hanafi fiqh, they are also called 'Usul'. Among the Hanafis, the order of issues by degree is as follows: (1) Zahir al-Riwayah. (2) Nawadir al-Riwayah. (3) Fatawa and Waqi'at. Exactly this order is to be observed in issuing fatwas: first, a fatwa is given according to Zahir al-Riwayah (as has passed), second according to Nawadir al-Riwayah, and in the matter of giving fatwa, the third and final degree is that of Fatawa and Waqi'at. In case of conflict, Zahir al-Riwayah is given preference. Yes, if the mashayikh have explicitly given fatwa contrary to Zahir al-Riwayah based on Nawadir or Fatawa, then those will be current. Allamah Shami, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, mentioned Zahir al-Riwayah here on this account. The mention of 'Masa'il al-Nawadir' and 'Masa'il al-Nawazil' is in upcoming verses. The detailed introduction of all three types of books has been presented by Allamah in 'Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', so it may be seen there. For further ease, the translation of Hadrat al-Ustadh Hadrat Aqdas Maulana Mufti Saeed Ahmad Palanpuri (may Allah have mercy on him) 'How do you give fatwa?' and the book of Hadrat Maulana Mufti Syed Muhammad Salman Mansurpuri 'Guiding Principles of Fatwa Writing' may also be consulted; with explanation, the introduction of these books is to be found there.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
The passage first presents a poetic matn describing the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. These are six books authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. The term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' indicates that their transmission is well-known and authentic, mutawatir. The commentary clarifies that these books are the foundational sources (Usul) of the Hanafi school. The passage then establishes a strict hierarchy for muftis: (1) Zahir al-Riwayah, (2) Nawadir al-Riwayah (rare transmissions), and (3) later Fatawa and Waqi'at (contemporary rulings). In fatwa, precedence is given to Zahir al-Riwayah, unless later mashayikh have explicitly adopted a ruling from Nawadir or Fatawa, in which case that becomes the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position. This rule ensures consistency and authority in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایۃ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six well-known books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani whose transmission is mutawatir or widely accepted; they are the primary source for fatwa in the Hanafi school.
نادر الروایۃ (Nawadir al-Riwayah): Rare transmissions not included in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah; considered secondary evidence.
فتاویٰ (Fatawa): Later collections of legal rulings issued by Hanafi muftis after the time of Imam Muhammad; includes Waqi'at (contemporary cases).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy prioritizes Zahir al-Riwayah, then Nawadir, then later Fatawa, ensuring consistency and authority.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Three-Tier Hierarchy of Hanafi Fatwa Sources
Hierarchy and conflict resolution rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three-tier hierarchy of Hanafi fatwa sources, apply the rule of precedence, and identify the exception when later scholars' adoption changes the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Fatwa must follow Zahir al-Riwayah first; only if later scholars explicitly adopt a rare or new ruling does it override.

This lesson introduces the fundamental hierarchy that governs how a Hanafi mufti selects the authoritative source for his fatwa. Without this structure, fatwa practice would be arbitrary. The passage from Aun al-Mughni lays out the three ranks and the critical rule of preference with an important exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three tiers
List the three categories in order: Zahir al-Riwayah, Nadir al-Riwayah (Nawadir), and Fatawa/Waqiat (Nawazil).
These correspond to primary, secondary, and tertiary sources.
2
Determine the default order for issuing fatwa
The mufti must first seek the ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah. If found, he gives fatwa accordingly. Only if no ruling is found there does he move to Nawadir, then to Nawazil.
This is the default sequence.
3
Apply the conflict rule
When sources from different tiers conflict, Zahir al-Riwayah takes precedence unless an exception applies.
4
Note the exception
If the later authoritative scholars (Mashayikh) have explicitly adopted a ruling from the lower tiers (Nawadir or Nawazil) and given fatwa on it, then that ruling becomes the operative fatwa, overriding the default preference.
This shows the dynamic nature of fatwa practice.

(۱) ظاہر الروایہ۔
(۲) نادر الروایہ۔
(۳) فتاوی اور واقعات۔
بالکل یہی ترتیب فتوی دینے میں بھی ملحوظ رہے گی، سب سے پہلے "ظاہر الروایہ" کے مطابق فتویٰ دیا جائے گا (جیسا کہ گزرا) دوسرے درجے میں "نادر الروایۃ" اور فتویٰ دینے کے سلسلے میں تیسرا اور آخری درجہ فتاوی اور واقعات کا ہوگا۔ تعارض کے وقت "ظاہر الروایہ" کو ترجیح ہوگی: ہاں! اگر مشائخ نے "ظاہر الروایہ" سے ہٹ کر، نوادر یا فتاویٰ وغیرہ پر فتوے کی صراحت کی ہو، تو پھر وہی رائج ہوں گے، علامہ شامی نے اسی مناسبت سے یہاں ظاہر الروایہ کا تذکرہ کیا ہے۔ مسائل النوادر اور مسائل النوازل کا تذکرہ آئندہ اشعار میں ہے،

تینوں طرح کی کتابوں کا تفصیلی تعارف شرح عقود رسم المفتی کے اندر علامہ نے پیش فرمایا ہے، وہاں دیکھ لیا جائے، مزید آسانی کے لیے حضرت الاستاذ حضرت اقدس مولانا مفتی سعید احمد صاحب پالن پوری کا ترجمہ: "آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟" اور حضرت مولانا مفتی سید محمد سلمان صاحب منصور پوری کی کتاب: "فتوی نویسی کے رہنما اصول" بھی دیکھے جاسکتے ہیں، وضاحت کے ساتھ اِن کتابوں کا تعارف وہاں موجود ہے۔

مسائل النوادر کی وضاحت
كذا له مسائل النوادر * إسنادها في الكتب غير ظاهر
ترجمہ: [۱۵] اسی طرح امام محمد کی تصانیف میں مسائل النوادر بھی ہیں، جن کی سندیں کتابوں میں ظاہر نہیں (مشہور نہیں)۔
شرح: مذکورہ چھ کتابوں کے علاوہ امام محمد کی اور بھی فقہی تصنیفات ہیں مگر ان کی روایات معروف و مشہور نہیں، جس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اسے کوئی ایک ہی شاگرد روایت کرتا ہے، ان کتابوں کو کتب نوادر اور اُن کے مسائل کو "مسائل النوادر" کہا جاتا ہے، اسی طرح امام محمد کے علاوہ امام صاحب کے دوسرے تلامذہ کی تصنیفات بھی کتب نوادر کہلاتی ہیں۔

مسائل النوازل کی وضاحت
وبعدها مسائل النوازل * خرجها الأشياخ بالدلائل
ترجمة: [۱۶] نوادر کے بعد مسائل النوازل کا درجہ ہے، جن (مسائل نوازل) کی مشایخ نے دلائل سے تخریج کی ہے۔
شرح: مسائل النوازل ایسے جدید مسائل ہیں، جو مجتہدین کے زمانے کے گذر جانے کے بعد پیش آئے اور مجتہدین سے صراحتًا اُن کا کوئی حکم مروی نہیں، بعد کے اکابر نے متقدمین کے اصول و فروع کو سامنے رکھ کر ان کا حکم بیان کیا ہے، اس طرح کے مسائل کی جامع کتاب کو "کتاب النوازل" کہا جاتا ہے۔
The arrangement of issues according to rank among the Hanafis is: (1) Zahir al-Riwayah. (2) Nadir al-Riwayah. (3) Fatawa and Waqiat. Exactly this order will be observed in issuing fatwas: first, a fatwa will be given according to Zahir al-Riwayah (as has passed); second, according to Nadir al-Riwayah; and third and final rank in issuing fatwas is that of Fatawa and Waqiat. In case of conflict, Zahir al-Riwayah will be given preference. Yes! If the Mashayikh have explicitly indicated fatwa according to Nawadir or Fatawa, departing from Zahir al-Riwayah, then those will be prevalent. Allama Shami mentioned Zahir al-Riwayah here on this basis. The mention of Masail al-Nawadir and Masail al-Nawazil will come in the following verses.

A detailed introduction of all three types of books has been presented by Allama in Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti; it can be seen there. For further ease, the translation of Hadrat al-Ustadh Hadrat Aqdas Maulana Mufti Saeed Ahmad Sahib Palanpuri's "Aap Fatwa Kaise Dein?" and the book of Hadrat Maulana Mufti Sayyid Muhammad Salman Sahib Mansurpuri, "Fatwa Naveesi Ke Rehnuma Usool", can also be consulted; an introduction of these books with clarity is available there.

Clarification of Masail al-Nawadir:
[15] Likewise, among the works of Imam Muhammad there are also Masail al-Nawadir, whose chains of transmission are not apparent (not famous) in the books.
Commentary: Apart from the mentioned six books, Imam Muhammad also has other juristic works, but their narrations are not well-known and famous, because only a single student narrates from him. These books are called Kutub al-Nawadir and their issues are called Masail al-Nawadir. Similarly, besides Imam Muhammad, the works of other students of Imam Abu Hanifa are also called Kutub al-Nawadir.

Clarification of Masail al-Nawazil:
[16] After the Nawadir comes the rank of Masail al-Nawazil, which the Mashayikh have derived with evidences.
Commentary: Masail al-Nawazil are those new issues that occurred after the era of the Mujtahidun passed, and no explicit ruling is narrated from the Mujtahidun regarding them. Later scholars, keeping in view the principles and subsidiary issues of the early scholars, have expressed their ruling. A comprehensive book of such issues is called Kitab al-Nawazil.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage from Aun al-Mughni, a sharh of Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, explains the hierarchical ranking of sources used by Hanafi muftis when issuing fatwas. The author begins by stating the three-tier hierarchy: first and foremost is Zahir al-Riwayah (the well-known and authoritative transmissions from the founding Imams, primarily the six works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani), second is Nadir al-Riwayah (rare or less well-known transmissions, also known as Nawadir), and third is Fatawa and Waqiat (later juristic opinions and real-case rulings, often called Nawazil).

The key rule is that in case of conflict among these sources, Zahir al-Riwayah takes precedence by default. However, there is an important exception: if the later authoritative scholars (Mashayikh) have explicitly adopted a ruling from the Nawadir or the later Fatawa and have given fatwa accordingly, then that ruling becomes the prevalent practice (mufta bihi). This nuance is crucial because it recognizes the evolution of practice over time even while maintaining the foundational sources as primary.

The passage then proceeds to define the two lower categories through versified couplets (verses 15 and 16) with commentary. Verse 15 explains Masail al-Nawadir: these are issues found in the works of Imam Muhammad that are not part of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah. Their chains of transmission are weak or singular, hence they are not widely known. The commentary clarifies that not only Imam Muhammad's extra works but also the compilations of other direct students of Imam Abu Hanifa fall under this category.

Verse 16 explains Masail al-Nawazil: these are new legal issues that arose after the era of the Mujtahid Imams. Since these issues were not explicitly addressed by the early authorities, later scholars (the Mashayikh) derived their rulings by applying the established principles (usul) and precedent (furu) of the school. A book that compiles such cases is called 'Kitab al-Nawazil'.

This hierarchy teaches the student of iftaa that the mufti must first search for the ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah. If found, he gives fatwa accordingly unless a later scholarly consensus has shifted to another view. If no clear ruling is there, he moves to the Nawadir, and then to the Nawazil. This systematic approach ensures consistency and authenticity in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmissions from the founding Imams, primarily the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat).
نادر الرواية / نوادر (Nadir al-Riwayah / Nawadir): Rare or less-known transmissions, including works of Imam Muhammad beyond the six books and works of other direct students of Imam Abu Hanifa. Their chains are not widely spread.
مسائل النوازل (Masail al-Nawazil): New legal issues that arose after the era of the Mujtahidun, whose rulings were derived by later scholars (Mashayikh) using the established principles of the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in case of conflict between Zahir al-Riwayah and later Fatawa, which source takes precedence by default?
A) Later Fatawa
B) Nawadir
C) Zahir al-Riwayah
D) The view of the ruling authority

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy prioritizes Zahir al-Riwayah, but later scholarly adoption can shift the operative ruling to lower-tier sources.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner

Definitions of Nawadir and Nawazil
Definitions of the lower two source categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Nawadir and Nawazil, distinguish them from Zahir al-Riwayah, and explain their role in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Nawadir are rare transmissions; Nawazil are new cases derived by later scholars using school principles.

Beyond the well-known six books of Imam Muhammad, there are other lesser-known works (Nawadir). And after the early imams, new issues arose that required deduction by later scholars (Nawazil). This lesson clarifies these two categories and their place in the fatwa hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage defines two categories: Masail al-Nawadir and Masail al-Nawazil.
2
Define Masail al-Nawadir
These are issues found in works of Imam Muhammad other than the six Zahir al-Riwayah books, or in works of other direct students of Imam Abu Hanifa. Their chains are not widely transmitted (ghayr zahir).
They are secondary sources.
3
Define Masail al-Nawazil
These are new issues that arose after the era of the Mujtahidun. No explicit ruling from them exists. Later scholars (Mashayikh) derived rulings using the school's principles and subsidiary issues.
They are tertiary sources.
4
Understand their place in the hierarchy
Both come after Zahir al-Riwayah in the default order. Nawadir comes second, Nawazil third. But they can become mufta bihi if explicitly adopted by later Mashayikh.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Hierarchy of Zahir al-Riwayah Books for Fatwa
Explaining the internal hierarchy of Zahir al-Riwayah books for fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy of Zahir al-Riwayah books to resolve conflicts between narrations and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Later authored Zahir al-Riwayah books abrogate earlier ones in case of conflict.

Zahir al-Riwayah is the primary source for Hanafi fatwa. However, since the six books were authored over time, later compositions may refine or supersede earlier rulings. This lesson explains the internal hierarchy: later books like al-Jami' al-Saghir take precedence over earlier ones like al-Mabsut, and al-Siyar al-Kabir is decisive for siyar. Al-Kafi, a compilation, serves as a reliable substitute when the originals are unavailable.

Guided Path
1
List the six books
Identify the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat.
Know their chronological order of composition.
2
Determine chronological order
Establish which book was authored later. The later book takes precedence over the earlier one when a conflict arises.
Al-Jami' al-Saghir came after al-Mabsut; al-Siyar al-Kabir is last.
3
Apply abrogation rule
If a conflict exists between two Zahir al-Riwayah books, the later composition's narration is preponderant (mufta bihi).
This is because the later book abrogates the earlier one, like naskh.
4
Recognize domain specificity
Al-Siyar al-Kabir is the last composition and particularly authoritative for matters of siyar (military expeditions, international law). For other topics, other later books like al-Ziyadat take precedence.
Do not apply al-Siyar al-Kabir's precedence universally.
5
Understand al-Kafi's role
Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is a compilation of the six books. It is a reliable summary but does not replace the original books in the hierarchy. It suffices when the originals are absent.
If a ruling in al-Kafi conflicts with a later original, the later original's ruling is preferred.

شرح : اس شعر میں علامہ نے جامع صغیر کی تصنیف کا نمبر بیان فرمایا ہے؟ چناں چہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مبسوط کے بعد جامع صغیر کی تصنیف ہوئی اور ان باتوں کے بیان سے علامہ کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ جب یہ بات واضح ہو چکی کہ فتوے کی ترتیب میں پہلا درجہ ” ظاہر الروایہ کا ہے، تو یہ بھی سمجھ لیں کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ کبھی ظاہر الروایۃ کی روایات بھی باہم متعارض ہوں، مثلاً: کسی مسئلے میں مبسوط اور جامع صغیر کی روایات میں تعارض ہو جائے ، تو ایسے موقع پر جامع صغیر کی روایت راج ہوگی؟ کیوں کہ وہ بعد کی تصنیف ہے، ناسخ کے درجے میں ہے۔
سیر کبیر آخری تصنیف ہونے کی وجہ سے قابل اعتبار ہے
۱۹ وَاخِرُ السِّتَّةِ تَصْنِيفًا وَرَدُ * السّيرُ الْكَبِيرُ، فَهُوَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ ترجمة : [19] اور چھ کتابوں میں سب سے اخیر میں تصنیف ہونے والی سیر کبیر ہے، اس وجہ سے ( بہ وقت تعارض ) وہی قابل اعتماد ہے۔
تركيب: "آخر الستة مميّز، تصنيفاً، موصوف اپنی صفت " ورد

سے مل کر تمیز میز تمیز سے مل کر مبتدا اور السیر الکبیر " اس کی خبر ہے۔ شرح : اس شعر میں بھی علامہ نے ”جامع صغیر کی طرح ”سیر کبیر" کی تصنیف کا نمبر بیان فرمایا ہے، مقصود یہاں بھی یہی ہے کہ اگر کبھی ظاہر الروایۃ میں میر کے کسی مسئلے میں تعارض ہو جائے، تو "سیر کبیر" کی روایت کا اعتبار ہوگا ، ؟ کیوں کہ وہ آخری تصنیف ہے؛ لہذا اُس کی روایت دوسری کتابوں کی ایسی روایت جس کا تعلق سیر سے ہو، اس کے لیے ناسخ کبھی جائے گی اور سیر کبیر کی ہی روایت قابل اعتماد ہوگی۔
”الكَافِي ظاہر الروایۃ کتابوں کی جامع ہے
۲۰ وَيَجْمَعُ السِّتْ كِتَابُ الْكَافِي * لِلْحَاكِمِ الشَّهِيدِ فَهُوَ الْكَافِي ترجمه : [۲۰] اور حاکم شهید کی "الكافي “امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کی چھوں کتابوں کی جامع ہے لہذا (اب) وہ کافی ہے۔
شرح ماقبل میں چوں کہ کتب ستہ ظاہر الروایہ کا تذکرہ آیا ہے، اس مناسبت سے علامہ نے یہ بیان فرمایا کہ حاکم شہید کی الکافی امام محمد کی کتب ستہ کی جامع ہے، جامع اس طرح ہے کہ حاکم شہید نے امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کی کتب ستہ کو یکجا فرمایا، تکرار کو حذف کیا اور ”الكافي“ کے نام سے کتب ستہ کا خلاصہ و نچوڑ تیار کر دیا، احناف کی فقہی کتابوں میں یہ کتاب بھی نہایت ہی قابل اعتماد ہے، کسی کے پاس اگر امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کی کتب ستہ نہ ہو، اور صرف الکافی" ہو، تو بھی کافی شافی ہے۔
Aun al-Mughni fi Hall Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. The original Mabsut is preferred. Note: The word "giza" appearing in the line relates to line 18; for ease, its translation is combined with the next line. The original phrase "fama fihi 'ala al-asl li-dha taqaddama" is: "fama fihi (al-Jami' al-Saghir) li-dha taqaddama 'ala al-asl". Clarification: the alif in "taqaddama" is an alif of prolongation. Commentary: In this line, the author (Allama) has mentioned the composition number of al-Jami' al-Saghir. Thus he states that al-Jami' al-Saghir was composed after al-Mabsut. By mentioning these things, the author intends that once it is clear that the first rank in the order of fatwa belongs to Zahir al-Riwayah, then also understand that sometimes the narrations of Zahir al-Riwayah may contradict each other. For example, if the narrations of al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir conflict on an issue, then on such occasion the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir will be preponderant because it is the later composition and occupies the position of an abrogator. Al-Siyar al-Kabir, being the last composition, is reliable. 19. And the last of the six in composition came down: al-Siyar al-Kabir, so it is relied upon. Translation: [19] And among the six books, the last to be composed is al-Siyar al-Kabir; for this reason (at the time of conflict) it is reliable. Structure: "Akhir al-sittati" is tamyiz, "tasnifan" is the adjective of the mausuf, combining with tamyiz to form mubtada, and "al-Siyar al-Kabir" is its khabar. Commentary: In this line as well, the author has mentioned the composition number of al-Siyar al-Kabir like al-Jami' al-Saghir. The purpose here is the same: if sometimes in Zahir al-Riwayah there is a conflict on an issue, then the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir will be given weight because it is the last composition; therefore its narration will be considered abrogating for narrations of other books related to Siyar, and only al-Siyar al-Kabir's narration will be reliable. Al-Kafi is a compilation of the Zahir al-Riwayah books. 20. And Kitab al-Kafi, by al-Hakim al-Shahid, encompasses the six, so it is sufficient. Translation: [20] And al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is a compilation of Imam Muhammad's six books; therefore it is now sufficient. Commentary: Since the mention of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah has come in the previous discussion, the author states that al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is a compilation of Imam Muhammad's six books. It is a compilation in that al-Hakim al-Shahid combined the six books of Imam Muhammad, deleted repetitions, and prepared a summary and essence of the six books under the name al-Kafi. Among the Hanafi fiqh books, this book is also extremely reliable. If someone does not have the six books of Imam Muhammad but only has al-Kafi, then it is sufficiently adequate.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule concerning the hierarchy of reliance among the books of Zahir al-Riwayah when their narrations conflict. The commentator explains that although the first source for fatwa is Zahir al-Riwayah, within that category the later authored books take precedence over the earlier ones. For example, al-Jami' al-Saghir was written after al-Mabsut, so if they conflict, the ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir is preponderant because it is later and thus abrogates the earlier. Similarly, al-Siyar al-Kabir is the last of the six books to be composed, so in matters of siyar (military expeditions and international law), its narrations are relied upon. The passage also notes that al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is a compilation of all six books, and it is a reliable substitute if one does not have the original six. The author emphasizes that this rule is about the internal hierarchy of Zahir al-Riwayah, not an external ranking.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat.
الجامع الصغير (Al-Jami' al-Saghir): A book by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, composed after al-Mabsut, covering various fiqh topics.
السير الكبير (Al-Siyar al-Kabir): The last of the six books of Imam Muhammad, dealing with siyar (laws of war and peace), relied upon in case of conflict in that subject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hierarchy of Zahir al-Riwayah, if al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir conflict on a ruling, which book's ruling is given precedence?
A) Al-Mabsut
B) Al-Jami' al-Saghir
C) Al-Kafi
D) Al-Siyar al-Kabir

Key Takeaway
The later authored Zahir al-Riwayah books abrogate earlier ones, with al-Siyar al-Kabir most authoritative for siyar and al-Kafi as a reliable compilation.

Priority of Siraj al-Kabir's Narration
Rule about prioritizing Siraj al-Kabir in conflicting narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of prioritizing Siraj al-Kabir when conflicting narrations on siyar arise and explain the rationale of naskh by later composition.

Core Idea
Siraj al-Kabir overrides earlier Zahir al-Riwayah texts in siyar because it is the last authored book.

This passage addresses a common challenge for a mufti: when two books from Zahir al-Riwayah differ on a point of siyar (military expeditions and international relations), which one should be followed? The rule is clear: Siraj al-Kabir, being the final work of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, acts as an abrogating text. In this lesson, you will learn to apply this hierarchy and understand its basis in Hanafi usul al-ifta.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict
Recognize that the conflicting narrations are both from Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books).
2
Determine the subject
Confirm that the conflict is specifically about a siyar matter (e.g., prisoner exchange, rules of warfare).
The rule applies only to siyar, not to other chapters like ibadat or muamalat.
3
Apply the rule
Give precedence to the narration from Siraj al-Kabir over all other Zahir al-Riwayah books.
This is based on the principle that a later composition abrogates (naskh) earlier ones.
4
Understand the rationale
Siraj al-Kabir is the last book authored by Imam Muhammad, so its rulings supersede earlier narrations in the same subject area.
This is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) for resolving conflicts, not a textual naskh of the Quran or Sunnah.
5
Note the scope
This rule is specific to siyar; for other chapters, different books may take precedence (e.g., Jami' al-Saghir for purity).
Always check the subject matter before applying the hierarchy.

سے مل کر تمیز میز تمیز سے مل کر مبتدا اور السیر الکبیر “ اس کی خبر ہے۔ شرح : اس شعر میں بھی علامہ نے ”جامع صغیر کی طرح ”سیر کبیر" کی تصنیف کا نمبر بیان فرمایا ہے، مقصود یہاں بھی یہی ہے کہ اگر کبھی ظاہر الروایۃ میں میر کے کسی مسئلے میں تعارض ہو جائے، تو "سیر کبیر" کی روایت کا اعتبار ہوگا ، ؟ کیوں کہ وہ آخری تصنیف ہے؛ لہذا اُس کی روایت دوسری کتابوں کی ایسی روایت جس کا تعلق سیر سے ہو، اس کے لیے ناسخ کبھی جائے گی اور سیر کبیر کی ہی روایت قابل اعتماد ہوگی۔
[The text explains that in the poem, the author mentions the number of the composition of Siraj al-Kabir, similar to Jami' al-Saghir. The point is that if there is a conflict in Zahir al-Riwayah regarding a matter of siyar, the narration from Siraj al-Kabir will be given weight because it is the last composition; thus its narration will abrogate other narrations related to siyar, and only the narration of Siraj al-Kabir is reliable.]
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage states a methodological rule for muftis: when there is a contradiction among the books of Zahir al-Riwayah on matters of siyar (military expeditions and international relations), the narration from Siraj al-Kabir (The Great Siyar) is given precedence. The reason is that it was the last of Imam Muhammad's six core books to be written. Just as a later ruling abrogates an earlier one (naskh), the later book takes priority. This rule specifically applies to siyar chapters; for other chapters, different books may take precedence.

Key Terms
سیر کبیر (Siraj al-Kabir): The Great Siyar, one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, dealing with international law and military expeditions.
ظاہر الروایۃ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that form the primary relied-upon texts of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Siraj al-Saghir because it is more concise.
B) Siraj al-Kabir because it is the last book authored by Imam Muhammad.
C) Neither, as both are unreliable.
D) The one that agrees with the majority of other books.

Key Takeaway
When narrations conflict in siyar, rely on Siraj al-Kabir because, as the final work, it abrogates earlier texts.

Al-Kafi as a Reliable Compendium of Zahir al-Riwayah
Describing Al-Kafi as a reliable summary of the six core books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of Al-Kafi in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy and explain why it is considered sufficient for issuing fatawa.

Core Idea
Al-Kafi is a trusted summary of the six core books, sufficient for fatwa even without the originals.

In the Hanafi tradition, the six books of Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah) are the primary sources of fatwa. However, later scholars compiled concise summaries for ease of reference. This passage introduces Al-Kafi by Hakim al-Shahid, which extracts the essential rulings from those six books. Understanding its authority is crucial for a mufti who may not have access to the full set.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source books
Recognize that the six books of Imam Muhammad (e.g., al-Mabsut, al-Jami‘ al-Saghir) are the foundation of Hanafi fatwa.
2
Understand the compilation method
Know that Al-Kafi combines these six books, removes repetitions, and presents a coherent summary.
This makes it a 'sufficient' (kafi) reference.
3
Assess its authority
Realize that Al-Kafi is considered highly reliable in the Hanafi school; a mufti can rely on it even without the originals.
This is a practical rule for fatwa practice.
4
Apply to fatwa hierarchy
Place Al-Kafi within the hierarchy: It is part of the later compilations but directly derived from Zahir al-Riwayah, thus carrying strong authority.
The mufta bihi position is that Al-Kafi suffices when originals are unavailable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكَافِي ظاہر الروایۃ کتابوں کی جامع ہے ۲۰ وَيَجْمَعُ السِّتْ كِتَابُ الْكَافِي * لِلْحَاكِمِ الشَّهِيدِ فَهُوَ الْكَافِي ترجمه : [۲۰] اور حاکم شہید کی "الكافي "امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کی چھوں کتابوں کی جامع ہے لہذا (اب) وہ کافی ہے۔ شرح ماقبل میں چوں کہ کتب ستہ ظاہر الروایہ کا تذکرہ آیا ہے، اس مناسبت سے علامہ نے یہ بیان فرمایا کہ حاکم شہید کی الکافی امام محمد کی کتب ستہ کی جامع ہے، جامع اس طرح ہے کہ حاکم شہید نے امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کی کتب ستہ کو یکجا فرمایا، تکرار کو حذف کیا اور ”الكافي“ کے نام سے کتب ستہ کا خلاصہ و نچوڑ تیار کر دیا، احناف کی فقہی کتابوں میں یہ کتاب بھی نہایت ہی قابل اعتماد ہے، کسی کے پاس اگر امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کی کتب ستہ نہ ہو، اور صرف الکافی" ہو، تو بھی کافی شافی ہے۔
[Al-Kafi is a compilation of the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. 20: And the book Al-Kafi collects the six books, by Hakim al-Shahid, so it is sufficient. Translation: [20] And Hakim al-Shahid's Al-Kafi is a compilation of the six books of Imam Muhammad, so it is sufficient. Commentary: Since the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah were mentioned earlier, the author explains that Hakim al-Shahid's Al-Kafi compiles them by combining Imam Muhammad's six books, removing repetition, and producing a summary and essence. This book is highly reliable; if one does not have access to the six books, Al-Kafi alone suffices.]
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage introduces Al-Kafi by Hakim al-Shahid (d. 334 AH) as a condensed version of Imam Muhammad's six core books. The author states that Al-Kafi collects the six books, eliminates redundancies, and presents the essential rulings. It is considered a reliable source in the Hanafi school, to the extent that a mufti can rely on it even without the original six books. This is a practical rule for fatwa: Al-Kafi is sufficient as a primary reference when the originals are unavailable.

Key Terms
الكافي (Al-Kafi): A book by Hakim al-Shahid that summarizes Imam Muhammad's six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, removing repetitions.
حاكم شهيد (Hakim al-Shahid): Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Marwazi, a Hanafi scholar who compiled Al-Kafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Al-Kafi is a selection from the six books with repetition removed.
C) Al-Kafi includes only narrations from Abu Hanifa.
D) Al-Kafi is a commentary on the six books.

Key Takeaway
Al-Kafi is a reliable summary of the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah and is sufficient for fatwa.

The Authoritative Status of Al-Mabsut in Hanafi Fatwa
Establishing Al-Mabsut as authoritative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that rulings in Al-Mabsut of Sarakhsi are binding and must not be contradicted when issuing fatwa.

Core Idea
Al-Mabsut of Sarakhsi is the binding commentary on Al-Kafi; no fatwa may contradict it.

This lesson establishes the hierarchical authority of Al-Mabsut among Hanafi sources. The passage declares it as the most reliable commentary on Al-Kafi, akin to a sun among stars. Understanding this ranking is crucial for any mufti — it dictates which opinions are operative and which are not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
Recognize that Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is the foundational matn being commented upon.
2
Recognize the commentary hierarchy
Understand that Al-Mabsut of Sarakhsi is declared the strongest commentary, like the sun among others.
3
Understand the binding rule
The passage states: 'no action is taken contrary to it, nor is it deviated from'. This means Al-Mabsut's rulings are authoritative.
4
Note the source of the rule
The commentary quotes Najm al-Din al-Tartusi affirming that any opinion opposing Al-Mabsut is void.
5
Apply in practice
When issuing fatwa, prioritize Al-Mabsut over other commentaries; its opinion is mufta bihi.

مبسوط ” کافی“ کی عمدہ اور قابل اعتماد شرح ہے ۵۲ أَقْوى شُرُوحِهِ الَّذِي كَالشَّمْسِ * مَبْسُوطُ شَمْسِ الْأُمَّةِ السَّرَخُسِي ۲۲ مُعْتَمَدُ النُّقُولِ، لَيْسَ يُعْمَلُ بِخُلْفِهِ ، وَلَيْسَ عَنْهُ يُعْدَلُ ترجمه : [۲۱] شمس الائمہ سرخی صلى الله عليه وسلم کی مبسوط، کافی کی سب سے شان دار شرح ہے، بالکل سورج کی طرح۔ [۲۲] مذاہب کے نقل کرنے میں مبسوط سرخسی قابل اعتماد ہے ؛ (لہذا) اس میں آئے ہوئے قول کے علاوہ قول پر نہ عمل کیا جائے گا، نہ ہی اس ( مبسوط سرخی میں آئے ہوئے قول) سے عدول کیا جائے گا۔ شرح : جب "الكافي" کا تذکرہ آگیا، تو علامہ شامی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یہ وضاحت فرمائی کہ حاکم شہید کی الکافی کی بہت سے علماء نے شرح لکھی ہے، اُن میں سب سے زیادہ بہتر اور حمد و شرح شمس الائمہ سرخی صلى الله عليه وسلم کی مبسوط " ہے۔ علامہ نجم الدین ابراہیم بن علی البغدادی طرطوسی (متوفی : ۷۵۸ھ) فرماتے ہیں کہ جو بات ” مبسوط مرخصی" کے خلاف ہو، اُس پر عمل نہیں کیا جائے گا، اس پر اعتماد کرنا اور اسی کے مطابق فتوی دینا ضروری ہے۔ ( آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟ : ۴۷)
[Al-Mabsut is an excellent and reliable commentary of Al-Kafi. 52: The strongest of its commentaries, like the sun, is Al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. 22: Reliable in transmission; no action is taken contrary to it, nor is it deviated from. Translation: [21] Al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi is the most splendid commentary of Al-Kafi. [22] Al-Mabsut of Sarakhsi is reliable in transmitting madhhab positions; therefore, no action contrary to its stated opinion shall be taken, nor shall one deviate from it. Commentary: When Al-Kafi was mentioned, the author clarifies that many scholars wrote commentaries on it, but the best and most praiseworthy is Al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. Najm al-Din Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Baghdadi al-Tartusi (d. 758 AH) says that no action is taken contrary to Al-Mabsut; it must be relied upon and fatwa given accordingly.]
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage establishes Al-Mabsut by Sarakhsi as the preeminent commentary on Al-Kafi. It is described as the most powerful commentary, like the sun, and is deemed 'reliable in transmission' (mu'tamad al-nuqul). The rule is clear: a mufti must not act contrary to a ruling found in Al-Mabsut, nor deviate from it. The commentary quotes Najm al-Din al-Tartusi affirming that any opinion opposing Al-Mabsut is void. Thus, Al-Mabsut has near-authoritative status in the Hanafi school for fatwa, especially when extracting rulings from Al-Kafi.

Key Terms
مبسوط (Al-Mabsut): The famous commentary by Sarakhsi on Al-Kafi, considered the most authoritative exposition.
شمس الأئمة السرخسي (Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi): The author of Al-Mabsut, a leading Hanafi faqih (d. 483 AH).

Selection of Narrations from Abu Hanifa
A rule about narration selection hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of Imam Muhammad's selection in establishing the Zahir al-Riwayah and distinguish it from narrations selected by other companions.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school's core texts are based on Imam Muhammad's selection of Abu Hanifa's narrations.

When a mufti encounters a legal issue, he must know which narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa carry authoritative weight. This passage introduces the foundational hierarchy: Imam Muhammad's selections constitute the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, while narrations transmitted by other companions like Abu Yusuf and Zufar are part of the nawadir. Understanding this selection process is essential for proper fatwa methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the multiplicity of narrations
Recognize that Abu Hanifa had many narrations (positions) transmitted by different students. This establishes a need for selection.
The text says 'many narrations came from Abu Hanifa' (جاءت روايات).
2
Understand Imam Muhammad's selection
Imam Muhammad selected some of these narrations for inclusion in his six books (Zahir al-Riwayah). These form the primary source for fatwa.
The passage says 'he selected some of them' (اختار منها بعضها).
3
Recognize the role of other companions
The remaining narrations were selected by other senior students (rifaq) like Abu Yusuf and Zufar. Their selections belong to the nawadir category.
The text says 'the rest the other companions selected' (والباقي يختار منه سائر الرفاق).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام صاحب سے بہت سی روایات مشہور ہیں ۲۳ وَاعْلَمُ بِأَنَّ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَهُ * جَاءَتْ رِوَايَاتٌ غَدَتْ مُنِيْفَهُ اخْتَارَ مِنْهَا بَعْضَهَا ، وَالْبَاقِي * يَخْتَارُ مِنْهُ سَائِرُ الرِّفَاقِ ترجمه : [۲۳] جان لو کہ امام ابو حنیفہ رحمہ اللہ سے بہت سی روایات آئی ہیں جو بلند ہیں، ان میں سے بعض روایات کو انہوں نے (امام محمد نے) انتخاب کیا اور باقی کو دوسرے رفقاء (یعنی امام ابو یوسف اور امام زفر وغیرہ) نے انتخاب کیا۔
[Many narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa are famous. 23: And know that from Abu Hanifa came many narrations that are lofty; he selected some of them, and the rest the other companions selected. Translation: [23] Know that many narrations came from Imam Abu Hanifa, which are elevated; some of these narrations were selected by him (Imam Muhammad) and the rest were selected by the other companions (i.e., Abu Yusuf, Zufar, etc.).]
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept that Imam Abu Hanifa had numerous narrations (transmitted positions). His student Imam Muhammad selected some of these narrations for inclusion in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah. The remaining narrations were selected by other leading students of Abu Hanifa, such as Abu Yusuf and Zufar. This establishes a hierarchy: the narrations chosen by Imam Muhammad are part of the core school texts, while others may be found in the works of his peers. This is a methodological rule for a mufti to know the origins of differing positions within the school.

Key Terms
رفاق (Rifaq): Companions, referring to the other major students of Abu Hanifa such as Abu Yusuf and Zufar.
زاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that contain the selected narrations of Abu Hanifa.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or less authoritative narrations, including those selected by other companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) All the companions collectively

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's authoritative core (Zahir al-Riwayah) rests on Imam Muhammad's selection of Abu Hanifa's narrations, while other companions' selections are secondary.

Authority of Al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi in Hanafi Fatwa
Establishing Al-Mabsut as the primary authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the authority level of Al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi and apply the rule that fatwa must be based on it, rejecting any conflicting opinions.

Core Idea
Al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is the supreme authority; any ruling conflicting with it is rejected for fatwa.

This lesson establishes a key rule in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the hierarchy of sources. You will see why Al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi is likened to the sun among commentaries, and how its authority overrides later or conflicting opinions. Understanding this hierarchy prevents the mufti from relying on weaker transmissions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source and its claim
Read the first line: 'The strongest of its commentaries, which is like the sun: al-Mabsut'. Recognize that this is a declaration of supremacy over other commentaries on al-Kafi.
The metaphor 'like the sun' indicates unparalleled clarity and authority.
2
Extract the operative rule
From the translation: 'one does not act contrary to it, nor does one deviate from it'. This is the binding rule: Al-Mabsut's rulings are conclusive for fatwa.
The Urdu commentary reinforces: 'jo baat Mukhaalif-e-Mabsut Sarakhsi ho, us par amal nahi kiya jayega'.
3
Note the supporting authority
The commentary cites Allamah Najm al-Din al-Tartusi (d. 758 AH) who explicitly states that reliance and fatwa must be based on Al-Mabsut and any contrary view is invalid.
This shows the rule is not just the author's opinion but is endorsed by later Hanafi masters.
4
Understand the practical implication
For a mufti, this means when faced with a conflict between a ruling in Al-Mabsut and a ruling in a later or lesser work, the mufti must follow Al-Mabsut. This prevents arbitrary selection of opinions.
The authority of Al-Mabsut is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَقْوى شُرُوحِهِ الَّذِي كَالشَّمْسِ * مَبْسُوطُ شَمْسِ الْأُمَّةِ السَّرَخُسِي
مُعْتَمَدُ النُّقُولِ، لَيْسَ يُعْمَلُ بِخُلْفِهِ ، وَلَيْسَ عَنْهُ يُعْدَلُ
ترجمه : [۲۱] شمس الائمہ سرخی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی مبسوط، کافی کی سب سے شان دار شرح ہے، بالکل سورج کی طرح۔
[۲۲] مذاہب کے نقل کرنے میں مبسوط سرخسی قابل اعتماد ہے ؛ (لہذا) اس میں آئے ہوئے قول کے علاوہ قول پر نہ عمل کیا جائے گا، نہ ہی اس ( مبسوط سرخسی میں آئے ہوئے قول) سے عدول کیا جائے گا۔
شرح : جب "الكافي" کا تذکرہ آگیا، تو علامہ شامی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے یہ وضاحت فرمائی کہ حاکم شہید کی الکافی کی بہت سے علماء نے شرح لکھی ہے، اُن میں سب سے زیادہ بہتر اور خوب شرح شمس الائمہ سرخی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی مبسوط " ہے۔ علامہ نجم الدین ابراہیم بن علی البغدادی طرطوسی (متوفی : ۷۵۸ھ) فرماتے ہیں کہ جو بات ” مبسوط سرخسی" کے خلاف ہو، اُس پر عمل نہیں کیا جائے گا، اس پر اعتماد کرنا اور اسی کے مطابق فتوی دینا ضروری ہے۔ ( آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟ : ۴۷)
The strongest of its commentaries, which is like the sun: al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi. Reliable in transmission; one does not act contrary to it, nor does one deviate from it. Translation: [21] Al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi is the most splendid commentary of al-Kafi, exactly like the sun. [22] In transmitting the schools, al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is trustworthy; therefore, no action is taken on a saying other than what appears in it, nor is one to deviate from the saying found in it. Commentary: When al-Kafi was mentioned, Allamah Shami clarified that Hakim Shahid's al-Kafi has many commentaries written by scholars; among them, the best and most excellent commentary is al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi. Allamah Najm al-Din Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Baghdadi al-Tartusi (d. 758 AH) says: Whatever is contrary to 'al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi' is not acted upon; it is necessary to rely on it and give fatwa accordingly.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule establishing the authority of a particular source. The text first states that al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi is the strongest commentary on al-Kafi, comparing it to the sun in clarity and reliability. It then asserts that this work is the authority in transmission; one must not act against its rulings and cannot deviate from them. The Urdu commentary explains that when 'al-Kafi' was mentioned, Allamah Shami specified that among its many commentaries, al-Mabsut is the best. It further cites Allamah Najm al-Din al-Tartusi who states that any ruling conflicting with al-Mabsut is not to be acted upon; reliance and fatwa must be based on it. This establishes a clear hierarchy: al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is the primary reference for Hanafi fatwa, and its authority is binding. The commentary also references the page number from 'Aap Fatwa Kaise Dein?' for further reading.

Key Terms
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): The extensive commentary on al-Kafi by Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, considered the most authoritative and relied-upon source for Hanafi fatwa.
الكافي (al-Kafi): A foundational Hanafi fiqh work by al-Hakim al-Shahid, upon which al-Mabsut comments.
شمس الأئمة (Shams al-A'immah): Title of al-Sarakhsi, meaning 'Sun of the Imams', indicating his high rank in Hanafi scholarship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) They require reconciliation with al-Mabsut.
D) They are preferred if from later scholars.

Key Takeaway
Al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is the supreme authority in Hanafi fatwa; any ruling contradicting it must be rejected.

Multiple Narrations from Abu Hanifa: Selection and Authority
Explaining the existence and selection of multiple riwayat from Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why multiple riwayat from Abu Hanifa exist and apply the principle of ikhtiyar to determine the operative position in the Hanafi madhhab.

Core Idea
Multiple narrations resolved by selection (ikhtiyar), not uncertainty.

In the Hanafi madhhab, multiple narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa on a single issue are not a sign of inconsistency but rather reflect a systematic methodology. This lesson explores how the Imam himself selected some narrations for fatwa, while his senior students (such as Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) selected others. All accepted positions are ultimately attributed to the Imam, ensuring the unity and reliability of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core statement
Read the opening Arabic verses: they state that multiple riwayat exist from Abu Hanifa, and that he selected some; the rest are selected by his companions. Recognize that this establishes the principle of ikhtiyar.
The term 'ikhtiyar' is key: it means selection, not arbitrary choice.
2
Understand the implications for attribution
The passage emphasizes that after selection, there is no saying other than the Imam's. This means that the positions chosen by the students are not separate; they are considered part of the Imam's madhhab.
The companions swore an oath that they would not deviate from the Imam's methodology.
3
Examine the reasons for multiple riwayat
The commentary lists up to six reasons for multiple narrations. Three are summarized: error in transmission by narrators, the Imam retracting an opinion without all students knowing, and one narration based on istihsan, another on qiyas.
These reasons show that multiple narrations arise from legitimate scholarly processes, not confusion.
4
Apply the rule to fatwa practice
When a mufti encounters conflicting narrations, they must refer to the selected (mukhtar) position. The hierarchy: first check selection by Abu Hanifa, then by the Sahibayn, then by later authorities.
The fatwa hierarchy ensures consistency across the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمُ بِأَنَّ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَهُ * جَاءَتْ رِوَايَاتٌ غَدَتْ مُنِيْفَهُ
اخْتَارَ مِنْهَا بَعْضَهَا ، وَالْبَاقِي * يَخْتَارُ مِنْهُ سَائِرُ الرِّفَاقِ
فَلَمْ يَكُنْ لِغَيْرِهِ جَوَابَ * كَمَا عَلَيْهِ أَقْسَمَ الْأَصْحَابُ
ترجمه : [۲۳] جان لیجیے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے منقول ہوکر ) ایسی روایتیں آئی ہیں، جو خوب مشہور ہو چکی ہیں۔
[۲۴] اُن ہی (روایتوں) میں سے کسی کو امام صاحب صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فتوے کے لیے) منتخب کرلیا ہے اور باقی میں سے (فتوے کے لیے ) منتخب کرتے ہیں ، دوسرے تمام شاگردان ۔
[۲۵] لہذا اس اعتبار سے فقہ حنفی میں امام صاحب کے علاوہ کسی کا قول نہیں، جیسا کہ اس بات پر شاگردوں نے قسم کھائی ہے۔
شرح : یہاں علامہ شامی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے دو باتیں بیان فرمائی ہیں: ایک یہ کہ ایک مسئلے میں ایک مجتہد کے دو قول ہو سکتے ہیں یا نہیں؟ دوسرے یہ کہ صاحبین یا امام صاحب صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے اور دوسرے شاگردوں کے اقوال پر عمل مذہب حنفی سے الگ نہیں۔ جہاں تک پہلی بات کا تعلق ہے، تو اس سلسلے میں عرض ہے کہ ایک مجتہد کے ایک مسئلے میں مختلف وجوہات کی بنیاد پر متعدد اقوال ہو سکتے ہیں اور ان وجوہات کی تعداد چھ تک پہنچتی ہے، جس کی مکمل تفصیلات شرح میں موجود ہیں ، خلاصے کے طور پر یہاں بھی ذکر کر دی جارہی ہیں:
راویوں سے امام کی بات کو سنے یا سمجھنے میں غلطی کا ہونا۔
امام کا اپنے قول سے رجوع کر لینا ، مگر بعض شاگردوں کو اس کی خبر نہ ہوتا۔
دوقولوں میں سے ایک کا بہ طریق استحسان دوسرے کا بہ طریق قیاس منقول ہونا۔
And know that from Abu Hanifa came narrations that have become high. He selected some of them, and the rest are selected by all the other companions. So according to this, there is no answer for other than him, just as the companions swore upon this. Translation: [23] Know that from Imam Abu Hanifa (alayhi al-salam) such narrations have come that are very famous. [24] He (Imam) selected some of them for fatwa, and from the rest, all other students select (for fatwa). [25] Therefore, in this respect, in the Hanafi fiqh, there is no saying of anyone other than Imam, as the students have sworn upon this. Commentary: Here Allamah Shami stated two things: first, whether a mujtahid can have two opinions in one issue or not; second, that acting on the sayings of the Sahibayn or Imam and other students is not separate from the Hanafi madhhab. As for the first matter, it is stated that a mujtahid can have multiple sayings in one issue based on various reasons, the number of which reaches six; the complete details are in the sharh, but here they are mentioned in summary: 1. Error in hearing or understanding the Imam's statement from the narrators. 2. The Imam retracted his own statement but some students were not informed. 3. One of the two sayings is transmitted by way of istihsan and the other by way of qiyas.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage addresses a methodological rule in Hanafi fiqh: the existence of multiple narrations (riwayat) from Imam Abu Hanifa on a single issue. The Arabic verses state that Imam himself selected some narrations for fatwa, while the remaining are selected by his students (the Sahibayn and others). This implies that all rulings derived from these selected narrations are attributed to the Imam, as if there is no saying other than his. The Urdu translation and commentary expand on this: Allamah Shami raises two questions: first, can a mujtahid have two opinions on one issue? Second, that the opinions of the Sahibayn and other students are not separate from the Hanafi madhhab. For the first, he explains that multiple sayings can occur due to up to six reasons, of which three are summarized: (1) error in transmission or understanding by the narrators, (2) Imam's retraction of an earlier opinion unknown to some students, and (3) one saying being based on istihsan (juristic preference) and another on qiyas (analogy). This highlights that the selection of narrations by later scholars is part of the madhhab's internal methodology, and all accepted positions are ultimately attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
رواية (riwayah): A narrated opinion or transmission from Imam Abu Hanifa, possibly through various chains or circumstances.
اختيار (ikhtiyar): Selection of a particular narration for fatwa, done by Imam Abu Hanifa himself or by later students such as Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can a mujtahid (like Imam Abu Hanifa) have multiple sayings on one issue?
A) Because of differences in ijtihad based on changing circumstances.
B) Due to errors in transmission or the Imam's retraction among other reasons.
C) Because students added their own opinions to the Imam's.
D) Because the madhhab allows arbitrary choices.

Key Takeaway
Multiple narrations from Abu Hanifa are resolved through selection (ikhtiyar) by the Imam and his students; the mufta bihi position is the selected one, not any arbitrary narration.

Causes of Multiple Opinions and Tarjih Rules
Explains causes of multiple opinions and tarjih rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the six causes of multiple opinions from a single mujtahid and apply the Hanafi tarjih hierarchy to choose the preferred ruling.

Core Idea
Later opinion overrides earlier; if unknown, explicit preference; else usul tarjih rules apply.

This passage from Aun al-Mughni clarifies a fundamental aspect of Hanafi fatwa methodology: a single mujtahid (like Imam Abu Hanifa) may have multiple opinions on the same issue. Understanding the legitimate reasons for this multiplicity and the systematic hierarchy for preferring one opinion over another is essential for any mufti. The commentary provides six causes and a three-step tarjih method to ensure consistency and authority in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phenomenon
Recognize that the passage addresses the possibility and validity of multiple opinions from one mujtahid within the Hanafi school, contrary to the assumption that a scholar has only one view per issue.
This is a key feature of Hanafi methodology that allows for flexibility.
2
List the six causes
Extract each of the six reasons given in the text: (1) transmission error, (2) retraction not known, (3) istihsan vs. qiyas, (4) fatwa vs. taqwa, (5) hesitation due to conflicting evidences, (6) multiple interpretations of a single proof.
Memorize these as they are often tested in iftaa exams.
3
Understand the tarjih hierarchy
The three levels of preference: first, the later opinion supersedes the earlier; second, an explicit preference statement (e.g., 'more beneficial'); third, general usul al-fiqh tarjih rules (e.g., preferring hadith over Quran in conflict).
This hierarchy must be followed sequentially.
4
Apply the hierarchy to a scenario
Given a specific case with two opinions, walk through each level: check for later opinion, then for explicit preference, then apply usul rules. Determine which opinion is preponderant (rajih).
Practice with hypotheticals to internalize the process.
5
Note the role of the mujtahid fi al-madhhab
At the third level, only a mujtahid within the madhhab can perform usul tarjih. A lower-level mufti must rely on the preferences of such scholars.
This limits who can exercise this level of tarjih.

عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي

• دوقولوں میں سے ایک کا فتوے کی رو سے اور دوسرے کا تقوے کی رو سے
منقول ہونا۔
• دلائل میں تعارض کی وجہ سے امام کا حکم میں متردد ہو کر دورائے قائم کرنا۔ کسی دلیل کے مفہوم میں ایک سے زائد احتمال ہونے کی وجہ سے امام کی
رائے کا متعدد ہونا۔
لہذا جب کسی مسئلے میں کسی مجتہد کے مختلف اقوال ہوں، تو مندرجہ ذیل وجوہ
ترجیح کے ذریعے کسی قول کو راجح قرار دیا جائے گا:
• اگر مختلف اقوال میں سے کسی قول کے بارے میں معلوم ہو جائے کہ وہ امام کا بعد کا قول ہے، تو وہ قول مرجوع الیہ ہو جائے گا اور پہلے والا قول معدوم سمجھا
جائے گا ، اس پر عمل نہیں ہوگا۔ • اور اگر آخری قول معلوم نہ ہو سکے ، تو پھر یہ دیکھا جائے کہ کسی قول کے ساتھ کوئی ترجیعی اشارہ موجود ہے یا نہیں ؟ مثلاً کسی قول کو خود امام نے ارفق للناس، يا أوفق بالزمان" وغیرہ کہا ہو، تو اس وجہ ترجیح کی بنیاد پر وہی قول راجح
ہوگا ، اُس پر عمل کیا جائے گا۔ • اور اگر کسی قول کے ساتھ کوئی ترجیحی اشارہ نہ ہو، تو دوسروں کو مسئلہ بتانے والا یا خود عمل کرنے والا اگر مجتہد فی المذہب ہے، تو اصول فقہ میں تعارض ادلہ کی بحث میں جو وجوہ ترجیح بیان کیے گئے ہیں، مثلاً : دو آیتوں میں تعارض کے وقت
حدیث کی طرف رجوع کرنا، دو حدیثوں میں تعارض کے وقت اقوال صحابہ کی طرف رجوع کرنا ؟ اقوال صحابہ میں تعارض کے وقت قیاس کی طرف رجوع کرنا وغیرہ ان وجو د ترجیح میں سے کسی کے ذریعے کسی ایک قول کو ترجیح دے
Awn al-Mughni fi Hall 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. Page 53. 25. So he had no answer other than that, as the Companions swore upon it. Translation: [23] Know that from Imam Abu Hanifa (peace be upon him) there have been transmitted narrations that have become well-known. [24] From among them, the Imam himself selected one for fatwa, and all the other students select from the remaining. [25] Therefore, in this respect, in Hanafi fiqh there is no saying of anyone other than the Imam, as the students swore to this. Commentary: Here Allamah Shami (peace be upon him) has explained two things: one, whether a single mujtahid can have two opinions in one issue; second, that acting on the opinions of the Sahibayn or the Imam and other students is not separate from the Hanafi madhhab. As for the first point, it is stated that a single mujtahid can have multiple opinions in one issue based on various reasons, and the number of these reasons reaches six, the full details of which are in the commentary; they are summarized here: 1) Error in hearing or understanding the Imam's statement by the transmitters. 2) The Imam's retraction of his own opinion, but some students not being aware. 3) One of the two opinions transmitted via istihsan and the other via qiyas. 4) One of the two opinions transmitted from the perspective of fatwa and the other from taqwa. 5) The Imam establishing two opinions due to hesitation in ruling because of conflicting evidences. 6) Multiplicity of the Imam's opinion due to more than one possibility in the meaning of a proof. Therefore, when a mujtahid has different opinions on an issue, then one opinion will be deemed preponderant through the following grounds of preference: - If it becomes known that any one of the different opinions is the later opinion of the Imam, then that opinion becomes the one to be returned to (marju' ilayh) and the earlier opinion is considered null and void; no action is taken on it. - If the later opinion cannot be known, then it is seen whether there is any preferential indication with an opinion, such as the Imam himself saying about an opinion 'more suitable for the people' or 'more in keeping with the time', etc., then based on that ground of preference that opinion is preponderant and acted upon. - If there is no preferential indication with any opinion, then if the one informing others or acting himself is a mujtahid within the madhhab, then from the discussion of conflicting evidences in Usul al-Fiqh, the grounds of preference mentioned there are used, for example: when two verses conflict, refer to hadith; when two hadiths conflict, refer to the sayings of the Companions; when the sayings of the Companions conflict, refer to qiyas, etc., and by one of these grounds of preference, one opinion is preferred.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage from Aun al-Mughni explains two important rules in Hanafi fatwa methodology. First, it clarifies that a single mujtahid can indeed have multiple opinions on a single issue, contrary to what some might think. The author, Allamah Shami, lists six reasons for such multiplicity: (1) transmission errors, (2) the Imam retracting a view without all students knowing, (3) one view based on istihsan and another on qiyas, (4) one view for fatwa (public application) and another for taqwa (personal piety), (5) hesitancy due to conflicting evidences leading to two rulings, and (6) multiple interpretations of a single proof. Second, the passage provides a hierarchy for preferring one opinion over another: first, if the later opinion is known, it supersedes the earlier; second, if not, look for any explicit statement by the Imam indicating preference (e.g., 'more beneficial for people'); third, if no such indication, the mujtahid within the madhhab should apply the general rules of tarjih from Usul al-Fiqh, such as preferring hadith over Quran in case of conflict, then sayings of Companions over conflicting hadiths, and qiyas over conflicting sayings. This ensures consistency and authority in fatwa practice.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjih): The process of preferring one opinion over another based on specific grounds.
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar who is capable of ijtihad within the confines of the Hanafi madhhab, applying its principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the first priority when preferring one of a mujtahid's multiple opinions?
A) Look for an explicit statement that the opinion is more suitable for the people.
B) Determine if it is the later opinion of the mujtahid.
C) Apply the rules of conflict resolution from Usul al-Fiqh.
D) Choose the opinion that is easier for the public.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa methodology, when dealing with multiple opinions from a single mujtahid, precedence is given to the later opinion, then to explicitly preferred opinion, and finally to Usul al-Fiqh tarjih rules.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
