Tarjih of Multiple Rulings from One Mujtahid
Explaining preference rules for conflicting rulings from one mujtahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy of tarjih to determine the mufta bihi position when multiple opinions from Imam Abu Hanifa exist.

Core Idea
When a mujtahid has multiple opinions, only the later or preferred one is operative; the method of preference depends on the level of the scholar.

It is not uncommon that a single mujtahid, especially Imam Abu Hanifa, has more than one reported opinion on a given issue. This can happen due to conflicting evidences, considerations of public benefit, or personal caution. Hanafi usul al-ifta provides a clear hierarchy for resolving such conflicts, depending on whether the person seeking the ruling is a mujtahid fil-madhhab, a faqih, or a common Muslim. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti to issue correct fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of multiplicity
Recognize why a mujtahid may have multiple opinions: (a) one for fatwa and one for taqwa, (b) hesitation due to conflicting evidences, (c) multiple interpretations of the same evidence.
2
Apply chronological preference
If it is known which opinion is later, the later abrogates the earlier; the earlier is considered non-operative.
This is the strongest form of tarjih.
3
Check for explicit preferential indicators
If chronology is unknown, look for statements from the Imam indicating a preference, e.g., 'more beneficial for people' or 'more suitable for the time'.
These are explicit ta'liqat from the mujtahid.
4
Determine the level of the mufti
The method of tarjih differs based on who is doing the preference: a mujtahid fil-madhhab uses usul al-fiqh rules (e.g., preferring hadith over conflicting verses); a mere faqih follows the later scholars (mutā'akhkhirūn); a common Muslim follows a great pious scholar of his time.
Today's muftis are generally faqihs, so they must rely on the mutā'akhkhirūn.
5
Apply the rule in practice
When issuing a fatwa, first determine if there is a known later or preferred opinion. If not, and you are not a mujtahid, adopt the position established by the mutā'akhkhirūn.
This avoids personal ijtihad for those not qualified.

Source Text

دلائل میں تعارض کی وجہ سے امام کا حکم میں متردد ہو کر دورائے قائم کرنا۔ کسی دلیل کے مفہوم میں ایک سے زائد احتمال ہونے کی وجہ سے امام کی رائے کا متعدد ہونا۔
لہذا جب کسی مسئلے میں کسی مجتہد کے مختلف اقوال ہوں، تو مندرجہ ذیل وجوہ ترجیح کے ذریعے کسی قول کو راجح قرار دیا جائے گا:
• اگر مختلف اقوال میں سے کسی قول کے بارے میں معلوم ہو جائے کہ وہ امام کا بعد کا قول ہے، تو وہ قول مرجوع الیہ ہو جائے گا اور پہلے والا قول معدوم سمجھا جائے گا ، اس پر عمل نہیں ہوگا۔

• اور اگر محض فقیہ ہے، جیسے کہ آج کل کے اکثر مفتیانِ کرام ، تو یہ متأخرین کی ترجیحات کی پیروی کریں گے ، یعنی متاخرین نے جس قول پر فتویٰ دیا ہے، اس پر خود بھی عمل کریں گے، دوسروں کو بھی اُسی کے مطابق فتویٰ دیں گے۔
• اور اگر عام مسلمان ہیں، تو اپنے زمانے کے بڑے عالم، جو بڑے متقی و پر ہیز گار بھی ہوں ، اُن کے قول پر عمل کریں گے۔
خیر ! جب یہ بات ثابت ہو چکی کہ ایک مجتہد کے ایک مسئلے میں، متعدد اقوال ہو سکتے ہیں اور اس کی وجہ بھی سامنے آچکی ، تو اب یہ عرض ہے کہ اُن ہی مختلف روایات میں سے کسی کو کسی وجہ ترجیح کی بنا پر مجتہد فتقوے کے لیے منتخب کر لیتا ہے، جیسا کہ امام صاحب سے بہت سی روایتیں منقول و مشہور ہیں، اُن ہی میں سے کسی کو امام صاحب نے دلیل کی قوت کی بنا پر فتوے کے لیے منتخب کر لیا اور کو باقی کو چھوڑ دیا، لیکن امام صاحب نے غایت درجے کے تقوے وشدتِ احتیاط کی بنیاد پر، شاگردوں سے کہہ رکھا تھا کہ میرے مرجوح قول کو دلیل کے اعتبار سے اگر مضبوط سمجھو، تو اُسے اختیار کر لینا اور میرے اختیار کردہ راجح قول کی موافقت نہ کرنا؛ چناں چہ شاگردوں نے اسی ہدایت کے پیش نظر امام صاحب کی مختلف روایتوں میں سے، جس روایت کو دلیل کے اعتبار سے قومی سمجھا، اُسے اختیار کر لیا؟ اسی کو علامہ شامی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے و الباقي، يختار منه سائر الرفاق سے بیان فرمایا ہے۔
Aun al-Mughni fi Hall 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti
• One of two statements is transmitted as fatwa and the other as taqwa.
Due to conflict of evidences, the Imam becomes hesitant in ruling and establishes an avoidance. Due to more than one probability in the meaning of an evidence, the Imam's opinion becomes multiple.
Therefore, when there are different statements of a mujtahid in an issue, then through the following reasons of preference a statement will be considered preponderant:
• If among the different statements it becomes known about any statement that it is the Imam's later statement, then that statement will be the one referred to, and the earlier statement will be considered abrogated; action will not be taken upon it.
• And if the later statement cannot be known, then it is seen whether there is any preferential indication with any statement, for example, if the Imam himself said about a statement 'more beneficial for people' or 'more suitable for the time' etc., then based on this reason of preference that same statement is preponderant; action will be taken upon it.
• And if there is no preferential indication with any statement, then the one informing others of the issue or the one acting himself, if he is a mujtahid within the school, then in the principles of jurisprudence, in the discussion of conflict of evidences, the reasons of preference that are mentioned, for example, in case of conflict between two verses, referring to hadith; in case of conflict between two hadiths, referring to the statements of the Companions; in case of conflict between statements of Companions, referring to analogy, etc., through any of these reasons of preference he will give preference to one statement, and if no reason of preference exists, then through the testimony of his heart, whichever statement he considers preponderant, he will act upon it, and will inform others of the issue accordingly.
• And if he is merely a faqih, like most of today's respected muftis, then they will follow the preferences of the later scholars, i.e., they will themselves act upon the statement upon which the later scholars have given fatwa, and will give fatwa to others accordingly.
• And if they are common Muslims, then they will act upon the statement of the great scholar of their time, who is also greatly pious and abstinent.
Well! When it is established that a mujtahid can have multiple statements in one issue, and the reason for it has also become clear, now the point is that from among those different narrations the mujtahid selects one based on some reason of preference for fatwa, just as many narrations are transmitted and famous from Imam Sahib, from among them the Imam Sahib selected one for fatwa due to the strength of evidence and left the rest, but the Imam Sahib, based on extreme taqwa and intense caution, had told his students: 'If you consider my preponderated statement strong in terms of evidence, then adopt it and do not concur with my chosen preponderant statement.' Accordingly, the students, keeping this instruction in view, from among the different narrations of Imam Sahib, whichever narration they considered strong in terms of evidence, they adopted it. This is what 'Allama Shami (may Allah bless him) expressed with 'and the rest, from it the other companions choose.'
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage from 'Aun al-Mughni discusses the important usul al-ifta rule regarding multiplicity of rulings from a single mujtahid, specifically Imam Abu Hanifa. The text first identifies reasons why an Imam may have multiple opinions on one issue: one statement may be for fatwa (public ruling) and another for personal taqwa (piety); the Imam may be hesitant due to conflicting evidences and adopts a cautious avoidance; or the evidence itself may admit multiple interpretations, leading to multiple opinions.

Once multiple opinions exist, the text outlines a hierarchy of tarjih (preference) depending on the status of the person seeking or giving the ruling:

1. If the chronological order is known, the later opinion abrogates the earlier one; the earlier is considered non-existent.
2. If the later opinion is unknown, check for explicit preferential indicators from the Imam, such as saying a ruling is 'more beneficial for people' or 'more suitable for the time'.
3. If no such indicator exists, the person qualified as a mujtahid fil-madhhab (capable of ijtihad within the school) must apply the general rules of tarjih from usul al-fiqh: in case of conflicting verses, resort to hadith; conflicting hadiths, resort to companion statements; conflicting companion statements, resort to analogy. If no such preference exists, they may rely on their own considered judgment (shahadat al-qalb).
4. For a mere faqih (not a mujtahid), which the text notes is the case for most contemporary muftis, one must follow the preferences of the later scholars (mutā'akhkhirūn) – i.e., the established fatwa in the school.
5. For a common Muslim, one follows the great pious scholar of one's time.

The text then concludes by narrating that Imam Abu Hanifa himself, despite having chosen a preferred position for fatwa, instructed his students that if they find his other narrations stronger in evidence, they should adopt that instead. The students accordingly chose from his multiple narrations the one they deemed strongest in evidence. This is referenced by 'Allama Ibn 'Abidin (al-Shami) in his statement wa al-bāqī yukhtāru minhu sā'ir al-rifāq.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjih): The process of preferring one opinion over another when multiple opinions exist from a single mujtahid, based on specified criteria.
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar capable of exercising ijtihad within the Hanafi school, able to weigh evidences and apply usul al-fiqh rules to prefer one narration over another.
متأخرین (mutā'akhkhirūn): Later Hanafi scholars whose established fatwa (such as in major works like al-Hidaya or al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya) is to be followed by those who are not mujtahids.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mufti today is not a mujtahid fil-madhhab, how should he decide between conflicting reports from Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) He should perform ijtihad and weigh the evidences himself.
B) He should follow the fatwa of the later Hanafi scholars (mutā'akhkhirūn).
C) He should follow the opinion that is easiest for the people.
D) He should consult his own heart and choose.

Key Takeaway
The operative ruling from a mujtahid with multiple opinions is determined by chronological order, explicit preference, or the established fatwa of later scholars, depending on the mufti's level.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

8 min
Hierarchy of Taqlid and the Status of the Sahibayn's Opinions
Explains ruling hierarchy for mufti levels and Sahibayn's relation to Imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three levels of muqallid in seeking fatwa and explain the relationship between Imam Abu Hanifa's opinions and those of the Sahibayn, including the critical refinement.

Core Idea
Common Muslims follow great scholars; muftis follow later scholars; mujtahid follows his heart; Sahibayn's opinions, though rooted in Imam's narrations, often reflect independent ijtihad.

This passage from 'Aun al-Mughni' clarifies the hierarchy of who to follow in issuing and receiving fatwas. It distinguishes between a mujtahid, a faqih (mufti), and a common Muslim. It then addresses a key question: if Imam Abu Hanifa instructed his students to follow the strongest proof, and the Sahibayn sometimes chose different rulings, does acting on their views still keep one within the Hanafi school? The text presents the classical position and then a critical refinement from a later authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Levels of Muqallid
The passage specifies three categories: a fully qualified mujtahid, a faqih (mufti who cannot do ijtihad mutlaq), and a common Muslim. For each, a different rule applies for selecting the opinion to follow.
The mujtahid follows his own heart's inclination when no external preference exists; the faqih follows the preferences of the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin); the commoner follows a great pious scholar of his time.
2
Understand Imam Abu Hanifa's Multiple Narrations and His Instruction
Imam Abu Hanifa had multiple narrations on many issues. He selected one for fatwa based on strength of proof. Out of extreme piety, he told his students that if they consider another narration stronger, they should adopt it. This gave the students latitude to choose differently.
This instruction is the basis for differences between Imam and his students like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Analyze the Classical Claim about the Sahibayn
The classical claim is that the Sahibayn's sayings are still Imam's sayings because they are based on his narrations and the students swore they never opposed him. Therefore, following the Sahibayn does not take one out of Hanafiyyah.
The text says 'This is true in the majority of cases' – this is the target of the critical refinement.
4
Examine the Critical Refinement by Mufti Palanpuri
Mufti Saeed Ahmad Palanpuri argues that after the publication of the Sahibayn's books, it is clear they differed with Imam in many usul al-fiqh principles. Their capabilities are at the level of mujtahid mutlaq, so their opinions are often independently derived, not merely extensions of Imam's narrations. Thus the claim is only true in most, not all, cases.
This refinement is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, not a rejection of the earlier position.
5
Apply the Fatwa Hierarchy Today
A Hanafi muqallid can follow the Sahibayn's opinions, but should be aware that their views may be independent. The later scholars' preferences (muta'akhkhirin) are binding for muftis who cannot do ijtihad.
The practical consequence: one remains Hanafi when following Sahibayn, but this is not always identical to following Imam Abu Hanifa.

شاگردوں کے اقوال بھی امام صاحب کے اقوال ہیں امام صاحب کی اجازت سے فائدہ اٹھاتے ہوئے، شاگردوں نے جہاں بھی امام صاحب سے الگ کوئی رائے قائم کی اور کسی اور قول کو اختیار کیا، وہاں اس بات کا مکمل خیال رکھا کہ اُن کا اختیار کردہ قول، امام صاحب کی روایت سے متجاوز نہ ہو؟ اس اعتبار سے حضرت امام صاحب کے شاگردوں نے جو قول بھی اختیار کیا ہے، وہ امام صاحب ہی کی کسی نہ کسی روایت پر مبنی ہے اور وہ حضرات بھاری قسمیں کھا کر یہ دعوی کیا کرتے تھے کہ ہم نے امام صاحب کی کسی چیز میں مخالفت نہیں کی ہے لہذا حضرات صاحبین اور امام صاحب کے کسی دوسرے شاگرد کے قول پر عمل کرنے سے حنفی مقلد حنفیت کی تقلید سے خارج نہیں ہوگا؛ کیوں کہ اس معنی کر صاحبین وغیرہ نے جو قول اختیار کیا ہے، وہ کسی نہ کسی درجے میں امام صاحب کا قول بھی ہے۔

And if there is no reason for preference, then by the testimony of his heart, whichever saying he considers stronger, he should act upon it, and according to it he should inform others. • And if he is merely a faqih, like most of today's honorable muftis, then they will follow the preferences of the later scholars, meaning that they will themselves act upon the saying upon which the later scholars gave fatwa, and they will give fatwa to others accordingly. • And if they are common Muslims, then they will act upon the saying of the great scholar of their time, who is also great in piety and righteousness. Fine! When it has been established that a mujtahid can have multiple sayings in one issue, and the reason for that has become clear, now this is the presentation that from among those various narrations, the mujtahid selects one for fatwa based on some reason of preference, just as many narrations are transmitted and well-known from Imam Sahib, from among them the Imam selected one for fatwa based on the strength of the proof and left the rest, but the Imam, based on extreme piety and intense caution, had told his students that if you consider my weaker saying to be stronger in terms of proof, then adopt it and do not agree with my chosen stronger saying. Consequently, the students, following this instruction, from among the various narrations of Imam Sahib, adopted the narration they considered strong in terms of proof. This is what Allama Shami expressed with 'and the rest, from it the other companions choose.' The sayings of the students are also the sayings of Imam Sahib. Benefiting from the permission of Imam Sahib, wherever the students formed a different opinion from Imam Sahib and adopted another saying, they fully took care that their adopted saying does not exceed the narration of Imam Sahib. In this regard, whatever saying the students of Imam Sahib adopted, it is based on some narration of Imam Sahib, and they used to swear heavy oaths claiming that we have not opposed Imam Sahib in anything. Therefore, by acting upon the saying of the two Sahibs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and any other student of Imam Sahib, a Hanafi follower (muqallid) will not exit from Hanafiyyah; because, in this sense, whatever saying the two Sahibs etc. adopted is, in some degree, also the saying of Imam Sahib. This is true in the majority of cases. The teacher, his holiness Maulana Mufti Saeed Ahmad Sahib Palanpuri (may Allah have mercy on him) says that this statement will be considered correct in the majority of cases; because now most of the books of the two Sahibs have been published and come to light. By studying them, and also by studying general books of fiqh, this statement is not supported. Moreover, in many principles of usul al-fiqh, the two Sahibs differ from Imam Sahib, and with difference in principles, how can sayings remain unified? And the most important point is that the capabilities of the two Sahibs are considered to be at the level of a mujtahid mutlaq.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage from 'Aun al-Mughni' discusses the hierarchy of following in fatwa and the relationship between Imam Abu Hanifa's opinions and those of his students. The text first outlines three levels: a fully qualified mujtahid, when no external preference exists, may follow his own heart's inclination (a form of istihsan); a mere faqih (like most later muftis) must follow the preferences of the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin); and a common Muslim must follow a great pious scholar of his time. The passage then explains that Imam Abu Hanifa himself had multiple narrations on many issues, and he chose one for fatwa based on strength of evidence. However, out of extreme piety, he instructed his students that if they considered a different narration stronger, they should adopt it. This led the students (especially Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) to sometimes differ from Imam's preferred view. The text initially claims that the students' sayings are still Imam's sayings because they are based on his narrations, and thus following them does not take one out of Hanafiyyah. However, the author then presents a critical refinement from Mufti Saeed Ahmad Palanpuri, who notes that this is true only in most cases, not absolutely. He argues that after the publication of the Sahibayn's books, it is evident that they differed from Imam in many usul al-fiqh principles, making it impossible for their opinions to be identical to Imam's. Furthermore, their capability is considered that of a mujtahid mutlaq, implying independence. Thus, while following the Sahibayn remains within the Hanafi school, it is not merely an extension of Imam Abu Hanifa's views.

Key Terms
متأخرین (Muta'akhkhirin): Later Hanafi scholars after the classical period (roughly after the 6th century AH) whose tarjih is binding for later muftis.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two principal students of Imam Abu Hanifa.
مجتہد مطلق (Mujtahid Mutlaq): An absolute independent mujtahid who can derive rulings directly from primary sources without adhering to a specific madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a common Muslim do when seeking a fatwa?
A) Follow his own heart's inclination.
B) Follow the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin).
C) Follow the great pious scholar of his time.
D) Follow the strongest evidence from the sources.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi muqallid must follow a hierarchy: commoners follow a pious scholar, faqihs follow later scholars' tarjih, and mujtahids follow their own ijtihad; the Sahibayn's opinions are authoritative but not identical to Imam's in all cases.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Hierarchy of Hanafi Imams for Fatwa Selection
Explaining the sequence of preferred opinions within the Hanafi madhhab for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fixed hierarchy of Hanafi imams for fatwa selection and apply the rule that only a mujtahid mufti may depart from it based on stronger evidence.

Core Idea
For a muqallid mufti, the hierarchy is fixed: Imam, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar/Ibn Ziyad.

When issuing a fatwa, a Hanafi mufti must know which opinion to prioritize. This passage from Aun al-Mughni lays out the standard hierarchy and addresses a key dispute: whether a mufti can freely choose between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief students when they differ. The answer depends on whether the mufti is a mujtahid or a muqallid, a distinction that shapes the entire rasm al-mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fixed hierarchy
Read the matn lines 26-27: first look for an explicit choice (ikhtiyar) from Imam Abu Hanifa; if absent, go to Abu Yusuf; then Muhammad; then Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad. This is the default order for a muqallid mufti.
The hierarchy is cumulative: each subsequent imam is consulted only if the previous has no clear statement on the issue.
2
Understand the preliminary note on students' statements
The passage begins by arguing that the students' opinions are traceable to Imam Abu Hanifa, so following them does not exit the madhhab. However, the commentary qualifies this as true only in most cases, since the Sahibayn were mujtahid mutlaq and differed in usul.
This note reinforces that the hierarchy is not arbitrary but based on the chain of transmission and ijtihad.
3
Analyze the dispute on takhyir vs. stronger evidence
Lines 28-29 present two views: (1) some say the mufti has free choice (takhyir) when the Sahibayn oppose Imam; (2) others say follow the stronger evidence. The text resolves that the second view applies only to a mujtahid mufti.
The phrase 'al-asahh' (the more correct) is used to prefer the evidence-based approach for mujtahids.
4
Apply the distinction between mufti mujtahid and muqallid
For a muqallid mufti (the vast majority), the hierarchy is fixed and cannot be overridden. For a mujtahid mufti, the strength of evidence determines the preferred opinion, even if it means departing from the hierarchy.
This distinction is crucial for fatwa practice: most muftis today are muqallids and must follow the fixed order.

٢٦ وَحَيْثُ لَمُ يُوجَدُ لَهُ اخْتِيَارُ * فَقَوْلُ يَعْقُوبَ هُوَ الْمُخْتَارُ ٣٧ ثُمَّ مُحَمَّدٍ ، فَقَوْلُهُ الْحَسَنُ * ثُمَّ زُفَرِ، وَابْنِ زِيَادِ نِ الْحَسَنُ ٢٨ وَقِيلَ بِالتَّخْسِيرِ فِي فَتُوَاهُ إِنْ خَالَفَ الْإِمَامَ صَاحِبَاهُ ٢٩ وَقِيلَ مَنْ دَلِيلُهُ أَقْوى رَجَحُ * وَذَا لِمُفْتِ ذِي اجْتِهَادِ نِ الْأَصَحُ ترجم : [۲۶] اور جس مسئلے میں امام صاحب کا اختیار کردہ کوئی قول
نہ ہو ، تو وہاں پھر امام ابو یوسف کے ہی قول کو لیا جائے گا۔ [۲۷] (اگر ان کا قول نہ ہو ) تو پھر امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول ہی پسندیدہ ہوگا (اگر ان کا قول بھی نہ ہو ) تو پھر امام زفر صلى الله عليه وسلم اور حسن بن زیاد کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ [۲۸] اور بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ (کسی مسئلے میں اگر ) صاحبین، امام
صاحب کی مخالفت کریں، تو مفتی کوفتوی دینے کے سلسلے میں اختیار ہے۔ [۲۹] اور یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے کہ (امام صاحب اور صاحبین میں سے ) جن کی دلیل مضبوط ہو گی ، اُن کے قول کو ترجیح ہوگی ، لیکن زیادہ صحیح یہی ہے کہ یہ بات مفتی
مجتہد کے بارے میں ہے (نہ کہ مقلد کے بارے میں)۔
تركيب محمد زفر ابن زیاد “ سب کا عطف ” یعقوب“ پر
Aun al-Mughni fi Hall Uqud Rasm al-Mufti
56
The statements of the students are also the statements of Imam Sahib, benefiting from Imam Sahib's permission. Wherever the students formed a different opinion from Imam Sahib and adopted another statement, they fully ensured that their adopted statement did not transgress the narration of Imam Sahib. In this respect, whatever statement the students of Imam Sahib have adopted, it is based on some narration of Imam Sahib himself, and they used to swear heavily claiming that they had not opposed Imam Sahib in anything. Therefore, a Hanafi muqallid who acts upon the statement of the Sahibayn or any other student of Imam Sahib (peace be upon him) does not exit from following the Hanafiyyah, because in this meaning, the statement adopted by the Sahibayn etc. is also, to some degree, the statement of Imam Sahib.
This matter is according to the majority of cases.
The teacher, His Holiness Mawlana Mufti Sa'id Ahmad Sahib Palanpuri (may Allah have mercy on him) says that this matter will be considered correct according to the majority of cases, because now most books of the Sahibayn have been printed and become public; studying them, as well as studying general books of fiqh, does not support this matter. Moreover, there are several principles of usul al-fiqh in which the Sahibayn differ from Imam Sahib, and with difference in principles, how can statements remain united? And the most important point is that the abilities of the Sahibayn are considered to be at the level of a mujtahid mutlaq.

Aun al-Mughni fi Hall Uqud Rasm al-Mufti
57
Such great abilities cannot not think of something new; this is not possible. (Aap Fatwa Kaise Den? : 58; footnote)
27
The order of adopting the statements of Hanafi jurists in matters of fatwa
26 And where there is found no choice [from Imam] for it, then the statement of Ya'qub is the chosen one. 27 Then Muhammad's, so his statement is good. Then Zufar's and Ibn Ziyad's is good. 28 And it was said that there is option in his fatwa if the two companions oppose the Imam. 29 And it was said: whoever's evidence is stronger is preponderant, and this is for a mufti who is a mujtahid; this is the more correct. Translation: [26] And in a matter where there is no chosen statement of Imam Sahib, then there the statement of Imam Abu Yusuf will be taken. [27] (If his statement is not available) then the statement of Imam Muhammad (peace be upon him) is preferable. (If his statement is also not available) then the statement of Imam Zufar (peace be upon him) and Hasan ibn Ziyad is considered reliable. [28] And some say that (in a matter if) the two companions oppose Imam Sahib, then the mufti has choice in giving fatwa. [29] And it has also been said that (among Imam Sahib and the two companions) whoever's evidence is stronger, their statement will be given preponderance, but the more correct is that this matter is about a mufti who is a mujtahid (not about a muqallid).
Construction: Muhammad, Zufar, Ibn Ziyad all are attached to 'Ya'qub'.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from Aun al-Mughni fi Hall Uqud Rasm al-Mufti discusses two interrelated topics: first, a preliminary note on the status of the statements of Imam Abu Hanifa's students; second, the specific hierarchy for selecting opinions when giving fatwa within the Hanafi madhhab. The author begins by defending the position that the opinions of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and other major students are ultimately traceable to Imam Abu Hanifa's own narrations, so acting upon them does not take one out of the Hanafi fold. However, the teacher Mufti Sa'id Ahmad Palanpuri is quoted as qualifying this as true only in most cases, noting that the Sahibayn differed with Imam in usul al-fiqh and were themselves mujtahid mutlaq capable of independent reasoning. Then the text presents the matn (verses) regarding the order of preference: first, look for an explicit choice (ikhtiyar) from Imam Abu Hanifa; if none, then take the statement of Abu Yusuf (Ya'qub); if none, then Muhammad al-Shaybani; if none, then Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad. The commentary then adds two optional views: some say that if the Sahibayn oppose Imam, the mufti has free choice (takhyir); others say to follow the stronger evidence. The text clarifies that the latter view (following stronger evidence) applies only to a mufti who is a mujtahid, not to a lay muqallid. This is a core rasm rule for Hanafi muftis in determining which opinion to give as fatwa.

Key Terms
اختيار (ikhtiyar): An explicit choice or preferred ruling attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa in a particular issue.
صاحبين (sahibayn): Abu Yusuf (Ya'qub) and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two primary students of Imam Abu Hanifa.
مفتی مجتہد (mufti mujtahid): A mufti who has the ability to exercise ijtihad (independent legal reasoning) to weigh evidence and determine the stronger opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which imam's statement should be preferred if neither Imam Abu Hanifa nor Abu Yusuf has a chosen statement in a particular issue?
A) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
B) Imam Zufar
C) Hasan ibn Ziyad
D) Any of the Sahibayn

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti must follow the fixed hierarchy: Imam, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar/Ibn Ziyad; only a mujtahid mufti may override based on stronger evidence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Hierarchy of Hanafi Imams for Fatwa Preference
Establishes the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy and the exception for mujtahids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy for fatwa and distinguish when a mufti may prefer the stronger dalil over the hierarchy.

Core Idea
Fatwa priority: Imam → Abu Yusuf → Muhammad → Zufar/Hasan; only mujtahid muftis may follow stronger proof against the hierarchy.

This lesson establishes the order of preference among Hanafi imams when issuing fatwas. It also clarifies a key dispute: when the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree with Imam Abu Hanifa, who should be followed? The answer depends on whether the mufti is a mujtahid or a muqallid.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the base hierarchy
Start from Imam Abu Hanifa's chosen opinion. If not found, take Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad. This is the default for all muftis.
This sequence is given in the text as verses 26-27.
2
Identify the dispute
When Sahibayn oppose Imam, some say mufti has free choice; others say follow stronger dalil. The text clarifies that the correct view is that this choice applies only to a mujtahid mufti.
Verses 28-29 address this dispute.
3
Apply the distinction
For a muqallid mufti (one who cannot independently weigh evidence), the hierarchy must be followed strictly. For a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, stronger evidence can override the hierarchy.
This is the practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute.

Source Text

۲۷ فتوے کے سلسلے میں فقہائے احناف کے قول کو اختیار کرنے کی ترتیب
٢٦ وَحَيْثُ لَمْ يُوجَدْ لَهُ اخْتِيَارُ * فَقَوْلُ يَعْقُوبَ هُوَ الْمُخْتَارُ ٣٧ ثُمَّ مُحَمَّدٍ، فَقَوْلُهُ الْحَسَنُ * ثُمَّ زُفَرَ، وَابْنِ زِيَادِ الْحَسَنُ ٢٨ وَقِيلَ بِالتَّخْسِيرِ فِي فَتُوَاهُ إِنْ خَالَفَ الْإِمَامَ صَاحِبَاهُ ٢٩ وَقِيلَ مَنْ دَلِيلُهُ أَقْوَى رَجَحُ * وَذَا لِمُفْتِ ذِي اجْتِهَادِ الْأَصَحُ
ترجم : [۲۶] اور جس مسئلے میں امام صاحب کا اختیار کردہ کوئی قول نہ ہو، تو وہاں پھر امام ابو یوسف کے ہی قول کو لیا جائے گا۔ [۲۷] (اگر ان کا قول نہ ہو) تو پھر امام محمد کا قول ہی پسندیدہ ہوگا (اگر ان کا قول بھی نہ ہو) تو پھر امام زفر اور حسن بن زیاد کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ [۲۸] اور بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ (کسی مسئلے میں اگر) صاحبین، امام صاحب کی مخالفت کریں، تو مفتی کو فتوی دینے کے سلسلے میں اختیار ہے۔ [۲۹] اور یہ بھی کہا گیا ہے کہ (امام صاحب اور صاحبین میں سے) جن کی دلیل مضبوط ہوگی، اُن کے قول کو ترجیح ہوگی، لیکن زیادہ صحیح یہی ہے کہ یہ بات مفتی مجتہد کے بارے میں ہے (نہ کہ مقلد کے بارے میں)۔
شرح : ان اشعار سے پہلے علامہ نے اپنی شرح میں یہ بات بیان فرمائی ہے کہ جس مسئلے میں ہمارے ائمہ (امام صاحب وصاحبین وغیرہ) متفق ہوں، اس میں کسی مجتہد فی المذہب کے لیے بھی جائز نہیں کہ وہ (عرف وضرورت کے علاوہ میں) ان ائمہ کی متفقہ رائے سے عدول کر کے اپنی رائے پر عمل کرے؛ کیوں کہ اُن کی رائے اس مجتہد کی رائے سے زیادہ صحیح ہے۔
27 Order of adopting the statements of Hanafi jurists in issuing fatwas. 26 And when his (Abu Hanifa's) chosen opinion is not found, then the statement of Ya'qub (Abu Yusuf) is the chosen one. 37 Then Muhammad, then his statement is good. Then Zufar, and Ibn Ziyad al-Hasan. 28 And it was said there is choice (takhayyur) in his fatwa if the two companions (Sahibayn) oppose the Imam. 29 And it was said: whose evidence is stronger is preferred, and this is for a mufti who is a mujtahid; this is the most correct. Translation: [26] And in a matter where Imam (Abu Hanifa) has no chosen statement, then the statement of Imam Abu Yusuf will be taken. [27] (If his statement is not present) then the statement of Imam Muhammad is preferred. (If his statement is also not present) then the statement of Imam Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad is considered. [28] And some scholars say that (if in a matter) the two companions oppose the Imam, then the mufti has choice in giving the fatwa. [29] And it has also been said that (among the Imam and the two companions) whose proof is stronger, their statement will be given preference, but the more correct is that this applies to a mufti who is a mujtahid (not to a muqallid). Commentary: Before these verses, the author stated in his commentary that in a matter where our Imams (Imam Abu Hanifa, the two companions, etc.) are agreed, it is not permissible for any mujtahid within the madhhab to deviate from their consensus and act on his own opinion (except in matters of custom and necessity), because their opinion is more correct than that mujtahid's opinion.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule (methodological rule) for Hanafi muftis on how to prioritize the opinions of Hanafi imams when issuing fatwas. The author begins by stating the hierarchy after Imam Abu Hanifa: when the Imam's own chosen opinion is unknown, the mufti should first look to the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf (Ya'qub). If that is not found, then to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. If that is also not available, then to Imam Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad. Then the author addresses a dispute: when the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) oppose Imam Abu Hanifa, some scholars say the mufti has free choice (takhayyur) between the two opinions. Others say the stronger dalil should be preferred. The author clarifies that the correct view is that this choice or preference is only for a mufti who is a mujtahid within the madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab), not for a muqallid (one who merely follows). The final commentary adds that when all major Hanafi imams agree, no one may depart from that consensus, emphasizing the binding nature of agreed rulings. This passage is fundamental for any Hanafi mufti to know the correct tarjih (preference) procedure.

Key Terms
صاحبین (Sāḥibayn): The two principal companions of Imam Abu Hanifa: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
مختار (mukhtār): The chosen or preferred opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa in a given issue.
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fī al-madhhab): A scholar within the Hanafi school who has the ability to derive rulings from the principles of the school, but not independently from primary sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a mufti does not know Imam Abu Hanifa's chosen opinion, what is the correct order for selecting a fatwa?
A) Abu Yusuf → Muhammad → Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad
B) Muhammad → Abu Yusuf → Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad
C) Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad → Abu Yusuf → Muhammad
D) Any opinion among the Hanafi imams is equally valid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy is: Imam's chosen view → Abu Yusuf → Muhammad → Zufar/Hasan, and only a mujtahid mufti may depart from this order based on stronger evidence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Hierarchy of Imams for Fatwa in Ikhtilaf
Rasm al-mufti rule on imam hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of preference among Hanafi imams for issuing fatwas and apply the hierarchy to resolve cases of ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Fatwa follows Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and Ibn Ziyad.

This passage from Aun al-Mughni clarifies the hierarchy of imams for fatwa when the founding Hanafi masters disagree. Understanding this order is essential for a mufti to determine which opinion is operative. The text also addresses a nuanced dispute: what if the Sahibayn both oppose Abu Hanifa?

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational hierarchy
From the text, list the imams in order: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa, (2) Imam Abu Yusuf, (3) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, (4) Imam Zufar and Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad.
If Imam Abu Hanifa has a qawl mukhtar, it is taken; otherwise, proceed down the list.
2
Understand scenarios involving Sahibayn
The text refines that if one of the Sahibayn agrees with Abu Hanifa, his opinion is preponderant. If both oppose him, later scholars differ.
The Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Analyze the dispute
Some scholars hold that when Sahibayn agree against Abu Hanifa, their view should prevail; the majority still prefer Abu Hanifa. Know both views but follow the mufta bihi.
The mufta bihi is the majority position: Abu Hanifa’s view is preponderant unless a later tarjih says otherwise.
4
Apply the hierarchy
Given a fictional case where Abu Hanifa says X is halal, Abu Yusuf says X is haram, and Muhammad is silent, the fatwa follows Abu Hanifa (since he has the highest rank).
Always check if the issue has a clear mufta bihi in the later madhhab works.

Source Text

عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي

۵۸
ہے، یعقوب مضاف الیہ ہونے کی وجہ سے حالت جری میں ہے، غیر منصرف ہونے کی وجہ سے کسرہ نہیں آیا؟ لہذا تمام معطوفات مجرور ہوں گے، زفر “ چوں کہ غیر منصرف ہے ؛ اس لیے کسرہ نہیں آنا چاہیے تھا، مگر ضرورت شعری کی بناء پر یہاں اس پر کسرے والی تنوین آئے گی ۔ ابن زیادِ الْحَسَن“ اصل میں حسن ابن زیاد ہے، ضرورت شعری کی بنا پر اس طرح کیا گیا ہے۔ ”الإمام مفعول مقدم ہے، ”صاحباہ“ بہ ترکیب اضافی ”خالف کا فاعل ہے۔ ” ذا“ اسم اشارہ مبتدا ہے( مشار الیہ وَقِيلَ مَنْ دَلِيلُهُ أَقْوى رَجَحُ “ ہے)” مفت“ موصوف ”ذِي اجْتِهَاد“ اس کی صفت ، موصوف صفت سے مل کر محذوف سے متعلق ہو کر خبر ہے۔ ”الأصح مبتدا’هذا (محذوف) اُس کی خبر ہے۔
وضاحت بعض نسخوں کے مطابق [مــحــمــد، زفر، ابن زیاد]؛ سب مرفوع ہیں، اس صورت میں ان کا عطف یعقوب“ پر نہیں ہوگا؛ بل کہ ”قول“ پر ہوگا ، عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ امام ابو یوسف کے بعد مرتبے میں امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ہیں ، پھر امام زفر صلى الله عليه وسلم اور ابن زیاد ہ ہیں ، لہذا اسی اعتبار سے ان کا قول ، مختار و پسندیدہ ہوگا۔
شرح : ان اشعار سے پہلے علامہ نے اپنی شرح میں یہ بات بیان فرمائی ہے کہ جس مسئلے میں ہمارے ائمہ (امام صاحب وصاحبین اه وغیرہ ) متفق ہوں، اس میں کسی مجتہد فی المذہب کے لیے بھی جائز نہیں کہ وہ (عرف وضرورت کے علاوہ میں) ان ائمہ کی متفقہ رائے سے عدول کر کے اپنی رائے پر عمل کرے؛ کیوں کہ اُن کی رائے اس مجتہد کی رائے سے زیادہ صحیح ہے۔

۵۹
اب یہاں سے علامہ شامی صلى الله عليه وسلم یہ بات بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی مسئلے میں ہمارے ائمہ کے مابین اختلاف ہو، تو ترجیح کی ترتیب کیا ہوگی؟ چناں چہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمارے ائمہ کے مابین اختلاف کی صورت میں اگر امام صاحب کا کوئی مختار قول ہو ، تو اس کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا، اگر امام صاحب کا کوئی قول نہ ہو، ہو ، تو پھر امام ابو یوسف صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا، پیش آمدہ مسئلے میں اگر امام ابو یوسف کا بھی کوئی قول نہ ہو، تو پھر امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کو اختیار کیا جائے گا، اگر ان کا بھی کوئی قول نہ ملے تو پھر امام زفر صلى الله عليه وسلم اور امام حسن بن زیاد وغیرہ کے قول کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا۔
اس کی تنقیح کرتے ہوئے یوں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ اگر کسی مسئلے میں ہمارے ائمہ
کے مابین اختلاف ہو ، تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں:
• امام صاحب تنہا ہیں۔ • صاحبین میں سے کوئی ساتھ ہیں، اگر ساتھ ہیں، تو امام صاحب ہی کا قول
راج ہوگا۔
اگر صاحبین میں سے کوئی ساتھ نہیں، تو پھر اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں:
وہ دونوں ایک ساتھ ہیں۔ • دونوں الگ الگ ہیں، اگر وہ دونوں بھی الگ الگ ہیں ؛ تو ایسی صورت
میں بھی امام صاحب ہی کا قول رائج ہوگا۔ اور اگر امام صاحب ایک طرف ہیں ، صاحبین دوسری طرف ؛ تو ایسی صورت میں حضرات فقہاء کی رائے مختلف ہے۔ بعض کہتے ہیں کہ اس صورت میں بھی امام صاحب ہی کا قول راج ہوگا۔ دوسرے بعض حضرات کی رائے بالکل اس سے مختلف
Aun al-Mughni fi Hall Uqud Rasm al-Mufti

58: [Grammatical explanation:] Ya'qub is in the genitive case because it is the second element of an idafa; due to being diptotic, it does not take kasra? So all conjuncts are majrur. Zufar, since it is diptotic, should not take kasra, but due to poetic necessity, tanwin with kasra comes here. Ibn Ziyad al-Hasan is originally Hasan ibn Ziyad, done so due to poetic necessity. 'al-Imam' is a fronted object, 'sahibahu' in idafa construction is the subject of 'khalafa'. 'Dha' is a demonstrative pronoun as mubtada (the pointed to is 'wa qila man daliluhu aqwa rajaha'), 'muft' is the mawsuf, 'dhi ijtihad' is its adjective; together they form the khabar of a deleted prepositional phrase. 'al-Asahh' is mubtada, 'hadha' (deleted) is its khabar.

Clarification: According to some manuscripts, [Muhammad, Zufar, Ibn Ziyad] are all marfu'; in that case, their conjunction is not to 'Ya'qub' but to 'qawl'. The meaning would be: after Imam Abu Yusuf, in rank are Imam Muhammad (peace be upon him), then Imam Zufar (peace be upon him) and Ibn Ziyad. Hence accordingly, their saying is chosen and preferred.

Commentary: Before these verses, the author (Allama) stated in his commentary that in a matter where our imams (Imam Sahib, Sahibayn, etc.) agree, no mujtahid within the madhhab is permitted to deviate from their agreed-upon opinion and act on his own (except due to custom or necessity), because their opinion is more correct than his opinion.

59: Now Allama Shami (peace be upon him) is explaining that if there is disagreement among our imams, what is the order of preference? Thus he says: In case of disagreement among our imams, if Imam Sahib has a chosen (mukhtar) opinion, then fatwa is given according to it. If Imam Sahib has no opinion, then fatwa is given according to the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf (peace be upon him). If there is no opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf in the occurring matter, then the opinion of Imam Muhammad (peace be upon him) is adopted. If no opinion of his is found, then fatwa is given according to the opinion of Imam Zufar (peace be upon him) and Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad, etc.

Refining this, it can be said: If there is disagreement among our imams in a matter, there are two scenarios:
- Imam Sahib is alone.
- One of the Sahibayn agrees with him. If one agrees, then Imam Sahib's opinion is preponderant.
If none of the Sahibayn agrees, then there are two sub-scenarios:
- They are together.
- They are separate. If they are separate, then also Imam Sahib's opinion is adopted. And if Imam Sahib is on one side and the two Sahibayn on the other, then the scholars differ. Some say in this case also Imam Sahib's opinion is preponderant. Others hold a completely different view.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the hierarchy of imams for issuing fatwas in the Hanafi madhhab when there is disagreement (ikhtilaf) among the founding imams. The text first discusses grammatical points of a poetic verse that lists the imams, clarifying that according to some manuscripts the names Muhammad, Zufar, and Ibn Ziyad are nominative and conjoined to 'qawl' (statement) rather than to 'Ya'qub', implying that they are independent sources. The main sharh then lays out the rule: the order of preference is (1) Imam Abu Hanifa, (2) Imam Abu Yusuf, (3) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, (4) Imam Zufar and Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad. If Imam Abu Hanifa has a chosen opinion, it is taken; otherwise, the next in line. The author further refines this with scenarios involving the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): if one of them agrees with Abu Hanifa, his opinion is preponderant; if they disagree with him, there is a difference among later scholars—some still prefer Abu Hanifa, while others differ. This is a rasm al-mufti rule essential for a mufti to know which qawl to adopt when primary sources diverge. The authority of this hierarchy is based on the established practice of the madhhab from the earlier authorities (mutakaddimin).

Key Terms
قول مختار (qawl mukhtar): The preferred or chosen opinion of an imam in a given issue, distinguished from other opinions he may have held.
راجح (rajih): The preponderant or weightier opinion that is to be followed in fatwa when there is conflict.
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar capable of ijtihad within the Hanafi school, following its principles and preferring among its rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hierarchy for fatwa in cases of ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams, whose opinion is followed if Imam Abu Hanifa has no opinion on the matter?
A) Imam Muhammad's opinion
B) Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion
C) Imam Zufar's opinion
D) The opinion of the Sahibayn together

Key Takeaway
In case of ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams, the mufti gives priority to Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and Hasan bin Ziyad.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
8 min
Basic Preference Order Among Hanafi Imams
Basic preference hierarchy and simple alignment cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default preference order among Hanafi imams for fatwa and apply it to simple alignment scenarios.

Core Idea
Fatwa follows Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and others.

When our Imams have differing opinions on an issue, a mufti must know whom to follow first. This lesson introduces the foundational hierarchy set by later Hanafi authorities. The passage begins with a clear order and then refines it based on how the imams align with one another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default order
The passage states: if Imam Abu Hanifa has a chosen opinion, take it; if not, take Imam Abu Yusuf; if not, take Imam Muhammad; if not, take Imam Zufar and others. Memorize this sequence.
This order is the starting point for all fatwa hierarchies.
2
Apply the first alignment rule
When Imam Abu Hanifa is alone (Sahibayn have no opinion) or when one Sahib agrees with him, his opinion is preponderant. This reinforces his priority.
The presence of one Sahib does not weaken the Imam's position.
3
Apply the second alignment rule
When both Sahibayn are together but separate from Imam Abu Hanifa, even then his opinion is preferred. This shows the strong precedence given to the founder of the school.
Only when both Sahibayn oppose him does the conflict require deeper analysis (see next lesson).

اس کی تنقیح کرتے ہوئے یوں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ اگر کسی مسئلے میں ہمارے ائمہ کے مابین اختلاف ہو ، تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں:
• امام صاحب تنہا ہیں۔ • صاحبین میں سے کوئی ساتھ ہیں، اگر ساتھ ہیں، تو امام صاحب ہی کا قول راج ہوگا۔

وہ دونوں ایک ساتھ ہیں۔ • دونوں الگ الگ ہیں، اگر وہ دونوں بھی الگ الگ ہیں ؛ تو ایسی صورت میں بھی امام صاحب ہی کا قول رائج ہوگا۔ اور اگر امام صاحب ایک طرف ہیں ، صاحبین دوسری طرف ؛ تو ایسی صورت میں حضرات فقہاء کی رائے مختلف ہے۔ بعض کہتے ہیں کہ اس صورت میں بھی امام صاحب ہی کا قول راج ہوگا۔ دوسرے بعض حضرات کی رائے بالکل اس سے مختلف ہے، وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ایسی صورت میں مفتی کو اختیار ہے، جن کے قول پر چاہے فتویٰ دے، مفتی خواہ مجتہد ہو یا مقلد ۔ اور اس سلسلے میں تیسری راے جو محققین کی ہے، وہ یہ ہے کہ مفتی اگر مقلد ہے، تب تو اُس پر لازم ہے کہ وہ امام صاحب ہی کے قول پر فتوی دے ۔ ہاں! اگر مفتی مجتہد ہے، تو اُسے اختیار ہو گا کہ وہ قوت دلیل کی بنیاد پر کسی قول کو ترجیح دے۔
اس تیسری رائے کو جو زیادہ درست کہا گیا ہے، وہ اس بنیاد پر کہ اس کا تعلق مفتی مجہد سے ہے ، اس تیسری راے میں مفتی مجتہد ، مفتی غیر مجتہد کا فرق ہے اس سے پہلی اور دوسری رائے میں تطبیق بھی ہو جاتی ہے، وہ اس طرح کہ جنھوں نے مطلقاً امام صاحب صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کو لینے کی بات کہی ہے ، اُن کی بات کا تعلق مفتی مقلد سے ہے اور جنھوں نے مطلقاً اختیار دیا ہے، ان کے اختیار دینے کا تعلق مفتی مجتہد سے ہے ، اب اس طرح تینوں آراء کے مابین کوئی اختلاف باقی نہیں رہے گا۔ مُلاحظة : اس بحث میں جو بار بار مجید مفتی“ کا لفظ آیا ہے، اس سے مجتہد مطلق مراد نہیں ؛ بل کہ فی ر مقید مراد ہے، اس میں ”مجھ
،،
المذہب "مجتهد في المسائل اصحاب تخریج اور اصحاب صحیح و ترجیح ؛ سب
ہی شامل ہیں۔
مجتہدین کے تین طبقات ہیں: (۱) مجتہد مطلق مستقل (۲) مجتہد مطلق منتسب (۳) مجتہد فی المذہب تینوں کی تفصیلات فتوی نویسی کے رہنما اصول میں دیکھئے۔
From here, Allamah Shami (may Allah have mercy on him) states that if there is a difference of opinion among our Imams on an issue, what is the order of preference? So he says: In the case of a difference among our Imams, if Imam Abu Hanifa has a chosen opinion, then fatwa will be given according to it. If Imam Abu Hanifa has no opinion, then fatwa will be given according to the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf. If in the occurring issue Imam Abu Yusuf also has no opinion, then the opinion of Imam Muhammad will be adopted. If even his opinion is not found, then fatwa will be given according to the opinion of Imam Zufar and Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad and others. Elaborating on this, it can be said: If there is a difference among our Imams on an issue, there are two scenarios: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa alone, (2) One of the Sahibayn is with him. If one is with him, then Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is preponderant. If neither Sahib is with him, then two scenarios: both Sahibayn are together, or both are separate. If they are separate, even then Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is prevalent. And if Imam Abu Hanifa is on one side and the two Sahibayn on the other, then the jurists have different views. Some say that even in this case Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is preponderant. Others have a contrary view; they say that in such a case the mufti has a choice, he may give fatwa according to whichever opinion he wishes, whether the mufti is a mujtahid or a muqallid. The third view of the verifiers is that if the mufti is a muqallid, then it is incumbent upon him to give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion. But if the mufti is a mujtahid, then he may choose to prefer any opinion based on strength of evidence. This third view is considered more correct because it distinguishes between mujtahid and non-mujtahid mufti, and it reconciles the first two views: those who absolutely said to take Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion refer to the muqallid mufti, and those who absolutely gave choice refer to the mujtahid mufti. Thus there remains no conflict among the three views. Note: In this discussion, the repeated term 'mujtahid mufti' does not mean mujtahid mutlaq; rather it means mujtahid muqayyad, which includes mujtahid fil-madhhab, mujtahid fil-masa'il, ashab al-takhrij, and ashab al-tashih wa al-tarjih. The mujtahids have three levels: (1) Mujtahid mutlaq mustaqill, (2) Mujtahid mutlaq muntasib, (3) Mujtahid fil-madhhab. Details of these three are to be seen in the principles of fatwa writing.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a detailed rasm al-mufti rule on the hierarchy of preference among Hanafi imams when there is ikhtilaf. It begins by stating the basic order: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad. Then it refines the rule by considering various alignments: (1) When Abu Hanifa is alone (i.e., the Sahibayn do not have an opinion) or when one of the Sahibayn agrees with him, his opinion is preferred. (2) When the Sahibayn are both together but separate from him, even then his opinion is preferred. (3) When Abu Hanifa stands on one side and both Sahibayn on the opposite side, then there are three scholarly opinions among later Hanafis: the first says Abu Hanifa's opinion is still preferred; the second gives the mufti absolute choice; the third distinguishes between a muqallid mufti (who must follow Abu Hanifa) and a mujtahid mufti (who may choose). The author endorses the third view as it reconciles the first two and is more precise. Finally, it clarifies that 'mujtahid mufti' here refers to a mujtahid muqayyad (bound mujtahid) within the madhhab, not a mujtahid mutlaq, and lists three levels of mujtahids. This passage is essential for a mufti to know how to issue fatwa when confronted with multiple narrations within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
صاحبین (sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two primary disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the basic preference hierarchy, which Imam's opinion should be followed first?
A) Imam Muhammad
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Abu Hanifa
D) Imam Zufar

Key Takeaway
The default fatwa hierarchy is Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and others; this is the starting point for any Hanafi mufti.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Refined Preference Rule: Mufti's Level and the Three Opinions
Refined rule for conflict between Abu Hanifa and both Sahibayn, with three opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three opinions when Imam Abu Hanifa and both Sahibayn disagree, and identify the mufta bihi view that distinguishes between muqallid and mujtahid muftis.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti must follow Abu Hanifa; a mujtahid may choose by evidence.

When both Sahibayn oppose Imam Abu Hanifa, the simple hierarchy is not enough. Later Hanafi jurists gave three different rulings. This lesson unpacks each view, their basis, and the verified reconciliation that depends on the mufti's own level of ijtihad. Understanding this is crucial for issuing fatwa correctly within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict scenario
The scenario: Imam Abu Hanifa holds one opinion, and both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold a different opinion together. This triggers the need for a refined rule.
This is the only case where the basic hierarchy is contested.
2
List the three opinions
First opinion: even here, Abu Hanifa's view is preponderant. Second opinion: the mufti has absolute choice, whether he is a mujtahid or muqallid. Third opinion (verified): it depends on the mufti's level.
Memorize the three views and their proponents.
3
Analyze the reconciliation
The third view reconciles the first two by noting that the first view is for the muqallid mufti, while the second view is for the mujtahid mufti. Thus no real contradiction exists.
This reconciliation is praised by the author as 'more correct'.
4
Define the terms 'mujtahid' and 'muqallid' in this context
'Mujtahid mufti' here refers to a mujtahid muqayyad within the madhhab (not a mutlaq), including those capable of takhrij and tarjih. A muqallid mufti cannot perform ijtihad.
The passage also mentions three levels of mujtahid: mutlaq mustaqill, mutlaq muntasib, and fil-madhhab.

اس تیسری رائے کو جو زیادہ درست کہا گیا ہے، وہ اس بنیاد پر کہ اس کا تعلق مفتی مجہد سے ہے ، اس تیسری راے میں مفتی مجتہد ، مفتی غیر مجتہد کا فرق ہے اس سے پہلی اور دوسری رائے میں تطبیق بھی ہو جاتی ہے، وہ اس طرح کہ جنھوں نے مطلقاً امام صاحب صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کو لینے کی بات کہی ہے ، اُن کی بات کا تعلق مفتی مقلد سے ہے اور جنھوں نے مطلقاً اختیار دیا ہے، ان کے اختیار دینے کا تعلق مفتی مجتہد سے ہے ، اب اس طرح تینوں آراء کے مابین کوئی اختلاف باقی نہیں رہے گا۔ مُلاحظة : اس بحث میں جو بار بار مجید مفتی“ کا لفظ آیا ہے، اس سے مجتہد مطلق مراد نہیں ؛ بل کہ فی ر مقید مراد ہے، اس میں ”مجھ
،،
المذہب "مجتهد في المسائل اصحاب تخریج اور اصحاب صحیح و ترجیح ؛ سب
ہی شامل ہیں۔
مجتہدین کے تین طبقات ہیں: (۱) مجتہد مطلق مستقل (۲) مجتہد مطلق منتسب (۳) مجتہد فی المذہب تینوں کی تفصیلات فتوی نویسی کے رہنما اصول میں دیکھئے۔
From here, Allamah Shami (may Allah have mercy on him) states that if there is a difference of opinion among our Imams on an issue, what is the order of preference? So he says: In the case of a difference among our Imams, if Imam Abu Hanifa has a chosen opinion, then fatwa will be given according to it. If Imam Abu Hanifa has no opinion, then fatwa will be given according to the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf. If in the occurring issue Imam Abu Yusuf also has no opinion, then the opinion of Imam Muhammad will be adopted. If even his opinion is not found, then fatwa will be given according to the opinion of Imam Zufar and Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad and others. Elaborating on this, it can be said: If there is a difference among our Imams on an issue, there are two scenarios: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa alone, (2) One of the Sahibayn is with him. If one is with him, then Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is preponderant. If neither Sahib is with him, then two scenarios: both Sahibayn are together, or both are separate. If they are separate, even then Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is prevalent. And if Imam Abu Hanifa is on one side and the two Sahibayn on the other, then the jurists have different views. Some say that even in this case Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is preponderant. Others have a contrary view; they say that in such a case the mufti has a choice, he may give fatwa according to whichever opinion he wishes, whether the mufti is a mujtahid or a muqallid. The third view of the verifiers is that if the mufti is a muqallid, then it is incumbent upon him to give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion. But if the mufti is a mujtahid, then he may choose to prefer any opinion based on strength of evidence. This third view is considered more correct because it distinguishes between mujtahid and non-mujtahid mufti, and it reconciles the first two views: those who absolutely said to take Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion refer to the muqallid mufti, and those who absolutely gave choice refer to the mujtahid mufti. Thus there remains no conflict among the three views. Note: In this discussion, the repeated term 'mujtahid mufti' does not mean mujtahid mutlaq; rather it means mujtahid muqayyad, which includes mujtahid fil-madhhab, mujtahid fil-masa'il, ashab al-takhrij, and ashab al-tashih wa al-tarjih. The mujtahids have three levels: (1) Mujtahid mutlaq mustaqill, (2) Mujtahid mutlaq muntasib, (3) Mujtahid fil-madhhab. Details of these three are to be seen in the principles of fatwa writing.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a detailed rasm al-mufti rule on the hierarchy of preference among Hanafi imams when there is ikhtilaf. It begins by stating the basic order: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad. Then it refines the rule by considering various alignments: (1) When Abu Hanifa is alone (i.e., the Sahibayn do not have an opinion) or when one of the Sahibayn agrees with him, his opinion is preferred. (2) When the Sahibayn are both together but separate from him, even then his opinion is preferred. (3) When Abu Hanifa stands on one side and both Sahibayn on the opposite side, then there are three scholarly opinions among later Hanafis: the first says Abu Hanifa's opinion is still preferred; the second gives the mufti absolute choice; the third distinguishes between a muqallid mufti (who must follow Abu Hanifa) and a mujtahid mufti (who may choose). The author endorses the third view as it reconciles the first two and is more precise. Finally, it clarifies that 'mujtahid mufti' here refers to a mujtahid muqayyad (bound mujtahid) within the madhhab, not a mujtahid mutlaq, and lists three levels of mujtahids. This passage is essential for a mufti to know how to issue fatwa when confronted with multiple narrations within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مجتهد مقید (mujtahid muqayyad): A bound mujtahid within the Hanafi madhhab who can perform takhrij, tashih, and tarjih but does not have the absolute independence of a mujtahid mutlaq.
مقلد (muqallid): A mufti who lacks ijtihad capacity and must follow the Imam of the madhhab without modification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the verified view (third opinion), what is the duty of a muqallid mufti when Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ?
A) He may choose any opinion based on his preference.
B) He must follow the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa.
C) He must follow the opinion of the Sahibayn (majority).
D) He must refer the question to a mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
When Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn conflict, the mufta bihi view distinguishes between a muqallid (must follow Abu Hanifa) and a mujtahid (may choose by evidence).

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
The Mufti's Choice: Muqallid vs Mujtahid
Parsing a rule that reconciles earlier views by distinguishing mufti types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the third opinion's rule to determine whether a mufti must follow Imam Abu Hanifa or may choose based on evidence, and classify mujtahideen into their three levels.

Core Idea
A mufti's discretion depends on his level: muqallid must follow the imam; mujtahid may weigh evidence.

When multiple opinions exist within the Hanafi school, which one should a mufti adopt? Early scholars held two absolute views: one said always follow Imam Abu Hanifa, the other gave absolute choice. This passage presents the third opinion of the verifiers that resolves the conflict by distinguishing between the muqallid mufti and the mujtahid mufti. Understanding this distinction is foundational for anyone issuing fatwas or analyzing Hanafi legal methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions
Recognize that there are three views on mufti's choice: absolute adherence to Imam Abu Hanifa, absolute discretion, and a middle view that distinguishes based on the mufti's capacity.
The first two opinions are extremes; the third reconciles them.
2
Understand the third opinion's distinction
The third opinion states that a muqallid mufti must give fatwa only according to Imam Abu Hanifa's statement, while a mujtahid mufti has discretion to prefer any opinion based on evidence strength (qawat al-dalil).
This distinction rests on the mufti's ability to independently evaluate evidence.
3
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a hypothetical mufti, determine whether he is a muqallid or a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, then state his obligation according to the third opinion.
Scenario: A mufti who memorizes the school's rulings but cannot derive from primary sources is a muqallid.
4
Classify the levels of mujtahideen
Note the three classes: mujtahid mutlaq mustaqill (independent absolute), mujtahid mutlaq muntasib (affiliated absolute), and mujtahid fi al-madhhab (within the school). Understand that the mujtahid mufti in this discussion refers to the third category and its sub-ranks.
Details of each class are found in the guide to fatwa writing; here we focus on recognition.

Source Text

ہے، وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ایسی صورت میں مفتی کو اختیار ہے، جن کے قول پر چاہے فتویٰ دے، مفتی خواہ مجتہد ہو یا مقلد ۔ اور اس سلسلے میں تیسری راے جو محققین کی ہے، وہ یہ ہے کہ مفتی اگر مقلد ہے، تب تو اُس پر لازم ہے کہ وہ امام صاحب ہی کے قول پر فتوی دے ۔ ہاں! اگر مفتی مجتہد ہے، تو اُسے اختیار ہو گا کہ وہ قوت دلیل کی بنیاد پر کسی قول کو ترجیح دے۔ اس تیسری رائے کو جو زیادہ درست کہا گیا ہے، وہ اس بنیاد پر کہ اس کا تعلق مفتی مجہد سے ہے ، اس تیسری راے میں مفتی مجتہد ، مفتی غیر مجتہد کا فرق ہے اس سے پہلی اور دوسری رائے میں تطبیق بھی ہو جاتی ہے، وہ اس طرح کہ جنھوں نے مطلقاً امام صاحب صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کو لینے کی بات کہی ہے ، اُن کی بات کا تعلق مفتی مقلد سے ہے اور جنھوں نے مطلقاً اختیار دیا ہے، ان کے اختیار دینے کا تعلق مفتی مجتہد سے ہے ، اب اس طرح تینوں آراء کے مابین کوئی اختلاف باقی نہیں رہے گا۔ مُلاحظة : اس بحث میں جو بار بار مجید[؟] مفتی“ کا لفظ آیا ہے، اس سے مجتہد مطلق مراد نہیں ؛ بل کہ فی [؟] ر مقید مراد ہے، اس میں ”مجھ[؟] المذہب "مجتهد في المسائل اصحاب تخریج اور اصحاب صحیح و ترجیح ؛ سب ہی شامل ہیں۔ مجتہدین کے تین طبقات ہیں: (۱) مجتہد مطلق مستقل (۲) مجتہد مطلق منتسب (۳) مجتہد فی المذہب تینوں کی تفصیلات فتوی نویسی کے رہنما اصول میں دیکھئے۔
He says that in such a situation the mufti has a choice: he may give fatwa according to whichever opinion he wishes, whether the mufti is a mujtahid or a muqallid. And regarding this, the third opinion which is of the verifiers is that if the mufti is a muqallid, then it is necessary for him to give fatwa according to the statement of Imam Sahib alone. Yes, if the mufti is a mujtahid, then he has the choice to give preference to some opinion based on the strength of evidence. This third opinion which is said to be more correct is on the basis that it relates to the mufti who is a mujtahid. In this third opinion, there is a distinction between the mujtahid mufti and the non-mujtahid mufti. This also brings reconciliation between the first and second opinions, in that those who said to take the statement of Imam Sahib absolutely, their statement relates to the mufti who is a muqallid, and those who gave absolute choice, their giving of choice relates to the mufti who is a mujtahid. Thus, now there will be no difference among the three opinions. Note: In this discussion, the term 'mujtahid mufti' that appears repeatedly does not mean absolute mujtahid; rather it means restricted [mujtahid fil madhhab]. This includes the 'mujtahid fi al-madhhab', 'mujtahid fi al-masa'il', ashab al-takhrij, and ashab al-sahih wa al-tarjih; all are included. There are three classes of mujtahideen: (1) absolute independent mujtahid, (2) absolute affiliated mujtahid, (3) mujtahid within the school. See the details in the guide to fatwa writing.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage addresses the methodological rule for which opinion a mufti should adopt when there are multiple views within the Hanafi school. It presents the third opinion of the muhaqqiqun (verifiers), which distinguishes between a mufti who is a muqallid (follower) and a mufti who is a mujtahid. The muqallid mufti must adhere to the explicit ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa, while the mujtahid mufti has the discretion to weigh evidence and give preference to any opinion, including those of the students. This third opinion reconciles the earlier two absolute views: one that restricted to Imam Abu Hanifa (for muqallids) and one that gave absolute choice (for mujtahids). The author further clarifies that the term 'mujtahid mufti' here does not mean a mujtahid mutlaq (absolute) but rather a mujtahid fi al-madhhab (within the school), which includes various categories like ashab al-takhrij and ashab al-tasheeh. The passage ends by listing the three classes of mujtahideen: mujtahid mutlaq mustaqill (independent absolute), mujtahid mutlaq muntasib (affiliated absolute), and mujtahid fi al-madhhab (within the school).

Key Terms
مفتی مقلد (mufti muqallid): A mufti who follows a particular imam without independent reasoning; must adhere to the imam's clear statement.
مفتی مجتہد (mufti mujtahid): A mufti capable of ijtihad within the school (mujtahid fi al-madhhab); has the authority to prefer any opinion based on evidence.
مجتہد مطلق مستقل (mujtahid mutlaq mustaqill): An independent absolute mujtahid who establishes his own school; not bound by any previous imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third opinion presented, what is the obligation of a muqallid mufti when there are multiple opinions in the school?
A) He may choose any opinion he wishes.
B) He must follow the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa.
C) He must follow the majority opinion.
D) He must refer to the ashab al-tarjih.

Key Takeaway
The mufti's level determines his obligation: muqallid must follow Imam Abu Hanifa; mujtahid may choose based on evidence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Following the Corrections of Ashab al-Tasheeh
Explaining the mufti's reliance on ashab al-tasheeh corrections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two sources of tarjeeh (by dalil and by ashab al-tasheeh) and apply the rule that in the absence of tarjeeh bi al-dalil, the mufti follows the corrected opinion of the ashab al-tasheeh.

Core Idea
When direct ijtihad is absent, fatwa follows the corrections of later Hanafi scholars (ashab al-tasheeh), who may prefer a student's opinion over the Imam's.

This lesson explains the practical fatwa methodology in the post-ijtihad era. The author, through a poetic verse and commentary, tells us that since the ability to weigh evidence (tarjeeh bi al-dalil) is no longer available, the mufti must adhere to the detailed classification (tafsil) established earlier, but with the crucial caveat that the ashab al-tasheeh have corrected and preferred certain opinions, even those of Imam Abu Hanifa's students. This rule shapes how a mufti navigates the dense Hanafi corpus today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling in the verse
The verse states: 'Now there is no tarjeeh by dalil, so only the statement according to the detail [is taken].' Understand that tarjeeh by dalil is absent.
Tarjeeh by dalil is the method of preferring one opinion over another based on direct evidence from Quran and Sunnah, which only a mujtahid mutlaq can perform.
2
Recognize the exception
The verse continues: 'as long as its contrary has not been corrected.' If the ashab al-tasheeh have corrected a contrary opinion, then that corrected opinion is taken.
The exception overrides the default adherence to Imam Abu Hanifa's view.
3
Define the role of ashab al-tasheeh
They are later scholars who identify the sahih (sound) and rajih (preferred) opinions within the school after reviewing all transmissions.
Their work is authoritative for fatwa; they may correct the apparent ruling of the madhhab.
4
Apply the example of Imam Zufar
The passage notes that seventeen of Imam Zufar's opinions were preferred over Imam Abu Hanifa's by the ashab al-tasheeh. This illustrates that a student's view can become mufta bihi.
Imam Zufar was a prominent student of Abu Hanifa; his views are considered in certain cases where the ashab al-tasheeh found them stronger.
5
Formulate the operational rule for fatwa
The mufti must first look for tarjeeh by ashab al-tasheeh; if none, follow the default tafsil (Imam Abu Hanifa for muqallid, etc.).
This ensures the student understands the hierarchy: ashab al-tasheeh's correction overrides the default.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ب سابقہ تفصیل کے مطابق ہی فتویٰ دینا ہے اب فَالُانَ لَا تَرْجِيْحَ بِالدَّلِيلِ فَلَيْسَ إِلَّا الْقَوْلُ بِالتَّفْصِيل مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ خِلافُهُ الْمُصَحَّحَا * فَنَأْخُذُ الَّذِي لَهُمْ قَدْ وَضَحَا فَإِنَّنَا نَرَاهُمُوُ قَدْرَجَحُوا * مَقَالَ بَعْضٍ صَحْبِهِ، وَصَحْحُوا مِنْ ذَاكَ مَا قَدْ رَبَّحُوا لِزُفَرِ * مَقَالَهُ فِي سَبْعَةٍ وَّعَشَر ترجمه : [۳۰] اب ( موجودہ زمانے میں ) دلیل کے ذریعے ترجیح ( والی بات) نہیں رہی، لہذا اب تو سابقہ تفصیل کے مطابق ہی (فتوے کے لیے ) قول کو لیا جائے گا۔ [۳۱] جب تک امام صاحب کے قول کے علاوہ، دوسرے قول کی تصحیح نہ کی گئی ہو، (اگر دوسرے قول کی تصحیح کی گئی ہو تو پھر ایسی صورت میں اُسی قول کو لیں گے جو اہل تشیع کے لیے واضح ہوا ہو ۔ [۳۲] اس لیے کہ ہم اصحاب تصحیح کو دیکھتے ہیں کہ اُنھوں نے ( بعض مرتبہ ) امام صاحب کے بعض شاگردوں کے قول کی تصحیح کی ہے اور اُن کے قول کو راجح قرار دیا ہے۔ [۳۳] ترجیح دیے ہوئے اُن ہی اقوال میں سے امام زفر صلى الله عليه وسلم کے وہ سترہ اقوال ہیں، جن کو اصحاب قبیح[؟] نے (امام صاحب کے اقوال کے مقابلے میں ) ترجیح دی ہے۔
Fatwa is to be given according to the previous detail. Now, there is no preference by evidence, so only the statement according to the detail [is taken], as long as its contrary has not been corrected; so we take that which has become clear to them. Indeed, we see that they have given preference to the statement of some of his Companions and have corrected from that which they have gained profit for Zufar: his statement in seventeen [issues]. Translation: [30] Now (in the present time) there is no preference by evidence, so now the statement is taken only according to the previous detail. [31] As long as the contrary of Imam Sahib's statement has not been corrected (if another statement has been corrected, then in such a case we will take that statement which has become clear to the people of correction). [32] Because we see that the people of correction have (sometimes) corrected the statement of some of Imam Sahib's students and declared their statement to be stronger. [33] Among those given preference, there are seventeen statements of Imam Zufar (may Allah bless him) which the people of correction have preferred over the statements of Imam Sahib.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage sets forth the practical methodology for issuing fatwas in the author's time. It begins by affirming that the current practice is to follow the detailed classification (tafsil) discussed earlier: that a muqallid mufti follows Imam Abu Hanifa, and a mujtahid mufti may choose. However, it adds that since the ability to perform tarjeeh by dalil (preference by direct evidence) is no longer present for most scholars, the reliance is placed on the work of the ashab al-tasheeh (scholars of correction) who have reviewed the school's opinions and identified which ones are sahih (sound) and which are rajih (preferred). The Arabic verse encapsulates this: 'Now there is no tarjeeh by dalil, so nothing remains but adopting the statement according to the detail, unless its opposite has been corrected; so we take that which has become clear to them.' The commentary explains: 'Now, in the present time, the route of preferring by evidence is gone, so the qawl is taken according to the previous detail.' This means that if the mufti is a muqallid, he takes Imam Abu Hanifa's qawl, but if the ashab al-tasheeh have corrected another qawl (i.e., declared it more correct), then that corrected qawl is followed. This is because the ashab al-tasheeh have sometimes preferred the statements of the students (like Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, etc.) over that of Imam Abu Hanifa. A prominent example is Imam Zufar (a student of Abu Hanifa), whose seventeen opinions were preferred over the imam's. Thus, the mufti must be aware of these later corrections and apply them accordingly. This passage emphasizes that the later scholars' tarjeeh (preference) is binding in fatwa because the direct ijtihad capacity has diminished.

Key Terms
اصحاب تصحیح (ashab al-tasheeh): The later Hanafi scholars who examined the transmissions and identified the sound (sahih) and preferred (rajih) opinions within the school.
ترجیح بالدلیل (tarjeeh bi al-dalil): Preferring one opinion over another based on the strength of evidence from Quran and Sunnah.
امام زفر (Imam Zufar): Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a prominent student of Imam Abu Hanifa, whose seventeen opinions were preferred over the imam's by later ashab al-tasheeh.
نفصیل (tafsil): The detailed classification of muftis into muqallid and mujtahid categories, each with a specific rule for adopting qawls.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition does a mufti adopt a ruling from a student (e.g., Imam Zufar) over Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Always, because students are also mujtahidun.
B) When the ashab al-tasheeh have corrected and preferred that ruling.
C) Only if the mufti himself prefers the student's evidence.
D) Never, because the Imam's ruling is always superior.

Key Takeaway
In the absence of tarjeeh by dalil, the mufti must follow the detailed classification unless the ashab al-tasheeh have corrected and preferred a different opinion, which then becomes the operative ruling.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
