Hierarchy of Opinions for Muqallid Mufti and Its Exception
Explains the fixed hierarchy and its exception via mujtahid tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy of opinions for a muqallid mufti and identify the exception when mujtahids in the madhhab have given preference.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti follows a fixed hierarchy unless mujtahids have preferred another opinion.

A mufti who is not a mujtahid must issue fatwas based on the opinions of Hanafi imams, but how does he choose when they differ? This passage lays out a clear hierarchy—starting with Imam Abu Hanifa, then Imam Abu Yusuf, then Imam Muhammad, and so on—but also reveals a crucial exception: later mujtahids within the madhhab may override this order based on evidence or necessity. Understanding this rule is essential for correct fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufti categories
Recognize the two types of mufti: a mujtahid mufti has choice in disputed issues; a muqallid mufti is bound to a hierarchy.
The passage states that today all muftis are muqallids (except as Allah wills).
2
State the default hierarchy
The muqallid mufti must seek opinions in order: first Imam Abu Hanifa, if not found then Imam Abu Yusuf, then Imam Muhammad, then other students step by step.
This hierarchy is based on the chain of transmission and authority within the school.
3
Recognize the exception
If the mujtahids within the madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab) have preferred a different opinion based on strength of evidence, custom, or necessity, the mufti follows that preferred opinion instead of the hierarchy.
This exception prevents rigid adherence to an order that may be weaker in specific cases.
4
Understand the example
The passage cites 20 issues where mujtahids have preferred Imam Zufar's opinion over Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions, showing the exception in practice.
Allama Shami adjusted the count to 20 after removing three objected cases.
5
Apply the rule in practice
When preparing a fatwa, first check the default hierarchy; then check if later mujtahids have expressed a preference; if so, follow their tarjih.
This approach balances authority with effective fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح : ابھی سابقہ اشعار میں یہ بات آئی کہ مختلف فیہ مسائل میں مفتی مجتہد کو اختیار ہوگا اور مفتی کمقلد امام صاحب کے قول پر فتویٰ دینے کا پابند ہوگا۔ اب علامہ شامی یہ فرمارہے ہیں کہ اب کے زمانے میں مجتہد مفتی نہیں رہے، جو ہیں سب مقلد ہیں (الا ماشاء اللہ ) لہذا اب اختیار والی بات بھی نہیں رہے گی، اب تو سابقہ تفصیل کے مطابق ہی فتویٰ دینا ہوگا، یعنی پیش آمدہ مسئلے میں سب سے پہلے امام صاحب صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کو تلاش کیا جائے گا اور اُسی کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا؟ اگر امام صاحب کا قول نہ ملے، تو امام ابو یوسف کے قول کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا ؟ اگر اُن کا بھی قول نہ ہو، تو پھر امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا، اسی طرح درجہ بہ درجہ دوسرے شاگردوں کے قول کو فتوے کے لیے اختیار کیا جائے گا۔ به وقت ضرورت سابقہ تفصیل کے خلاف فتوی دیا جا سکتا ہے ۶۳ ہاں! اگر ہمارے سامنے یہ بات آجائے کہ مجتہدین فی المذہب نے قوتِ دلیل کی بنیاد پر یا عرف وضرورت وغیرہ کی وجہ سے اس ترتیب کے خلاف، مثلاً : امام صاحب کے قول کے ہوتے ہوئے صاحبین کے قول پر فتوی دیا ہے، تو پھر ایسی صورت میں حضرات مجہتدین کے ترجیح دئے ہوئے قول پر فتویٰ دیا جائے گا، اور بالفعل ایسا ہوا بھی ہے کہ حضرات مجتہدین نے کسی وجہ ترجیح کی بنیاد پر ، امام صاحب ہ کے قول کے مقابلے میں دوسرے بعض شاگردوں کے قول کو راجح قرار دیا ہے، اس کی بڑی مثال : مجتہدین فی المذہب کا سترہ مسائل میں امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے قول کو چھوڑ کر ، امام زفر کے قول پر فتویٰ دیتا ہے۔ ، مُلاحظة : سترہ مسائل میں سے تین پر اعتراض ہے کہ یہ امام زفر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہیں۔ اعتراض والے اقوال کو ساقط کر کے علامہ شامی نے تعداد میں تک پہنچائی ہے، ان تمام بیسوں مسائل کو علامہ نے اپنے حاشیے میں منظوم شکل میں ذکر کر دیا ہے۔ (دیکھئے: حاشية ابن عابدين، الطلاق، النفقة، مطلب في فرض النفقة لزوجة الغائب : ۳۳۲٬۳۳۱/۵، ط: زکریا دیوبند)
Explanation: In previous verses it came that in disputed issues, a mujtahid mufti has choice, and a muqallid mufti is bound to give fatwa according to Imam's opinion. Now Allama Shami says that nowadays there are no mujtahid muftis; all are muqallids (except as Allah wills). Therefore the choice is no longer present. Now fatwa must be given according to the previous detail: in an occurring issue, first the statement of Imam [Abu Hanifa] is sought and fatwa is given accordingly; if Imam's statement is not found, then fatwa is given according to Imam Abu Yusuf's statement; if his statement is also not found, then according to Imam Muhammad's statement; similarly, step by step, the statements of other students are adopted for fatwa. At a time of need, fatwa can be given contrary to the previous detail. Page 63 Yes! If it comes before us that the mujtahids within the madhhab, based on strength of evidence or custom and necessity, have given fatwa contrary to this order, e.g., preferring the statements of the two companions over Imam's statement, then in such a case fatwa will be given according to the preferred statement of those mujtahids. And indeed it has happened that the mujtahids, for some preferential reason, have considered the statement of some other student as rajih over Imam's statement. A major example: the mujtahids within the madhhab leaving Imam and the two companions in seventeen issues and giving fatwa according to Imam Zufar's statement. Note: Three of the seventeen issues are objected that they are not specific to Imam Zufar. Removing the objected statements, Allama Shami has brought the count to twenty. Allama has mentioned all these twenty issues in his marginalia in poetic form. (See: Hashiya Ibn Abidin, Talaq, Nafaqa, Matalib fi Fard an-Nafaqa li Zawj al-Ghaib: 5/331-332, Zakaria Deoband publication)
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule: the method a muqallid mufti must follow in issuing fatwas. The author first recalls the distinction between a mujtahid mufti (who has choice in differing issues) and a muqallid mufti (who is bound). Then he states the current reality: there are no longer mujtahid muftis; all are muqallids. Therefore, the muqallid mufti must follow a fixed hierarchy: first seek the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa, if not found then Imam Abu Yusuf, then Imam Muhammad, then the other students in order. However, an exception is made: if the mujtahids within the madhhab (like later scholars who engage in tarjih) have explicitly preferred a different opinion based on strength of evidence, custom, or necessity, then that preferred opinion is followed. He gives the concrete example of twenty issues where the mujtahids have preferred Imam Zufar's opinion over that of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions. This shows that the hierarchy is not absolute; it can be overridden by the collective ijtihad of the school's mujtahids. The passage also notes a discrepancy about the exact number of issues, resolving it to twenty.

Key Terms
مختلف فیہ (mukhtalaf fihi): Issues in which there is disagreement among Hanafi imams
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar within the Hanafi school who is capable of weighing and preferring one opinion over another (tarjih)
ترجیح (tarjih): The process of preferring one scholarly opinion over another based on strength of evidence or practical considerations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a muqallid mufti do if the mujtahids within the madhhab have preferred Imam Zufar's opinion over Imam Abu Hanifa's?
A) He must follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion.
B) He must follow Imam Zufar's opinion.
C) He must remain silent and not give a fatwa.
D) He must choose whichever opinion he prefers.

Key Takeaway
The muqallid mufti follows a fixed hierarchy unless the mujtahids of the madhhab have done tarjih, in which case the preferred opinion is followed.

The Rule When No Narration from Early Scholars Exists
Introduces the rule for when no transmitted ruling exists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that when no riwayah from early Hanafi scholars exists, the mufti must consult the next level of the fatwa hierarchy, and identify the correct next step.

Core Idea
No riwayah from mutaqaddimin means the mufti must follow the hierarchy, not his own opinion.

This verse from the poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' presents a key principle in Hanafi fatwa methodology. It states a condition: when a new issue arises and no transmitted ruling from the early scholars is found. The verse itself only sets up the condition; the remedy lies in the established hierarchy of sources (Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, later fatwas). Understanding this principle is essential for a mufti to avoid arbitrary judgments.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Condition
Identify that the verse states a conditional: 'When there is no narration from our scholars...'. Focus on the word 'lam tujad' (is not found).
The condition is the absence of riwayah from the early scholars (mutaqaddimin).
2
Identify the Subject
The verse specifies 'our scholars, those of recitation' – referring to the early Hanafi authorities whose transmitted rulings form the core of the madhhab.
This excludes later scholars and personal opinion.
3
Understand the Implied Response
The verse is a truncated conditional; it does not state the consequent. The full rule, known from Rasm al-Mufti, is that the mufti must then turn to the next tier: Nawadir (rare transmissions), then fatwas of later scholars (muta'akhkhirin).
The hierarchy is: Zahir al-Riwayah → Nawadir → Later fatwas → Ijtihad within the madhhab.
4
Memorize as an Anchor
This verse serves as a memorization anchor for the principle: when riwayah is absent, do not jump to personal opinion; follow the prepared hierarchy.
This is a foundational rule in mufti training.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی مسئلے میں متقدمین کی روایت نہ ہو تو ..؟ ۳۴ ثُمَّ إِذَا لَمْ تُوجَدِ الرِّوَايَهُ * عَنْ عُلَمَائِنَا ذَوِي القِرَايَهُ
When there is no narration from our scholars of recitation (early scholars) in a matter...? 34 Then, if there is no narration from our scholars, those of high recitation.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents a new verse (number 34) from the poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti'. It states a condition: when a particular issue arises and no narration (i.e., transmitted ruling) is found from the early Hanafi scholars—referred to as 'our scholars, those of recitation'—then the mufti must have a method to determine the ruling. The poem leaves the answer implied, but the full commentary (not included here) would explain what to do next, such as ijtihad or referring to other sources. This verse serves as a principle for dealing with novel issues not covered in transmitted texts.

Key Terms
متقدمین (mutaqaddimin): The early Hanafi scholars, especially the founding imams and their direct students
روایت (riwayah): A transmitted ruling or statement from a Hanafi scholar

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The mufti must perform ijtihad.
B) The mufti must consult early scholars.
C) It only states the condition without giving the answer.
D) The mufti may issue fatwa based on his opinion.

Key Takeaway
When no transmitted ruling from early Hanafi scholars exists, the mufti must seek guidance from the next level of the fatwa hierarchy, not from personal opinion.

Fatwa Hierarchy When No Early Transmission Exists
Establishing the fatwa hierarchy when no early transmission exists and later scholars differ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy: state the rule for preferring the majority view among later scholars when no early transmission exists, and identify when a mufti must resort to ijtihad.

Core Idea
When early transmissions are absent, the later majority opinion governs the fatwa.

In Hanafi iftaa, the mufti must know which opinion to give when the early masters (mutaqaddimūn) left no recorded ruling. This lesson explains the hierarchy: first confirm that no early transmission exists, then adopt the majority view among later mujtahids (muta'akhkhirūn). It also warns of the grave responsibility of personal ijtihad when even later scholars have no recorded position.

Guided Path
1
Identify absence of early transmission
Determine that there is no known ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, or Zufar on the issue. If such a ruling exists, it takes precedence and the later majority rule does not apply.
The early masters are the foundational authorities of the madhhab.
2
Locate disagreement among later scholars
List the opinions of later Hanafi jurists such as al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani, Abu Ja'far al-Thahiri, and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi.
These later scholars engage in tarjih (preference) among existing transmissions.
3
Apply the majority rule
Count the opinions. The view held by the majority of these later scholars is given precedence (yurabbah).
This is the default rule when no early transmission exists.
4
Check for overriding factors
If a later mujtahid (e.g., al-Tahawi) explicitly prefers a minority view based on stronger evidence or custom, that overriding tarjih may be followed instead of the simple majority.
The earlier part of the passage notes that mujtahidun fi al-madhhab may depart from the standard order based on strength of evidence.
5
Resort to ijtihad with taqwa
If even the later scholars have no recorded statement, the mufti must exercise ijtihad—serious reasoning—while fearing Allah. Only the reckless would give rulings without such care.
This underscores the gravity of fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(دیکھئے: حاشية ابن عابدين، الطلاق، النفقة، مطلب في فرض النفقة لزوجة الغائب : ۳۳۲٬۳۳۱/۵، ط: زکریا دیوبند)
کسی مسئلے میں متقدمین کی روایت نہ ہو تو ..؟
۳۴ ثُمَّ إِذَا لَمْ تُوجَدِ الرِّوَايَهُ * عَنْ عُلَمَائِنَا ذَوِي القِرَايَهُ
۳۵ وَاخْتَلَفَ الَّذِينَ قَدْ تَأَخَّرُوا * يُرَبَّحُ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْأَكْثَرُ
٣٦ مِثْلُ الطَّحَاوِي وَأَبِي حَفْصِ الكَبِيرُ * وَأَبَوَيْ جَعْفَرِ وَاللَّيثِ الشَّهِيرُ
٣٧ وَحَيْثُ لَمْ تُوجَدُ لِهؤُلاء * مَقَالَةٌ ، وَاحْتِيجَ لِلِافْتَاء فَلْيَنْظُرِ الْمُفْتِي بِجِدٍ وَّاجْتِهَادُ * وَلْيَخْشَ بَطْشَ رَبِّهِ يَوْمَ الْمَعَادُ
۳۹ فَلَيْسَ يَجُسُرُ عَلَى الْأَحْكَام * سِوى شَقِي خَاسِرِ الْمَرَام
At time of necessity, a fatwa can be given contrary to the previous detail. Yes! If it comes to our knowledge that the mujtahidun fi al-madhhab (mujtahids within the madhhab) have given fatwa contrary to this order based on strength of evidence or due to custom and necessity, for example, preferring the saying of the Sahibayn over Imam Sahib's saying, then in such a case fatwa will be given on the saying preferred by the mujtahids. And indeed this has happened: the mujtahids have preferred the saying of some other disciples over the saying of Imam Sahib based on some reason of preference. A major example: the mujtahidun fi al-madhhab give fatwa on Imam Zufar's saying in seventeen issues, leaving aside the sayings of Imam Sahib and the Sahibayn. Note: Three of the seventeen issues are objected to that they are not specific to Imam Zufar. Removing the objected sayings, Allama Shami has brought the number to twenty. All these twenty issues Allama has mentioned in his gloss in poetic form. (See: Hashiya Ibn Abidin, al-Talaq, al-Nafaqa, Matlab fi Fard al-Nafaqa li Zawjat al-Gha'ib: 331-332/5, Dar Zakariya Deoband) If there is no transmission from our early scholars in a matter? 34. Then when there is no transmission from our scholars of recitation (i.e., the early masters), 35. And the later scholars have differed, then the saying upon which the majority is will be given precedence. 36. Like al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, and the two Abu Ja'far (i.e., Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani and Abu Ja'far al-Thahiri) and the famous al-Layth (i.e., Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi). 37. And where there is no statement for these (scholars) and fatwa is needed, then let the mufti look with seriousness and ijtihad, and let him fear the grasp of his Lord on the Day of Return. 39. For none dares to (give) rulings except a wretched loser of the goal.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage belongs to the field of Rasm al-Mufti, dealing with the hierarchy of fatwa when transmitted rulings from the early Hanafi masters (متقدمین) are absent. The author first notes that mujtahidun fi al-madhhab (later jurists qualified to weigh evidences within the madhhab) may depart from the standard order of preference (Imam Abu Hanifa first, then Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) if there is stronger evidence or custom. He gives the example of Imam Zufar's opinion being preferred in seventeen (later corrected to twenty) issues over Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Then he presents a poetic maxim: When no transmission from early scholars exists, and later scholars differ, the view of the majority among them is to be preferred. Key later authorities mentioned: Imam al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH), Abu Hafs al-Kabir (d. 264 AH), Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani (d. 362 AH), Abu Ja'far al-Thahiri (d. 320 AH), and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi (d. 373 AH). If even these later masters have no recorded opinion, the mufti must engage in ijtihad—serious reasoning—while fearing Allah, as giving rulings is a grave responsibility that only the reckless undertake lightly. This establishes a clear procedural hierarchy: (1) transmitted rulings of the early masters, (2) preferred opinions of later mujtahids, (3) majority view among later scholars if no single preferred view, (4) personal ijtihad with taqwa.

Key Terms
متقدمین (mutaqaddimūn): The early Hanafi masters, particularly Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Zufar, whose transmitted rulings form the foundation of the madhhab.
متاخرین (muta'akhkhirūn): Later Hanafi jurists after the early masters, such as al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, and Abu al-Layth, who engaged in tarjih (preference) among the existing transmissions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when should a mufti prefer the opinion of the majority among later Hanafi scholars?
A) Always, because later scholars are more knowledgeable.
B) Only when there is no transmission from the early Hanafi masters (mutaqaddimūn) on the issue.
C) Only when Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is unknown.
D) Only when the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy, when no early transmission exists, the mufti follows the majority opinion of later scholars; if even that is absent, he must engage in ijtihad with taqwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
7 min
When Later Hanafi Jurists Differ: Following the Majority
Versified rasm al-mufti rule with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy when no early imam's narration exists, identify when to follow the majority of later scholars, and state the conditions for permissible ijtihad.

Core Idea
When no early imam's ruling exists, the mufti follows the majority of prominent later jurists; if none, ijtihad with fear.

This passage from 'Aun al-Mughni' lays down the rasm al-mufti rule for cases where no direct transmission from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, or Muhammad is available. It specifies that if later scholars (mutā'akhkhirūn) have a unanimous opinion, that is binding; if they differ, the mufti must give preference (tarjīḥ) to the majority among the well-known later jurists like al-Ṭaḥāwī, Abū Ḥafṣ al-Kabīr, Abū Ja‘far, and Abū al-Layth. Only when no transmitted opinion at all exists may the mufti engage in ijtihād, and even then with utmost caution and fear of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Confirm absence of early imam's narration
The mufti must first verify that none of the early mujtahid imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) have a recorded statement on the issue. This is the foundation of the hierarchy.
If an early imam's ruling is found, it must be followed without deviation.
2
Check for later scholars' agreement
If the later scholars (mutā'akhkhirūn) all agree on a ruling, their consensus is binding. If they differ, proceed to the next step.
Unanimity among later scholars carries the same authority as a early imam's ruling in this context.
3
Identify the majority among prominent later scholars
When later scholars differ, the mufti must count the opinions of the major figures (e.g., al-Ṭaḥāwī, Abū Ḥafṣ, etc.) and follow the ruling supported by the majority.
The mufti must have knowledge of the positions of these specific scholars.
4
Consider ijtihad only as last resort
If no statement exists from any later scholar (neither unanimous nor individual), the mufti may perform ijtihad, exerting his scholarly effort with sincerity and fear of Allah.
This is a heavy responsibility; only the reckless issue rulings without following this hierarchy.
5
Apply the ethical warning
The passage warns that only a wretched person dares to issue rulings without proper authority. The mufti must always be mindful of his accountability before Allah.
This underscores the gravity of fatwa and the need for scholarly humility.

Source Text

عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي ۶۴ ۳۵ وَاخْتَلَفَ الَّذِينَ قَدْ تَأَخَّرُوا * يُرَبَّحُ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْأَكْثَرُ ٣٦ مِثْلُ الطَّحَاوِي وَأَبِي حَفْصِ الكَبِيرُ * وَأَبَوَيْ جَعْفَرِ وَاللَّيثِ الشَّهِيرُ ٣٧ وَحَيْثُ لَمْ تُوجَدُ لِهؤُلاء * مَقَالَةٌ ، وَاحْتِيجَ لِلِافْتَاء فَلْيَنْظُرِ الْمُفْتِي بِجِدٍ وَّاجْتِهَادُ * وَلْيَخْشَ بَطْشَ رَبِّهِ يَوْمَ الْمَعَادُ ۳۹ فَلَيْسَ يَجُسُرُ عَلَى الْأَحْكَام * سِوى شَقِي خَاسِرِ الْمَرَام ترجمة : [۳۴] پھر جب علم و بصیرت رکھنے والے ہمارے علماء سے (کسی مسئلے میں ) کوئی روایت نہ ہو۔ [۳۵] اور بعد کے علماء کے مابین اختلاف ہو جائے، تو ایسی صورت میں اکثر علماء کے اختیار کردہ قول کو ترجیح ہوگی۔ [۳۶] مثال کے طور پر امام طحاوی ہیں ، ابوحفص کبیر ہیں، اسی طرح امام ابو جعفر اور مشہور امام ابواللیث مال وغیرہ ہیں۔ (۳۷) اور جہاں کہیں ان حضرات کا بھی کوئی قول نہ ہو اور فتوی دینے کی ضرورت سامنے ہو۔ [۳۸] تو پھر ایسی صورت میں مفتی کو چاہیے کہ وہ (پیش آمدہ مسئلے میں ) خوب غور وفکر سے کام لے اور ساتھ ہی ساتھ آخرت میں اللہ کے مواخذے سے بھی ڈرتا رہے۔ [۳۹] اس لیے کہ احکام شرعیہ کے بیان کرنے (فتوی دینے ) میں بد بخت و نا مراد ہی جری و دلیر بنتا ہے۔
عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي شرح : ماقبل میں یہ بات آچکی کہ جب کسی مسئلے میں ہمارے ائمہ مجتہدین کا قول ہوگا، تو درجہ بہ درجہ اُن ہی کے قول کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا، اس سے عدول جائز نہیں، اب یہاں سے علامہ شامی یہ بیان فرما ر ہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی مسئلے میں ہمارے ائمہ مجتہدین کی کوئی روایت نہ ہو ؛ البتہ متأخرین نے اس مسئلے میں کلام کیا ہو اور وہ سب کسی ایک بات متفق ہوں ، تو اُن متأخرین کے متفقہ قول کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا۔ متاخرین میں اختلاف ہونے کی صورت کا حکم یہاں سے علامہ یہ ضابطہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ پیش آمدہ مسئلے میں اگر متآخرین کے مابین اختلاف ہو، تو پھر ایسی صورت میں اکابر فقہائے متآخرین مثلاً امام طحاوی، امام ابو حفص کبیر، امام ابو جعفر اور امام ابواللیث وغیرہ کی اکثریت جس حکم کی طرف مائل ہوگی ، اُسی پر فتوی دیا جائے گا۔ کسی مسئلے میں اگر متقدمین و متاخرین میں سے کسی کا کوئی قول نہ ہو؟ ،، اس کے بعد ” وحيث لم توجد ... اہ سے علامہ یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی مسئلے میں امام صاحب یا دیگر اصحاب مذهب، اسی طرح مشائخ متقدمین و متاخرین میں سے کسی سے کوئی صراحت منقول نہ ہو، تو بالغ نظر مفتی اپنے مقام و منصب اور خوف وخشیت خداوندی کو پیش نظر رکھتے ہوئے ، پیش آمدہ مسئلے میں صحیح جواب تک رسائی کے لیے اپنی پوری علمی طاقت و کوشش صرف کر دے، اس سلسلے کردے،
Aun al-Mughni fi Hall 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. 64. 35: And when those who came later differed, the one with the majority (opinion) is given preference. 36: Such as al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far, and the famous al-Layth. 37: And when no statement exists from these, and there is need for fatwa, 38: Then let the mufti look with seriousness and ijtihad, and fear the might of his Lord on the Day of Return. 39: For no one dares to (issue) rulings except a wretched, failed one. Translation: [34] When there is no narration from our knowledgeable scholars regarding a matter. [35] And when the later scholars differ, then in such a case the opinion adopted by the majority of scholars shall be given preference. [36] For example, Imam al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, likewise Imam Abu Ja'far and the famous Imam Abu al-Layth, etc. [37] And when there is no saying from these gentlemen either, and there is need to give a fatwa, [38] Then in such a case the mufti should ponder and reflect deeply on the presented matter, and also fear Allah's accountability in the Hereafter. [39] Because only an unlucky and failed person becomes bold and daring in explaining Islamic rulings (giving fatwa). 
Aun al-Mughni fi Hall 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. Commentary: It has been previously mentioned that when we have a saying of our mujtahid imams regarding a matter, fatwa is given according to their saying, rank by rank, and it is not permissible to deviate from it. Now here 'Allamah Shami states that if there is no narration from our mujtahid imams concerning a matter, but the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) have spoken about it and they all agree on one point, then fatwa will be given according to their unanimous opinion. As for the case when there is difference among the later scholars: From here, 'Allamah states this rule: if there is difference among the later scholars regarding a presented issue, then among the great later jurists such as Imam Tahawi, Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Imam Abu Ja'far, and Imam Abu al-Layth, etc., the ruling towards which the majority inclines will be the one on which fatwa is given. [Question: What if there is no saying from either the earlier or later scholars?] After this, from 'And where there is no statement...' 'Allamah states that if there is no explicit statement transmitted from Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa) or other companions of the madhhab, nor from the early and later shuyukh, then the mature mufti, keeping in view his position and the fear of Allah, should exert all his scholarly power and effort to reach the correct answer in the presented issue.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule (methodological rule) for issuing fatwas in the Hanafi school. It outlines the hierarchy a mufti must follow when no explicit narration from the early mujtahid imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is found. The author, Ibn 'Abidin (sharh by 'Allamah Shami), explains that if the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) agree, their unanimous opinion is followed. If they differ, the opinion of the majority among the prominent later scholars—such as Imam al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi—is given preference. If none of these have any transmitted statement, the mufti must engage in ijtihad (reasoned effort) with sincerity and fear of Allah, as only a reckless person would issue rulings without such care. This rule ensures that fatwas are grounded in the school's transmitted authority while allowing for ijtihad when necessary.

Key Terms
متأخرون (muta'akhkhirūn): Later Hanafi jurists after the period of the early mujtahid imams (like Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). They include figures like al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, etc.
ترجيح (tarjīḥ): Giving preference to one opinion over another, here based on majority of the later scholars.
اجتهاد (ijtihād): Independent legal reasoning by a mufti when no transmitted opinion from earlier or later scholars exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what should a Hanafi mufti do when later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) disagree on a matter and no earlier imam's narration exists?
A) Follow the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa only.
B) Follow the opinion of the majority among prominent later scholars like al-Tahawi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir.
C) Choose the opinion that is easiest for the people.
D) Perform ijtihad immediately without considering later scholars.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufti must follow a strict hierarchy: first early imams, then later scholars' consensus or majority, and only then his own ijtihad with fear of Allah.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Hierarchy of Fatwa Sources in the Hanafi Madhhab: From Imams to Muta'akhkhirun to Individual Ijtihad
Hierarchical fatwa source rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchical structure of Hanafi fatwa sources to determine which opinion is mufta bihi when no direct ruling from the founding imams exists.

Core Idea
When the imams are silent: first later scholars' consensus, then their majority, then ijtihad or referral.

In Hanafi usul al-iftaa, a mufti must follow a strict hierarchy of sources. This lesson explains the procedure when no direct ruling from the founding mujtahids exists: turn to the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun), then the senior late jurists, then use ijtihad if capable, or refer the questioner. This passage from 'Aun al-Mughni' codifies these rules and warns against careless reliance on internet fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the highest available source
First check if there is a direct ruling from any of the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). If present, it is binding. If not, proceed.
2
Check for consensus of later scholars
If all later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) agree on a ruling, that consensus is binding. The mufti must follow it.
3
Check for majority among senior late jurists
If later scholars disagree, follow the majority opinion of the senior late jurists like Imam Tahawi, Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Imam Abu Ja'far, and Imam Abu al-Layth.
4
Determine the mufti's competence
If no explicit statement exists from any scholar, assess if the mufti is 'baligh nazar'. If yes, he must exert full effort to derive the ruling. If not, he must refer the questioner to a more qualified mufti or seek the answer from him.
5
Apply the hierarchy with modern caution
Be aware of the danger of blindly copying fatwas from the internet without considering context. Every fatwa must account for time, place, and circumstances.

Source Text

عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي
شرح : ماقبل میں یہ بات آچکی کہ جب کسی مسئلے میں ہمارے ائمہ مجتہدین کا قول ہوگا، تو درجہ بہ درجہ اُن ہی کے قول کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا، اس سے عدول جائز نہیں، اب یہاں سے علامہ شامی یہ بیان فرما ر ہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی مسئلے میں ہمارے ائمہ مجتہدین کی کوئی روایت نہ ہو ؛ البتہ متأخرین نے اس مسئلے میں کلام کیا ہو اور وہ سب کسی ایک بات متفق ہوں ، تو اُن متأخرین کے متفقہ قول کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا۔
متاخرین میں اختلاف ہونے کی صورت کا حکم یہاں سے علامہ یہ ضابطہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ پیش آمدہ مسئلے میں اگر متآخرین کے مابین اختلاف ہو، تو پھر ایسی صورت میں اکابر فقہائے متآخرین مثلاً امام طحاوی، امام ابو حفص کبیر، امام ابو جعفر اور امام ابواللیث وغیرہ کی اکثریت جس حکم کی طرف مائل ہوگی ، اُسی پر فتوی دیا جائے گا۔
کسی مسئلے میں اگر متقدمین و متاخرین میں سے کسی کا کوئی قول نہ ہو؟
،،
اس کے بعد ” وحيث لم توجد ... اہ سے علامہ یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی مسئلے میں امام صاحب یا دیگر اصحاب مذهب، اسی طرح مشائخ متقدمین و متاخرین میں سے کسی سے کوئی صراحت منقول نہ ہو، تو بالغ نظر مفتی اپنے مقام و منصب اور خوف وخشیت خداوندی کو پیش نظر رکھتے ہوئے ، پیش آمدہ مسئلے میں صحیح جواب تک رسائی کے لیے اپنی پوری علمی طاقت و کوشش صرف کر دے، اس سلسلے میں معمولی سی بھی غفلت نہ برتے ؛ تا کہ صحیح طریقے سے اپنی ذمے داری سے عہدہ بر آ ہو سکے اور اگر مفتی بالغ نظر نہیں، اُس کے اندر اتنی صلاحیت نہیں کہ محنت و کوشش کے نتیجے میں درست جواب تک پہنچ سکے تو پھر اس کے لیے یہی بہتر ہے کہ وہ اپنے سے بڑے مفتی کی طرف مستفتی (سائل ) کو بھیج دے یا اپنے سے بڑے مفتی سے خود جواب معلوم کر کے مستفتی کو جواب بھی بتائے اور یہ بھی بتادے کہ یہ جواب فلاں مفتی صاحب سے میں نے معلوم کیا ہے، اندازے سے بے سوچے سمجھے جواب دینا؛ یہ نہایت ہی خطرناک بات ہے، اللہ پاک پر بہتان ہے؛ کیوں کہ احکام شرع کے بیان کرنے میں مفتی اللہ پاک کا نائب ہوتا ہے۔ ایک خطر ناک بات
آج کل بعض کمزور استعداد والے مفتی صاحبان ؛ بل کہ بعض غیر مفتی حضرات بھی تحقیق اور غور و خوض کے بغیر محض انٹرنیٹ کی مدد سے لوگوں کو مسئلہ بتاتے رہتے ہیں ، یہ نہایت ہی خطرناک صورت ہے، کوئی بھی فتوی صورتِ مسئولہ کا جواب ہوتا ہے؛ وقت، حالات ( کبھی شخص کبھی عمومی ) وغیرہ چیزوں کو سامنے رکھ کر جواب دیا جاتا ہے۔ یہ ضروری نہیں کہ اس وقت بھی بالکل وہی صورت حال ہو ، جو اس فتوے کے تحریر کیے جانے کے وقت تھی ، ظاہر ہے ایسی صورت میں وہ فتوی اس صورت حال کے مطابق درست نہیں ہوگا ؛ لہذا جو لوگ اس طرح کر رہے ہیں، اُن کے لیے ایسے عمل سے احتراز لازم و ضروری ہے!

نوا ہم ضابطے
وَههُنَا ضَوَابِطُ مُحَرَّرَهُ * غَدَتْ لَدَى أَهْلِ النُّهَى مُقَرَّرَهُ
Awn al-Mughni fi Hall 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti
Explanation: Previously it was mentioned that when there is a saying of our mujtahid imams in a matter, then fatwa is given according to their saying step by step, and deviating from it is not permissible. Now from here, Allama Shami is explaining that if there is no narration from our mujtahid imams in a matter, but later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) have spoken about this matter and all agree on one thing, then fatwa will be given according to their agreed-upon saying.
The ruling in case of disagreement among the later scholars: From here, Allama is stating this rule that if in the occurring matter there is disagreement among the later scholars, then in such a case, fatwa will be given according to the ruling toward which the majority of the senior later jurists, such as Imam Tahawi, Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Imam Abu Ja'far, and Imam Abu al-Layth etc., incline.
What if there is no saying from either the early or later scholars in a matter?
Then after that, from "Wa haythu lam tujad..." Allama is explaining that if there is no explicit statement transmitted from Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa) or other companions of the madhhab, similarly from the early and later scholars, then a mature mufti, keeping in view his position and the fear of God, should exert all his intellectual power and effort to reach the correct answer in the occurring matter, and should not show any negligence in this matter, so that he may fulfill his responsibility properly. And if the mufti is not mature (baligh nazar), if he does not have the capability to reach the correct answer through effort and exertion, then it is better for him to refer the questioner (sa'il) to a greater mufti, or himself find out the answer from a greater mufti and inform the questioner, also mentioning that he has found this answer from such-and-such mufti. Giving an answer based on guesswork without thinking is extremely dangerous; it is slander against Allah the Pure, because in explaining the rulings of Shari'ah, the mufti is the deputy of Allah the Pure. A dangerous matter:
Nowadays, some muftis of weak ability, rather some non-muftis, without research and deliberation, merely with the help of the internet, keep telling people rulings. This is an extremely dangerous situation. Any fatwa is an answer to the specific situation; it is given keeping in view time, circumstances (sometimes individual, sometimes general), and other things. It is not necessary that the same situation exists now as existed at the time of writing that fatwa. Obviously, in such a case, that fatwa will not be correct according to the current situation. Therefore, it is necessary and essential for those who are doing this to refrain from such practice!
40
New rules:
And here are established rules * that have been settled among people of understanding.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage from 'Aun al-Mughni' expounds the hierarchy of sources for fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab when there is no direct ruling from the founding imams. It begins by reiterating the foundational principle: when a saying from the mujtahid imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, etc.) exists on a matter, the mufti must follow it and cannot deviate. Then it addresses scenarios where no such direct narration exists. First, if later scholars (muta'akhkhirun, such as those from the 4th-6th centuries) have unanimously agreed upon a ruling, their consensus is binding and must be followed. Second, if the later scholars themselves differ, the mufti must follow the majority opinion of the senior later jurists, specifically naming Imam Tahawi, Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Imam Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani, and Imam Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi as examples. Third, if neither the early nor later scholars have any explicit statement on the matter, then a mufti who is 'baligh nazar' (possessing mature ijtihad) must exert his utmost effort to derive the correct ruling, carefully applying the principles of the madhhab. If he lacks such capability, he must refer the questioner to a more qualified mufti or learn the answer from him, crediting the source. The passage strongly condemns giving fatwa without proper knowledge, especially by relying on internet fatwas without considering the specific context (time, place, circumstances). It warns that such practice is slander against Allah, as the mufti acts as His deputy. The passage concludes with a couplet emphasizing that there are established rules (dawabit) for these matters. This serves as a critical guideline for muftis to maintain responsibility and adhere to the methodological hierarchy of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
متأخرون (muta'akhkhirun): Later Hanafi scholars after the time of the founding mujtahid imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). They typically span from the 4th century onwards. Their consensus is binding when no earlier text is found.
متقدمون (mutaqaddimun): Early Hanafi scholars, primarily the founding imams and their immediate students (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, Zufar, etc.).
بالغ نظر (baligh nazar): A mufti who possesses mature insight and the capability to engage in ijtihad within the madhhab, able to derive rulings from principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a mufti do if there is no ruling from the mujtahid imams and later scholars unanimously agree on a specific ruling?
A) The mufti may follow his own opinion.
B) The mufti must follow the unanimous ruling of the later scholars.
C) The mufti should refer the questioner to another scholar.
D) The mufti must follow the majority of the later scholars even if they agree.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must follow a strict hierarchy: first the imams, then the later scholars' consensus, then their majority, then ijtihad or referral.

Rule of Preference in Ibadat
First principle: in ibadat, Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is preferred absolutely.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is given preference in matters of worship and identify the exception when a contrary transmission from the Imam himself is established.

Core Idea
In worship, follow Imam Abu Hanifa's view absolutely, unless he himself preferred otherwise.

The first principle of tarjih (preference) established in Rasm al-Mufti is that in all matters of worship, the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is given absolute preference over that of his students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This is a foundational rule for muftis following the Hanafi school. The exception is if there is a valid transmission from the Imam himself that takes the other view, then that view is to be followed. This ensures consistency and authority in rulings related to ibadat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the domain
Confirm that the case you are dealing with is a matter of 'ibadat (worship). The rule applies specifically to worship, not to other areas like judiciary or inheritance.
Worship includes prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj, and other acts of devotion.
2
Identify the opinion holder
Determine which statement is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa (al-Imam). In Hanafi texts, 'al-Imam' refers to Abu Hanifa unless otherwise specified.
Note: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad are referred to as 'al-Sahibayn' or by name.
3
Apply the principle
Give preference to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion over that of his students without any further condition. This is the default rule.
The principle is 'mutlaqan' (absolutely).
4
Check for the exception
Investigate whether there is a valid transmission (riwayah sahihah) from Imam Abu Hanifa himself indicating that he adopted the opposing view. If such a transmission exists, then that other view is to be followed.
The exception is stated: 'ma lam tasih anhu riwayatun biha al-ghayr akhadh'.

As long as the other is not verified by wording, the preferable is that which is explicitly stated. Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
Preference of Imam's Opinion in Ibadat
Rasm rule on preferring Imam Abu Hanifa in ibadat absolutely unless student's narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm al-mufti rule for preferring Imam Abu Hanifa in ibadat and identify the exception when a student's narration is authenticated.

Core Idea
In worship matters, the Imam's view rules absolutely — unless a direct transmission from him supports a student's position.

This lesson presents a foundational rasm al-mufti rule governing the hierarchy of opinions within the Hanafi school when it comes to matters of worship (ibadat). The rule states a clear preference for Imam Abu Hanifa's view, but it also acknowledges an important exception: if a student of the Imam has based his opinion on an authentic narration (riwaya) from the Imam himself, then that student's view is actually the Imam's own transmitted position and thus takes precedence. Understanding this rule is essential for a mufti to issue correct fatwas in ibadat, avoiding the common pitfall of mechanically preferring the Imam's general opinion over a specific transmitted narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the domain
Recognize that this rule applies to all chapters of worship (ibadat), not to muamalat or other fiqh areas.
The rule is domain-specific; other areas have different tarjih principles.
2
State the general rule
The general rule is that in ibadat, the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is preferred absolutely (mutlaqan) over the opinions of his students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
This reflects the principle that the Imam is the founder and his methodology is primary in worship.
3
Identify the exception
The exception occurs when a student's opinion is based on a narration (riwaya) from Imam Abu Hanifa that the student has adopted. In that case, the student's view is preferred because it is effectively the Imam's own transmitted view.
The condition is that the narration must be authentic (tahih) from the Imam.
4
Examine the example
The passage provides an example: the case of tayammum for one who puts dates into water. According to the narration, the student's ruling on this matter is preferred over the Imam's general position.
This example illustrates how the exception operates in practice.
5
Understand the rationale
The exception exists because the student's opinion is not truly independent but is a transmission of the Imam's own teaching. The riwaya carries the authority of the Imam himself.
Thus, the rule remains consistent: the Imam's view is always preferred, but the riwaya is actually his view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage states a foundational rasm al-mufti rule: in matters of worship (ibadat), the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is given precedence over that of his students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, without any qualification. An exception exists: if a riwaya (narration) from Imam Abu Hanifa is authenticated that a student adopted, then that student's view is acted upon. The example given is the case of tayammum for a person who puts dates into water (a well-known issue in the Hanafi school where Abu Hanifa's narration on the matter leads to a student's opinion being preferred). This rule underscores that even in the domain where the Imam's opinion generally dominates, transmitted exceptions are honored.

Key Terms
الإمام (al-Imam): Imam Abu Hanifa, the founder of the Hanafi school
الغير (al-ghayr): The other, i.e., a student of the Imam (Abu Yusuf or Muhammad)
رواية (riwaya): A transmitted narration from Imam Abu Hanifa

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Preference of Abu Yusuf in Qada Matters
Rasm al-mufti rule on preferring Abu Yusuf in qada branches

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'Preference of Abu Yusuf in qada matters' to identify which opinion to give fatwa on in judicial branches.

Core Idea
In qada-related fiqh branches, the mufti must prefer Abu Yusuf's opinion due to his judicial expertise.

The Hanafi school assigns hierarchical preferences in different domains. This lesson introduces a key qawida from Rasm al-Mufti: for all issues pertaining to judicial matters (qada), the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is chosen. Understanding when and why this preference applies is essential for a mufti issuing fatwas in litigation-related cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the domain of the branch
Determine whether the given fiqh issue is related to qada (judicial matters, court proceedings, litigation).
Qada includes evidence, court procedures, judge's rulings, etc.
2
Recall the rule for qada
If the branch is qada-related, the mufta bihi is the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf.
This is a domain-specific tarjih rule.
3
Apply the rule to the issue
When issuing a fatwa, cite Abu Yusuf's view as the operative position for that qada branch.
Do not default to the general preference of Abu Hanifa.
4
Distinguish from other domains
For ibadat, prefer Abu Hanifa; for dhawi al-arham, prefer Muhammad. This rule applies only to qada.
Overgeneralizing is a common mistake.

Preference of Muhammad in Dhawi al-Arham
Rasm rule on preferring Muhammad in inheritance of distant relatives

Learning Objective

Core Idea
In inheritance of distant relatives, Hanafi fatwa follows Muhammad.

The Hanafi school has specific rules for determining which imam's opinion is preferred in different areas of fiqh. One such rule governs the inheritance of dhawi al-arham — blood relatives who are not Quranic heirs. This lesson explains that in these matters, the opinion of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Recognize the statement as a rasm al-mufti rule that specifies which imam's opinion to follow in a particular area.
2
Define dhawi al-arham
Understand that dhawi al-arham are blood relatives who are not entitled to fixed shares in inheritance, such as cousins, uncles, and nephews.
They are distinct from ashhab al-faraid (Quranic heirs).
3
Identify the preferred imam
The rule states that the opinion of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani is to be followed in all issues concerning dhawi al-arham.
Muhammad's works, especially the Zahir al-Riwayah, are the most comprehensive sources for inheritance law.
4
Note the scope and exceptions
This rule applies only to dhawi al-arham, not to all inheritance matters. For Quranic heirs (ashhab al-faraid), other rules may apply.
Common error: extending this rule to all inheritance cases.
5
Connect to other rasm rules
Compare with parallel rules: in ibadat, the Imam's opinion is preferred; in qada, Abu Yusuf's opinion is preferred.
These rules together form the hierarchy of preference in Hanafi fatwa.

The Rule of Zahir al-Riwayah Priority
Rule on preferring zahir al-riwayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that zahir al-riwayah is not abandoned for a contrary narration and apply it to determine the correct fatwa hierarchy.

Core Idea
Zahir al-riwayah is the default; do not abandon it without strong justification.

This passage is a foundational principle from the Rasm al-Mufti literature. It establishes that the widely transmitted narrations (zahir al-riwayah) are the primary source for fatwa, and a mufti should not deviate from them in favor of a contrary but less reliable narration (ghayr zahir). Understanding this rule is essential for maintaining consistency and authority in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Read the verse and state that the zahir al-riwayah is not to be abandoned for a contrary narration.
2
Understand the scope
Recognize that this applies whenever a zahir riwayah contradicts a non-zahir riwayah.
The rule does not reject non-zahir narrations entirely; it sets a priority.
3
Recognize the exception
Note that the rule allows deviation when the non-zahir is supported by strong evidence or becomes the relied-upon position.
This exception preserves flexibility for legitimate tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَظَاهِرُ الْمَرُوِيِّ، لَيْسَ يُعْدَلَ * عَنْهُ إِلَى خِلَافِهِ ، إِذْ يُنْقَل
And the apparent of the narrated is not to be turned away from to its contrary, since it is transmitted.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage lays down a crucial principle: the zahir al-riwayah (the well-known transmitted narrations from the founding imams) must not be abandoned in favor of a non-zahir (shadhdh or irregular) narration, even if that non-zahir narration is also transmitted. The reason given is that the zahir al-riwayah is the established transmitted authority. This rule protects the reliability of fatwa by ensuring that only the primary, widely accepted transmissions are used. It does allow following a non-zahir narration in certain circumstances, as mentioned in other sections, but as a general rule, the zahir al-riwayah takes precedence.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known, widely transmitted narrations from Abu Hanifa and his students
غير ظاهر (ghayr zahir): Non-apparent, irregular, or rare narrations

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It can be abandoned for any other narration
B) It is not to be abandoned for a contrary narration
C) It is to be abandoned for non-zahir narrations
D) It is equal to other narrations

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-riwayah is the default authority; deviation requires strong justification.

Negation of Kufr from a Muslim Preferred
Rasm rule on preferring statements negating kufr even if weak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim on preferring statements that negate kufr from a Muslim, even if weak, and apply it to fatwa scenarios involving potential takfir.

Core Idea
Even a weak argument that avoids declaring a Muslim a kafir is preferred over a strong one that declares kufr.

This passage from the Rasm al-Mufti tradition provides a critical ethical and juristic guideline for muftis: always favor interpretations that preserve a Muslim's Islamic status. This reflects the Hanafi school's cautious approach to takfir, prioritizing the presumption of Islam (al-istishab) even when the evidence is weak.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the maxim
Commit the Arabic and English wording of the maxim to memory. This is a foundational rule in fatwa practice.
The maxim is a sughra (minor) legal maxim.
2
Understand the operative condition
The key phrase is 'even if weak' (wa law da'eefan). This overrides the usual preference for stronger evidence.
Weakness here refers to the strength of the legal evidence or interpretation.
3
Identify the exceptions
The maxim has an exception: when there is clear, unambiguous evidence of kufr that cannot be interpreted away.
The exception is governed by al-istishab (presumption of continuity).
4
Apply to a hypothetical fatwa scenario
Consider a person uttering an ambiguous statement. Choose the interpretation that avoids takfir even if linguistically weaker.
This reflects the Hanafi adab of caution in matters of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ قَوْلِ جَاءَ يَنْفِي الْكُفْرَ * عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ، وَلَوْ ضَعِيفًا أَحْرَى
And every statement that comes negating kufr from a Muslim, even if weak, is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage provides a crucial principle in ifta' related to takfir (declaring someone a disbeliever). When there are multiple possible interpretations or rulings, the one that negates (removes) the attribution of kufr from a Muslim is to be preferred, even if that interpretation is deemed weak (da'if) from a juristic perspective. This reflects the general Islamic ethical principle of avoiding takfir unless absolutely certain. The mufti should lean towards preserving the Islamic status of a Muslim whenever possible.

Key Terms
الكفر (al-kufr): Disbelief, the act of rejecting faith
ضعيف (da'if): Weak in terms of legal strength or evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule, which type of statement is preferred in fatwa when dealing with a Muslim?
A) The statement that declares kufr
B) The statement that negates kufr
C) The statement that is based on qiyas
D) The statement that is strong in evidence

Key Takeaway
In cases of doubt, the mufti must prefer the interpretation that avoids declaring a Muslim a disbeliever, even if that interpretation is weak.

Opinions Retracted by the Mujtahid Are Like Abrogated
Rasm rule on retracted opinions being like abrogated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim that a mujtahid's retracted opinion is like abrogated text, and identify when an opinion is no longer operative.

Core Idea
A mujtahid's retracted opinion is legally dead — like abrogated revelation — and cannot be followed.

This lesson introduces a key Rasm al-Mufti principle: when a mujtahid (such as Imam Abu Hanifa) retracts a previously held opinion, that opinion is treated as abrogated (mansukh) and loses all legal force. This analogy to Quranic naskh ensures that the final position of the mujtahid is the only operative one. Understanding this maxim is essential for muftis and students of fiqh to correctly navigate the hierarchy of opinions within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Understand the analogy to naskh
The retracted opinion is likened to abrogated revelation because both lose validity after a later authoritative source.
2
Identify the scope of the maxim
It applies to the opinions of a mujtahid within the madhhab, such as Abu Hanifa or his major students.
3
Apply the maxim to a scenario
If a mujtahid first held an opinion then retracted it, the retracted opinion is not to be used for fatwa.
4
Distinguish from mere disagreement
The maxim does not apply to opinions that were never retracted; only those known to have been recanted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ مَا رَجَعَ عَنْهُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ * صَارَ كَمَنْسُوحٍ، فَغَيْرَهُ اعْتَمِدُ
And everything from which the mujtahid retracted becomes like abrogated, so rely on other than it.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage establishes the principle that if a mujtahid (such as Abu Hanifa or his students) retracts a previous opinion, that opinion is treated as having been abrogated (mansukh). Consequently, it is no longer valid for practice or fatwa; one must rely on the later opinion (the one after retraction). This rule ensures that the final position of the mujtahid is what governs, similar to how a later revelation abrogates an earlier one in Quranic laws.

Key Terms
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): A jurist capable of independent legal reasoning
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Retraction of a previously held opinion
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated, no longer valid for practice

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It remains valid as an option
B) It becomes like abrogated
C) It is equal to the new opinion
D) It is preferred over the new one

Key Takeaway
A mujtahid's retracted opinion is like an abrogated text and cannot be used for fatwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Ten Principles of Fatwa Issuance (Dawabit al-Fatwa)
Hierarchical list of ten fatwa principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ten hierarchical principles for issuing a fatwa in the Hanafi school and apply them to determine the preferred ruling in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Fatwa follows a strict hierarchy: zahir al-riwaya over ghair zahir, mutun over sharh, and rulings that prevent takfir even if weak.

This passage from 'Awn al-Mughni' lays out the foundational principles (dawabit) that govern fatwa issuance in the Hanafi tradition. These principles are not arbitrary; they form a hierarchy that guides the mufti in selecting the most authoritative ruling from the vast corpus of Hanafi fiqh. Understanding these rules is essential for anyone who wishes to issue or evaluate fatwas within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the issue
Determine if the issue relates to qada (judicial rulings), inheritance involving dhawu al-arham, or general matters, as each has a preferred authority.
For qada, Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is selected; for dhawu al-arham, Imam Muhammad's.
2
Check for a student-based narration from Abu Hanifa
If a student of Abu Hanifa has adopted a specific opinion of the Imam, that opinion is preferred as long as no contrary established narration exists.
Example: the ruling on tayammum for one who puts dates in water.
3
Apply the hierarchy of sources: istihsan and transmitted rulings
Generally, istihsan is preferred over qiyas unless it is one of the few exceptions. Also, do not abandon zahir al-riwaya for ghair zahir al-riwaya.
If a textual evidence is supported by fiqhi transmission, it must be followed.
4
Consider rulings that prevent takfir and retracted opinions
Any transmitted saying that negates kufr from a Muslim is given precedence, even if weak. Similarly, if a mujtahid has retracted an opinion, it is like abrogated and not acted upon.
The later or preferred view takes precedence.
5
Navigate the textual hierarchy: mutun, sharh, and corrected versions
Rulings in mutun are preferred over sharh, and sharh over old fatawa, unless a later explicit correction (tashih) exists. If corrected, the corrected version prevails even if not in mutun.
This is a key check when multiple sources seem to conflict.

Source Text

[42] (2) As long as there is nothing established from Imam Abu Hanifa that a student has adopted, like the ruling of tayammum for one who puts dates in water. [43] (3) In any matter related to judicial rulings, for fatwa the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is selected. [44] (4) In matters concerning dhawu al-arham, the scholars have given fatwa based on Imam Muhammad's saying. [49] Every saying of a mujtahid from which he has retracted, its status is like abrogated (it will not be acted upon; rather) besides it, full reliance will be on the tarij (preponderant view). [50] (9) The inclusion of any saying in the mutun is an implicit preference for that saying. [51] (10) (Therefore, in that respect) sayings appearing in the mutun are to be preferred over those in the sharh, and sayings in the sharh are to be preferred over old fatawa that carry preference (in the context of issuing fatwa). [52] (But this is only as long as) the saying has not been expressly corrected (sahhaha) besides the mutun? (If it has been expressly corrected), then in that case the saying that has been expressly corrected will prevail (even if it is not in the mutun).

Similarly, in (verse 54) the active past of ifti'al is clearer than the imperative; so we have accepted that.

Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage from 'Awn al-Mughni' presents a set of ten crucial principles (dawabit) for issuing fatwa within the Hanafi school. These are not isolated rules but form a hierarchical system that guides the mufti in selecting the correct ruling. The first principle (42) establishes that if a student of Imam Abu Hanifa has chosen a particular opinion of the Imam (even if not reported widely), that opinion is preferred. An example is the ruling on tayammum for someone who puts dates in water—a specific case where a student's narration is followed. Second (43): In matters of qada (judicial rulings), the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is chosen. This reflects the practical orientation of Abu Yusuf's rulings. Third (44): In inheritance cases involving dhawu al-arham (distant kindred), the opinion of Imam Muhammad is preferred. Fourth (45): Istihsan (juristic preference) is generally preferred over qiyas (analogy), except for a few well-known exceptions. Fifth (46): The mufti must not abandon zahir al-riwaya (the well-known transmitted opinions) for ghair zahir al-riwaya (rare transmissions), even if the latter is transmitted. Sixth (47): If a textual evidence (dalil) is supported by the fiqhi transmission (riwaya), then that evidence must be followed. Seventh (48): Any transmitted saying that prevents takfir (declaring a Muslim a disbeliever) should be given precedence, even if it is weak. Eighth (49): If a mujtahid has retracted a previous opinion, that opinion is considered effectively abrogated; the later opinion or the preferred one takes precedence. Ninth (50): The inclusion of a ruling in the mutun (standard manuals) grants it an implicit preference over other sources. Tenth (51-52): Mutun are preferred over sharh (commentaries), and sharh over old fatawa, unless a particular ruling has been explicitly corrected (sahhaha) in a later source, in which case the corrected version takes precedence even if not in the mutun. The passage also includes notes clarifying the grammar and text of the original Arabic verses from the poem that these principles explain. The overall lesson is that fatwa requires careful navigation of the school's hierarchy of sources, and a mufti must be aware of the relative weight of different transmitted opinions.

Key Terms
ظاہر روایت (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known, widely transmitted rulings of the school (the six books of Imam Muhammad and other core works).
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) due to custom, necessity, or equity.
ذوی الارحام (dhawu al-arham): Distant kindred who inherit in the absence of primary heirs (ashab al-fara'id and 'asabat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principles in this passage, what is the general rule regarding istihsan (juristic preference) vs. qiyas (analogy) in fatwa?
A) Qiyas is always preferred over istihsan.
B) Istihsan is preferred over qiyas, except for a few exceptions.
C) They are equal in weight.
D) Neither is used; only texts are used.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy prioritizes zahir al-riwaya, then preferred opinions of the imams (Abu Yusuf for qada, Muhammad for dhawu al-arham), then istihsan over qiyas, and rulings that avoid takfir, with mutun taking precedence over sharh unless explicitly corrected.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Preference for Explicitly Corrected Narrations in Fatwa
Rule from Rasm al-Mufti on tarjīḥ of narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of preference for explicitly corrected narrations (taṣḥīḥ) in the Hanafi mufti's tarjīḥ hierarchy.

Core Idea
Explicit correction (taṣḥīḥ) by later scholars overrides the default preference for texts.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, a mufti often faces multiple narrations. The default is to rely on the well-known texts (mutūn). However, later scholars may explicitly correct a narration, declaring it the sounder position. This lesson explains when such a correction takes precedence and becomes the basis for fatwa, even if it contradicts the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
Recognise that the default tarjīḥ in Hanafi fatwa is to give preference to the positions found in the authoritative mutūn and old fatwas.
2
Recognise the exception
The default applies only as long as there is no explicit correction (taṣḥīḥ ṣarīḥ) of a narration. If a later scholar explicitly corrects a different qawl, that becomes the preferred position.
3
Understand the condition of explicitness
The correction must be explicit (ṣarīḥ). A mere implication or ambiguous statement does not overturn the default. Look for clear language like 'the correct view is...' or 'the fatwa is on...'.
4
Determine the effect
Once an explicit correction is established, that corrected qawl becomes the basis for fatwa, even if it does not appear in the mutūn. It is not necessary for it to be in the core texts.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider a mufti who sees a ruling in Kanz al-Daqā'iq but finds a later work where al-Haskafī explicitly states that the fatwa is on a different opinion. Apply the rule: the later explicit correction overrides the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدیم فتاوی پر ترجیح ہوگی (فتوی دینے کے سلسلے )۔
[۵۲] ( مگر یہ اُس وقت تک ہے ) جب تک کہ متون کے علاوہ قول کی صراحت کے ساتھ صحیح نہ کی گئی ہو؟ (اگر صراحتا تصحیح کی گئی ہو ) تو پھر ایسی صورت میں وہی قول رائج قرار پائے گا، جس کی صراحتا صحیح کی گئی ہے (اگر چہ وہ متون میں نہ آیا ہو)۔
مُلاحظة : ”مالم تصح“ کا تعلق ، چوں کہ تیسرے شعر سے ہے؟ س لیے ترجمہ اسی کے مطابق آسانی کے لیے کر دیا گیا۔ مالم تصح“ کا فاعل ”رواية“ ہے، ”بهـا الـغيـر أخـذ“ کی اصل عبارت یوں ہے: ” أخـذ الـغـيـر بھا“۔ ”بھا“ کی ضمیر روایۃ“ کی طرف راجع ہے۔
وضاحت : ”تعلقا“ (شعر: ۴۳) ، الكفرا“ (شعر: ۴۸) اور صححا“، ”صر حا“ (شعر :۵۲) میں الف اشباع کا ہے۔
نیز (شعر: ۴۹) میں (اعتمد ) کو افتعال سے امر کا صیغہ ماننے کے بجائے، افتعال کا ماضی مجهول ( اعتمد ) بھی پڑھ سکتے ہیں، اس صورت میں (فغیرہ) تائب فاعل ہو کر مرفوع ہوگا، بعض نسخوں میں اس طرح بھی ہے؛ باقی ہمارے لیے (اعتماد کا اشتعال کا امر ہونا، ضرورت شعری کی وجہ سے زیادہ واضح تھا؛ اس لیے اسے امر ہی مان کر (فغیرہ) کو اس کا مفعول بہ بنایا ہے۔
اسی طرح (شعر: ۵۴) میں افتعال کے امر کے بجاے، افتعال کا ماضی معروف ہونا زیادہ واضح ہے؛ اس لیے ہم نے اُسے ہی قبول کیا ہے۔
Preference is given to old fatwas (regarding giving fatwa).
[52] (But this is only) as long as the statement has not been explicitly corrected apart from the texts. (If explicitly corrected) then in that case that statement will become prevalent, the one that has been explicitly corrected (even if it is not in the texts).
Observation: The connection of 'mā lam tuṣaḥḥaḥ' is to the third verse? Therefore the translation has been made accordingly for convenience. The subject of 'mā lam tuṣaḥḥaḥ' is 'riwāyah'. The original phrase of 'bihā al-ghayr ukhidh' is 'akhadha al-ghayru bihā'. The pronoun 'bihā' refers to 'riwāyah'.
Clarification: In 'taʿallaqā' (verse 43), 'al-kufrā' (verse 48), 'ṣuḥḥiḥā', and 'ṣarraḥā' (verse 52), the alif is for prolongation.
Also in (verse 49), instead of taking 'iʿtamid' as the imperative verb from iftiʿāl, one may read it as the passive past tense of iftiʿāl (iʿtumid). In that case, 'fa-ghayruhu' would be the subject and be raised. In some manuscripts it is like that; however, for us, (the imperative form) was clearer due to poetic necessity; so we have taken it as imperative and made 'fa-ghayruhu' its object.
Similarly in (verse 54), instead of the imperative of iftiʿāl, the active past tense of iftiʿāl is clearer; so we have accepted that.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the poem 'Rasm al-Mufti' (verse 52). It clarifies a rule regarding the tarjīḥ (preference) of narrations when issuing fatwa. The default is that old fatwas and widely accepted texts are preferred. However, if a narration (riwāyah) is explicitly corrected (ṣarīḥan tuṣaḥḥaḥ) by later scholars—i.e., they declare that the correct position is a different narration—then that corrected narration becomes the basis for fatwa, even if it is not found in the original authoritative texts (mutūn). The author then explains the grammatical points of the verse. The 'observation' notes that the phrase 'mā lam tuṣaḥḥaḥ' in the poem connects to a previous line, and the translation is adjusted accordingly. The 'clarification' discusses the elongations in certain words and alternative readings of the word 'iʿtamid' (verse 49) and 'iʿtamid' (verse 54). This is essential for understanding the precise application of the rule: the correction must be explicit (ṣarīḥ), not merely implied.

Key Terms
تصحیح (taṣḥīḥ): Explicit correction by a scholar, declaring that a particular narration or opinion is the correct one
متون (mutūn): The core authoritative texts of the madhhab (e.g., Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī, Kanz al-Daqā’iq, etc.)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule in verse 52, when does a corrected qawl become the basis for fatwa?
A) Only if it is found in the mutūn
B) Only if the majority of scholars agree
C) When it is explicitly corrected (ṣarīḥan) by later scholars
D) When it is older than the existing fatwa

Key Takeaway
A mufti must follow explicitly corrected narrations (taṣḥīḥ ṣarīḥ) over the default reliance on texts (mutūn).

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Rasm Rule for Ibadat: Following Imam Abu Hanifa
States the rasm rule for ibadat with exception and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm rule for ibadat by identifying when to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's default opinion and when to follow a retracted narration adopted by the mashayikh.

Core Idea
In ibadat, the default is Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion unless the mashayikh adopt a retracted narration of his.

This lesson introduces a fundamental rasm al-mufti rule: in all matters of worship (ibadat), the fatwa is normally based on Imam Abu Hanifa's saying. However, there is an important exception: if the later authoritative scholars (mashayikh) have explicitly given fatwa on a narration that Imam Abu Hanifa himself retracted, that narration is followed instead. Understanding this hierarchy prevents errors in fatwa issuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case as an ibadat matter
First, confirm that the question pertains to an act of worship (prayer, fasting, hajj, zakat, etc.). The rasm rule applies only to ibadat, not mu'amalat.
Ibadat includes all ritual acts.
2
Locate Imam Abu Hanifa's known opinion
Find the well-known (mashhur) saying of Imam Abu Hanifa on the issue. This is the default ruling for fatwa.
Refer to reliable Hanafi sources like al-Hidayah or al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya.
3
Check if the mashayikh have adopted a retracted narration
Investigate whether the later scholars (mashayikh) have explicitly given fatwa on a narration that Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted (marju' 'anhu). If yes, that narration takes precedence over his default opinion.
The mashayikh's explicit adoption overrides the default.
4
Issue the fatwa according to the identified ruling
If no retracted narration is adopted, follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion. If a retracted narration is adopted, follow that instead. In both cases, the fatwa traces back to a narration of Imam Abu Hanifa.
The examples show that even when following a student's view, a parallel narration of Imam Abu Hanifa often exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي
ضابطے اور قاعدے بیان کیے ہیں، جنھیں علماء نے راجح قول کی علامت قرار دیا ہے ،علامہ نے ان قاعدوں کو نہایت ہی عرق ریزی سے ، متفرق کتابوں کی ورق گردانی کر کے حاصل کیا ہے اور انھیں یہ حوالہ اپنی شرح: شرح عقود رسم المفتي “ کے اندر بیان فرمایا ہے ، اب ہم ترتیب وار ہر ایک قاعدے کو مختصر اواضح
کرتے ہیں۔
عبادات کے تمام ابواب میں امام صاحب کے قول پر فتوی دیا جائے گا
(۱) جو مسائل نماز، روزہ، حج ، زکاۃ وغیرہ عبادات سے متعلق ہوں، اُن میں مطلقاً ( کوئی شاگر د ساتھ ہو یا نہ ہو ) امام صاحب صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول پر فتوی دیا جائے گا، الا یہ کہ امام صاحب کی کسی مرجوع عنہ روایت پر مشایخ نے فتوی کی صراحت کی ہو، تو پھر ایسی صورت میں امام صاحب کے قول مختار کو چھوڑ کر ، اُسی کے مطابق
فتوی دیا جائے گا۔

پر فتویٰ ہوا۔
21
اسی طرح نبیذ تمر سے وضو کے سلسلے میں امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر فتویٰ ہے، پانی نہ ہونے کی صورت میں اُس سے وضو نہ کر کے تقسیم کیا جائے گا، امام
صاحب سے اس سلسلے میں تین روایتیں ملتی ہیں، آخری روایت امام ابو یوسف ہی کی طرح ہے؛ لہذا اب اس اعتبار سے صرف امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر فتویٰ نہیں ہوا ؛ بل کہ در حقیقت وہ بھی امام صاحب ہی کے قول پر فتوی ہے۔
Aun al-Mughni fi Hall 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. Rules and maxims are stated, which scholars have considered signs of the preponderant opinion. The author has obtained these rules with great effort, by perusing various books, and mentioned them with references in his commentary: Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. Now we will explain each rule briefly in order. (1) In all chapters of ibadat (acts of worship), fatwa will be given according to the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa. Matters related to prayer, fasting, hajj, zakat, etc., in these there is absolute (whether a student is present or not) giving fatwa according to the saying of Imam Sahib (may Allah's peace and blessings be upon him), unless the mashayikh (later scholars) have explicitly given fatwa on a retracted narration of Imam Sahib, then in that case, leaving the chosen opinion of Imam Sahib, fatwa will be given according to that. But here it should be kept in mind that when it becomes necessary to leave the famous saying of Imam Sahib in a matter and the mashayikh give fatwa according to the saying of some student, that saying is such that there is some narration of Imam Sahib corresponding to it. In this sense, in the chapters of ibadat, fatwa is not given entirely on the saying other than Imam Sahib; for example, the saying about the purity of used water (ma' musta'mal) is from Imam Muhammad (may Allah's peace be upon him), and the fatwa is on it; but this is also a narration from Imam Sahib; hence in this respect, the fatwa is on the saying of Imam Sahib. Similarly, regarding ablution with date water (nabidh tamr), the fatwa is on the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf, that in the absence of water, one should not perform ablution with it but perform tayammum. Imam Sahib has three narrations in this regard, the last narration is like that of Imam Abu Yusuf; hence now in this respect, the fatwa is not only on the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf; rather, in reality, it is also a fatwa on the saying of Imam Sahib.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is from Aun al-Mughni, a commentary on Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, and it presents the first rasm rule for issuing fatwa: in all matters of ibadat (worship), the fatwa should be based on the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa. The passage clarifies that this is the default rule. However, there is an exception: if the later mashayikh (scholars) have explicitly given fatwa on a retracted narration (marju' 'anhu) of Imam Abu Hanifa, then that opinion is followed instead of his well-known opinion. Importantly, the passage explains that whenever a saying of a student (e.g., Imam Muhammad or Imam Abu Yusuf) is adopted, it is usually because there is also a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that supports it. Thus, the fatwa is never completely outside the school of Imam Abu Hanifa. Two examples are given: (1) the purity of used water (ma' musta'mal) — though the fatwa is according to Imam Muhammad, it is also a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa. (2) Ablution with nabidh tamr — the fatwa is according to Imam Abu Yusuf, but Imam Abu Hanifa also has a similar narration. Therefore, the rule is effectively that in ibadat, the fatwa always returns to some narration of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
مرجوع عنہ روایت (marju' 'anhu riwaya): A narration (from Imam Abu Hanifa) that he later retracted or abandoned.
مشایخ (mashayikh): Later authoritative Hanafi scholars who determine the relied-upon rulings.
امام صاحب (Imam Sahib): Refers to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default rule for giving fatwa in matters of ibadat according to this passage?
A) Follow Imam Muhammad's opinion
B) Follow Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion
C) Follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion
D) Follow the opinion of any student

Key Takeaway
In ibadat, the default fatwa follows Imam Abu Hanifa, but if the mashayikh explicitly adopt one of his retracted narrations, that takes precedence.
