Rasm Rule for Qada: Follow Imam Abu Yusuf
States the rasm rule for qada and testimonies, preferring Imam Abu Yusuf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm rule for judiciary matters by stating that Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is mufta bih and identify its reason and an example.

Core Idea
In judiciary matters, Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion takes precedence due to his practical judicial experience.

This passage presents a key rule from Rasm al-Mufti: in matters of judiciary (qada) and testimonies (shahadat), the operative fatwa follows Imam Abu Yusuf. The reason given is his long tenure as a judge, giving him unique practical insight. We will explore the rationale and see its application in the issue of talqin (prompting witnesses).

Guided Path
1
Identify the rasm rule and its scope
Locate the ruling: in judiciary and testimonies, the fatwa follows Imam Abu Yusuf. Note that this is a procedural guideline for muftis, not a fiqh ruling per se.
The scope is specifically qada and shahadat, not all fiqh.
2
Understand the rationale (sabab)
The text gives the reason: Imam Abu Yusuf served as a judge for a long time, gaining practical experience. This makes his opinions more reliable in these matters.
The rationale is based on his expertise, not necessarily his knowledge of texts.
3
Work through the example of talqin
The example: other imams forbid the judge from prompting witnesses, but Imam Abu Yusuf permits it if it helps reveal truth and there is no bias. The fatwa follows him.
This shows how the rasm rule translates into a specific fiqh ruling.
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a judge following Imam Abu Yusuf may guide witnesses; one following others may not. This affects court procedure.
The mufti must adopt the permissive view when issuing fatwa on judicial matters.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The passage clearly states that the mufta bih is Imam Abu Yusuf's view in these matters. The mufti should not revert to the general Hanafi position if it differs.
This is a binding rasm al-mufti rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قضاء سے متعلق مسائل میں امام ابو یوسف کا قول مفتی بہ ہے
(۲) قضا و شہادات سے متعلق مسائل میں حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے قول کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا؛ اس لیے کہ حضرت امام ابو یوسف عرصہ دراز تک مسند قضا پر فائز رہے، عملی طور پر اُنھوں نے مشکل قضا کا مشاہدہ کیا ، جس کی بنیاد پر اُن کے تجربات بڑھے ، لہذا اس وجہ سے قضا وغیرہ سے متعلق مسائل میں آپ کی رائے زیادہ وزنی ہوگی، جیسے : جب گواہ قاضی کی مجلس میں حاضر ہوں، تو دیگر ائمہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ قاضی گواہوں کو تلقین نہیں کر سکتا کہ تم اس طرح اپنی بات کہو، جب کہ امام ابو یوسف اس کی نہ صرف اجازت دیتے ہیں ؛ بل کہ اسے مستحسن قرار دیتے ہیں ، بشرطے کہ اس سے مزید معلومات ہونے کی امید ہو اور طرف داری کا قرینہ نہ پایا جائے ، فتویٰ حضرت امام ابو یوسف صلى الله عليه وسلم ہی کے قول پر ہے۔
In matters related to judiciary (qada) and testimonies (shahadat), the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is the mufta bih (operative). (2) In matters related to judiciary and testimonies, fatwa will be given according to the saying of Hadrat Imam Abu Yusuf; because Hadrat Imam Abu Yusuf remained seated on the seat of judgment for a long time, he practically observed difficult judiciary, on the basis of which his experiences increased. Therefore, due to this reason, in matters related to judiciary etc., his opinion will carry more weight. For example: When witnesses appear in the judge's court, the opinion of other imams is that the judge cannot prompt the witnesses to say their statement in a particular way, whereas Imam Abu Yusuf not only permits this, but considers it commendable (mustahsan), provided that there is hope of obtaining more information and no sign of partiality is found. The fatwa is on the saying of Hadrat Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah's peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents the second rasm rule: in judiciary and testimonies, the fatwa follows Imam Abu Yusuf. The reason given is that Imam Abu Yusuf served as a judge for a long time, giving him practical insight into judicial matters. Therefore, his opinions in these areas are more reliable. An example is given regarding the judge prompting witnesses: other schools (including possibly Imam Abu Hanifa) do not allow it, but Imam Abu Yusuf allows it and considers it commendable if it helps reveal the truth and there is no bias.

Key Terms
قضا (qada): Judiciary, court proceedings.
شہادات (shahadat): Testimonies, evidence.
تلقین (talqin): Prompting the witness on how to testify.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Because he was the most knowledgeable of the students

Key Takeaway
In judiciary and testimonies, the fatwa follows Imam Abu Yusuf because of his practical judicial experience, as illustrated by the ruling on talqin.

Fatwa Preference on Wudu with Nabidh al-Tamr
Explains fatwa preference for Imam Abu Yusuf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the Hanafi tarjih process resolves an intra-school ikhtilaf regarding wudu with nabidh and apply the principle of the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The fatwa on wudu with nabidh follows Imam Abu Yusuf, but this also reflects Imam Abu Hanifa's final narration, unifying the school's position.

This passage demonstrates a key aspect of Hanafi ifta: how apparent differences between imams are resolved through tarjih. We see that the fatwa on wudu with nabidh is attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf, but we learn that it matches the final narration of Imam Abu Hanifa, making the fatwa effectively from both. This illustrates how later Hanafi muftis establish the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue and disputed ruling
Recognize that the issue is whether wudu with date nabidh is valid when water is absent. The Hanafi school had multiple views.
The debate is about the definition of 'water' in wudu.
2
Recognize the two positions
Imam Abu Yusuf's view: wudu with nabidh is invalid, requiring tayammum. Imam Abu Hanifa's earlier narrations: possibly allowed wudu with nabidh.
These are both within the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the tarjih mechanism
The passage notes that Imam Abu Hanifa had three narrations; the last one aligns with Abu Yusuf. This last narration is given weight as the final considered view.
Tarjih by later transmission (riwayah) is a common method.
4
Draw the fiqh conclusion
The mufta bihi ruling: wudu with nabidh is invalid, and tayammum must be performed.
This is the operative fatwa.
5
Reflect on the rasm al-mufti rule
The fatwa is not solely on Abu Yusuf's opinion; it is effectively on Imam Abu Hanifa's final narration, unifying the school.
This shows how tarjih can reconcile apparent differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
21 اسی طرح نبیذ تمر سے وضو کے سلسلے میں امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر فتویٰ ہے، پانی نہ ہونے کی صورت میں اُس سے وضو نہ کر کے تقسیم کیا جائے گا، امام صاحب سے اس سلسلے میں تین روایتیں ملتی ہیں، آخری روایت امام ابو یوسف ہی کی طرح ہے؛ لہذا اب اس اعتبار سے صرف امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر فتویٰ نہیں ہوا ؛ بل کہ در حقیقت وہ بھی امام صاحب ہی کے قول پر فتوی ہے۔
21 Similarly, regarding wudu with date nabidh, the fatwa is on Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion: in the absence of water, one should not perform wudu with it, and [instead] it will be divided [i.e., tayammum]. Imam Sahib has three narrations on this matter, the last of which is similar to Imam Abu Yusuf's; hence now in this respect the fatwa is not solely on Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion, but in reality it is also on the opinion of Imam Sahib.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm al-mufti rule regarding the fiqh of wudu with nabidh al-tamr (date drink). The ruling explicitly states that the fatwa is on Imam Abu Yusuf's position, which permits wudu only with pure water and prohibits using nabidh in its place, leading to tayammum. However, the author notes that Imam Abu Hanifa transmitted three narrations on this issue, and the final one aligns with Imam Abu Yusuf. Therefore, the fatwa is not exclusively on Abu Yusuf; it effectively represents Imam Abu Hanifa's own later view. This illustrates how tarjih (preference) within the Hanafi school often considers multiple transmissions and converges on a single authoritative position.

Key Terms
نبیذ تمر (nabidh al-tamr): A drink made from dates

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad
D) Imam Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa on wudu with nabidh is based on Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion, which also represents Imam Abu Hanifa's final narration, illustrating how intra-school ikhtilaf is resolved through tarjih of later transmissions.
